1601 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. James


NUMBER 2001 KA 2292


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2292 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/28/02); 813 So. 2d 659; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 915



March 28, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 03-00-512. Section VII. Honorable Timothy E. Kelley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, convicted defendant of forgery and sentenced him to four years imprisonment at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it imposed an excessive sentence and defendant was denied effective assistance of counsel at sentencing. The appellate court found that the record did not contain a motion to reconsider sentence nor did defendant object to the sentence. Under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1D, a failure to file or make a motion to reconsider sentence precluded defendant from raising the excessiveness argument on appeal. The appellate court examined the sentence for excessiveness because it was necessary to do so as part of the analysis of the ineffective counsel issue. The trial court ordered a presentence investigation (PSI) report and considered the PSI in imposing sentence. Although defendant was a first felony offender, he had an extensive criminal record including alcohol and drug related offenses and crimes against the person. The trial court demonstrated full compliance with the requirements of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 in that it considered all the necessary elements before sentencing defendant. Defendant was sentenced to less than one-half of the maximum period of imprisonment allowed for forgery.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1602 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Vallien v. State ex rel. Dep't of Transp. & Dev.


01 0566-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01 0566 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/27/02); 812 So. 2d 894; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 853



March 27, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 24, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-EIGHTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CAMERON, NO. 10-14884. HONORABLE H. WARD FONTENOT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow brought wrongful death and survival claims against defendant department of transportation (DOT) that arose out of a car accident in which her husband was killed. The Thirty-Eighth Judicial District Court, Parish of Cameron (Louisiana), found the husband 25 percent at fault and assigned the remaining 75 percent to DOT. The court reduced the award to comport with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106. Both DOT and the wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband's truck struck an area of ponded water, causing him to lose control of his truck, slide across the highway through a ditch, and come to rest under a tree limb. The branch of the tree sheared off the top of the truck, piercing the passenger compartment. DOT asserted, inter alia, that the jury erred in concluding that the roadway and shoulder defects created an unreasonable risk of harm and that it had prior notice of any such defects, and it erred in its apportionment of fault. The wife sought a declaration that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 13:5106, 13:5112, were unconstitutional on the grounds that they violated the Louisiana Constitution's Equal Protection Clause, Sovereign Immunity Clause, and Access to Courts Clause. The appellate court found no manifest error in the jury's credibility determinations and conclusion that the roadway-shoulder variance created an unreasonable risk of harm; that DOT had actual or constructive notice of the defect and failed to take corrective measures within a reasonable time; the record supported that DOT should bear the majority of the fault; and, reluctantly, that the statutes were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1603 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Randazzo v. Boh Bros. Constr. Co.


No. 2001-CA-1953


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-1953 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/27/02); 814 So. 2d 671; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1391



March 27, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
 Randazzo v. Boh Bros. Constr. Co., 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1211 (La. App. 4th Cir. Apr. 30, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION. NO. 99-04984, DISTRICT "EIGHT". Honorable Gwendolyn F. Thompson, Workers' Compensation Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged the judgment of the Office of Workers' Compensation (Louisiana) awarding additional workers' compensation benefits to appellee retired employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee injured his back on the job in 1994, and underwent surgery and rehabilitation. The employee returned and worked from 1995 until he resigned/retired in 1997. The employee argued that the job he had performed for two years did not comply with his physician's limitations. The trial court awarded additional benefits, finding the employee had not retired within the meaning of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(d)(ii). Workers' compensation benefits were paid to the employee from 1994 until 1999, including 104 weeks of benefits after the employee had retired. The record convinced the appellate court that the employee permanently withdrew from the work force, as he announced to his co-workers that he was retiring and considered himself retired. The appellate court found no evidence in the record that the employee intended to return to work and the record did not reasonably support the trial court's conclusion that the employee had not permanently withdrew from the workforce.


OUTCOME: The award of additional benefits was reversed.

 

1604 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Flagg


No. 01-KA-965


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-1483 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/26/02); 815 So. 2d 208; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 864



March 26, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-5669, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Sentence vacated; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant pled guilty to possession with the intent to distribute cocaine, and was sentenced pursuant to the plea agreement. The State subsequently filed a habitual offender bill of information, alleging that the defendant was a fourth-felony offender. The 24th Judicial District Court, Jefferson Parish (Louisiana), sentenced the defendant to 20 years at hard labor, concurrent with the defendant's other sentences. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: At sentencing, the State argued that the defendant was subject to life imprisonment under the version of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15: 529.1A(1)(c)(ii) in effect at the time of the commission of the offense controlled. The trial judge disagreed and applied the version in effect at the time of sentencing. On appeal, the State argued that the trial judge erred in failing to impose the mandatory sentence pursuant to the law in effect at the time of the commission of the underlying offense. The appellate court agreed and vacated the sentence. Under the habitual offender statute as it existed at the time of the commission of the offense, the defendant was subject to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Under the amended version, the defendant was not subject to mandatory life imprisonment. The court held that the general rule that the law in effect at the time of the commission of the offense was determinative of the penalty controlled the defendant's sentencing. Therefore, the trial judge erred in giving the amended statute retroactive application in sentencing the defendant. The sentence was illegally lenient.


OUTCOME: The defendant's sentence was vacated and the case remanded for resentencing.

 

1605 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n


2001 CA 2594, Consolidated With 2001 CA 2595, Consolidated With 2001 CA 2596, Consolidated With 2001 CA 2597, Consolidated With 2001 CA 2598, Consolidated With 2001 CA 2599, Consolidated With 2001 CA 2600


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2594 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/20/02); 815 So. 2d 178; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 823



March 20, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1723 (La.App. 1 Cir., Apr. 26, 2002)
Writ granted by ANR Pipeline Co. v. 840 So. 2d 527, 2003 La. LEXIS 746 (La., Mar. 21, 2003)
Affirmed by, Remanded by ANR Pipeline Co. v. 851 So. 2d 1145, 2003 La. LEXIS 1957 (La., July 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 468,417, consolidated with 480,163; 480,161; 480,160; 480,159; 480,373; and 485,716, Respectively), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE TIMOTHY E. KELLEY, JUDGE.
ANR Pipeline Co. v. Louisiana Tax Comm'n, 774 So. 2d 1261, 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3558 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 22, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Motions ruled on. Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought declaratory judgments in the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana) that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1851(K) was unconstitutional, and other relief. The trial court dismissed all suits except one taxpayer's challenge to certain tax payments, and all the taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers challenged assessed valuations. The appellate court held the trial court's dismissals of six of the taxpayers' suits were final and appealable, but a judgment overruling an exception was interlocutory and not appealable. Only the trial court could address the taxpayers' requests for sanctions under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 863. When the appellate court ruled a taxpayer's constitutional challenge did not prescribe while, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1856(D), it awaited the tax commission's decision, it did not direct the commission to rule on the constitutional issue. The taxpayers' constitutional challenge filed before the tax commission's final decision was not premature because the commission had no authority to decide that challenge. The trial court did not have to grant mandamus directing the commission to transfer the taxpayers' constitutional challenge to the trial court because the commission could still enter a final judgment on the taxpayers' other claims. The trial court did not exercise appellate jurisdiction over the tax commission in the taxpayers' declaratory judgment actions, so it could not issue supervisory writs in those actions.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment sustaining an exception raising the objection of prematurity was reversed. Otherwise, the trial court's judgment was affirmed. One taxpayer's appeal was dismissed.

 

1606 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Dauterive Contrs., Inc. v. Landry & Watkins


01-1112


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-1112 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/13/02); 811 So. 2d 1242; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 759



March 13, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 92900-E, HONORABLE ANNE LENNAN SIMON, DISTRICT COURT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant construction company sued appellee law firm in the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Iberia Parish (Louisiana), for legal malpractice. The trial court granted the law firm's exception of prescription/peremption, and the company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The construction company alleged the firm was negligent for not timely filing a bankruptcy claim. The appellate court held La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605, which was the current law applicable to prescription of legal malpractice actions, referred to one-year and three-year periods, both of which were peremptive. Nothing could interfere with the running of these peremptive periods, such as contra non valentem or the continuous representation rule, and they could not be renounced. While, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605(E), the three-year period was inapplicable if fraud was proved, the one-year period still applied. Because the company's claim was perempted on the face of its petition, it had the burden of showing its claim was not perempted, and it did not meet that burden. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605(A) imposed a discovery exception on the one-year peremptive period, but the company knew or should have known of its claim more than one year before the action was filed. Due to the inapplicability of the continuous representation rule, the date of termination of the company's attorney-client relationship with the firm was a non-issue. The statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1607 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. George


No. 2001-KA-1061


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-1061 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/13/02); 829 So. 2d 440; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 819



March 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 20, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 395-266, SECTION "B". Honorable Patrick G. Quinlan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), of simple burglary and was sentenced as a fourth offender to life imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police saw defendant leaving the rear of a convenience store through a window, and he dropped various items when he realized he had been seen. The appellate court found there was sufficient evidence to support his burglary conviction. His counsel was not ineffective for failing to introduce medical evidence that he was physically unable to run and jump, in light of the evidence against him. In defendant's multiple offender prosecution, the State met its burden of showing he was advised of his rights when he pled guilty to a prior offense, by introducing a guilty plea/waiver of rights form signed and initialed by defendant, as well as his counsel and the trial judge, and the docket master and minute entry, both showing defendant was represented by counsel. While defendant's minimum mandatory sentence could be unconstitutionally excessive, it was presumed constitutional. Defendant, who had a lengthy criminal record, did not meet his burden of rebutting the presumption that his mandatory minimum sentence was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1608 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. City of Abbeville


01-1362


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-1362 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/06/02); 809 So. 2d 1244; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 574



March 6, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 6, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF VERMILION, NO. 75,865, HONORABLE EDWARD D. RUBIN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sued defendant city, the employee's former employer, seeking recovery of compensation for unused leave. The Fifteenth Judicial District, Parish of Vermilion, Louisiana, found in favor of the employee and awarded him $ 24,297 as compensation for unused leave in addition to attorney's fees. The trial court also denied the city's peremptory exception of no cause of action and its reconventional demand. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: During his employment with the city, the employee was a member of the city's civil service system. After he was terminated for cause, the employee appealed his termination to the city's civil service board, which amended the termination to a suspension without pay for 28 days and ordered the reinstatement of the employee. The employee was then placed on administrative leave and paid his full salary. During the period he was on administrative leave, the employee performed no labor or services for the city. The trial court later ordered the reinstatement of the decision terminating the employee. The employee then sued the city for compensation for his unused leave. The city argued the employee forfeited any unused leave because he was terminated. The employee alleged he was entitled to be paid for unused leave under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:631 et. seq. In affirming the trial court's decision, the appeals court concluded there was no clear written policy that leave earned by an employee was a mere gratuity. Consequently, the trial court was correct in finding the employee was entitled to be compensated for unused leave since it was a wage under the law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1609 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sewell


No. 35,549-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


35,549 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/27/02); 811 So. 2d 140; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 460



February 27, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Sewell, 840 So. 2d 535, 2003 La. LEXIS 773 (La., Mar. 21, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Sewell v. State, 118 So. 3d 1107, 2013 La. LEXIS 1697 (La., 2013)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Sewell v. State, 2014 La. LEXIS 1220 (La., May 14, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 199,992. Honorable Leon Emanuel, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of armed robbery. He was adjudicated a third-felony offender and was sentenced to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant threatened the victim with a gun, demanded the victim's money and car keys, shot the victim twice in the leg, took the victim's money and other items, and fled in the victim's car. An officer saw defendant in the stolen car and shined a light on him. Defendant fled from the car on foot. Another officer stopped defendant. When defendant was arrested, a shirt matching one described by the victim and other witnesses, and a gun -- which ballistic tests showed was used to shoot the victim -- were found in the street near defendant. The victim's driver's license was found on defendant. The victim identified defendant as the person who robbed and shot him. On appeal, the court found that (1) the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction; (2) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress the victim's identification of him despite the alleged suggestive circumstances; (3) the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's adjudication as a third-felony offender, as the State proved that his prior guilty pleas were informed and voluntary and made with an articulated waiver of his Boykin rights; and (4) defendant's sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1610 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Jarrell v. Jarrell


No. 35,837-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


35,837 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/27/02); 811 So. 2d 207; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 314



February 27, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 397,569. Honorable B. Woodrow Nesbitt, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee ex-wife moved for modification of custody and supervised visitation in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana). The district court granted her sole child custody and awarded appellant ex-husband supervised visits. The ex-husband later petitioned for joint custody, or unsupervised visitation. The district court restored his normal visitation and awarded the ex-wife attorney fees. The ex-husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court found that the ex-husband was a perpetrator of family violence. It granted the ex-wife the sole care and custody of their child. The ex-husband was awarded supervised visits and cast with all costs and attorney fees. Supervised visitation was to continue until the ex-husband successfully completed a treatment program for perpetrators of family violence prescribed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:364(C). Upon completion of the program, the ex-husband demanded joint custody of the parties' child or, alternatively, unsupervised visitation. The district court restored the ex-husband's normal visitation and awarded the ex-wife attorney fees plus interest. The ex-husband protested paying the award of attorney fees after having won unsupervised visitation. On appeal, the court found that (1) the attorney fees under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:367 were the obligation of the ex-husband, even though they were incurred by the ex-wife; (2) the district court was not plainly wrong in imposing the attorney fees without a specific prayer for relief; and (3) the district court did not abuse its discretion in awarding the attorney fees billed by the ex-wife's lawyer.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1611 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 01-KA-1007


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-1007 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/26/02); 811 So. 2d 1026; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 478



February 26, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 2002.
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Williams v. State, 999 So. 2d 751, 2009 La. LEXIS 1579 (La., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA NO. 99-3262, DIVISION "I". HONORABLE JO ELLEN GRANT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Convictions and sentences affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, for four counts of armed robbery and sentenced to 99 years' imprisonment on each count, each to run concurrently. The trial court then adjudged defendant a habitual felony offender and imposed one life sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the State elicited testimony from a woman whose car had been stolen days before the robbery. Specifically, the woman testified the car used in the robbery belonged to her, that it was stolen, and that gloves used in the robbery were found in the car when defendant was arrested in possession of the vehicle. On appeal, defendant argued the trial court erred by denying him a mistrial after the prosecutor used the car owner's testimony. Specifically, he argued the mention of the stolen car constituted impermissible other crimes evidence. Defendant also contended his life sentence was unconstitutionally excessive. The appellate court noted that generally evidence of other crimes was inadmissible because of the risk of grave prejudice to a defendant. The appellate court held even if the testimony was other crimes' evidence, it did not unambiguously point to defendant as the perpetrator of the car theft; thus, the trial court properly denied a mistrial. The appellate court concluded defendant's life sentence was a statutory mandatory minimum sentence and that he failed to rebut the presumption of the constitutionality of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1612 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Holmes


2001 KA 0955


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 0955 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/15/02); 811 So. 2d 955; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 218



February 15, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 312017-1 "B"), PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE ELAINE W. GUILLOT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In his sole assignment of error from the 22nd Judicial District Court, Tammany Parish (Louisiana), defendant, who had made a motion to quash, contended on appeal that the statute under which he was charged, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3, was unconstitutionally vague as written and as applied.


OVERVIEW: Generally, in order to preserve an alleged error for consideration on appeal, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 841 required that an objection be made to the irregularity at the time of its occurrence. Although defendant did not challenge the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3 in the proceedings below, the appellate court considered his challenge because he attacked the statute on its face. When the language of the statute was read in conjunction with a review of the history of the amendments to the statute, it was clear that the legislature intended to encompass areas such as public parks and recreational areas that were not within school boundaries. The appellate court found that the statute was not vague and was sufficiently clear and unambiguous to inform a person that violators were exposed to enhanced penalties when they engaged in prohibited conduct involving controlled dangerous substances in parks or recreational areas.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

 

1613 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Holmes


2001 KA 0956


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 0956 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/15/02); 811 So. 2d 960; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 220



February 15, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 312,918 "B"), PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE ELAINE W. GUILLOT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court (Louisiana) to four counts of distribution of cocaine in a drug free zone and one count of distribution of marijuana in a drug free zone, reserving his right to appeal. The trial court sentenced defendant on each count to 15 years at hard labor, without benefit of parole, and ordered that the sentences run concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the time of the pleas, the prosecutor and defense attorney stipulated that a factual basis existed for the charges; the trial court accepted the stipulations. The bill of information indicated that the offenses took place in a recreational park. Defendant contended that the statute under which he was charged, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3, was unconstitutionally vague as written and as applied. He contended that the recreational park was not property used for school purposes and, thus, did not fall within the areas addressed by and defined in the statute. He further argued that the Louisiana Legislature did not intend to include government-owned recreational areas that were not part of school property, as such areas were not specifically addressed in a separate subsection of the statute, as were drug treatment, religious, and public housing authority buildings and facilities. The State argued that the language of the statute was not vague and that the legislature clearly intended to include parks and recreational areas not identified with or adjacent to schools. The appellate court rejected defendant's arguments.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

1614 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 2001 KW 1027


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 1027 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/15/02); 809 So. 2d 556; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 221



February 15, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writs Eighteenth Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of West Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 963115. Honorable James J. Best, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  [**1] WRIT GRANTED IN PART AND DENIED IN PART. REMANDED FOR HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted in the Eighteenth Judicial District Court, West Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, for aggravated rape of a juvenile under the age of 12. The trial court denied his motions to quash the indictment and to discover and exclude hypnotically refreshed testimony, and defendant sought a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The crime charged in the indictment occurred 20 years before it was issued. At the time of the offense, it was a capital crime, and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 571 provided no prescriptive period for capital offenses. Imposition of the death penalty for this crime was found to be cruel and unusual punishment. The appellate court held that, even though the death penalty was not an available punishment, the associated procedural rules were still in effect, as no legislative action indicated an intention to change the lack of a prescriptive period for this offense. The exception to La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 510(C)(1), for child abuse prosecutions, giving the victim a privilege to refuse to disclose communications with her therapist, did not apply. If there was not significant prejudicial evidence induced by hypnosis, the victim's testimony was admissible, despite her hypnosis. The trial court's ruling that there was no indication the victim was hypnotized was based on a mistake of fact, requiring remand for an evidentiary hearing to allow defendant to inquire of the victim's therapist on this subject.


OUTCOME: The matter was remanded for an evidentiary hearing on the victim's hypnosis. Otherwise, writs were denied.

 

1615 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. A.P.


No. 2000 CA 2712


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 2712 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/15/02); 815 So. 2d 115; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 224



February 15, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the Juvenile Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 73,948. Honorable Marcia Harris Burden, Judge Ad Hoc, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED, AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state social services department challenged the judgment of the Juvenile Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which ordered the department to pay attorney's fees to appellee attorney for her representation of an indigent child, and reasonable attorney's fees for bringing the motion to compel payment.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile court appointed the attorney to represent a child alleged to be in need of care. The attorney submitted a request for payment to the department. The department denied the attorney's request, contending that payment to another attorney, who represented a parent in the proceeding, precluded payment to the attorney. The attorney filed a motion to compel payment of attorney's fees and reasonable costs and expenses incurred in the prosecution of the motion. On appeal, the department argued the clear language of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 46:460.21A(1) resulted in the attorney's representation being provided pro bono. The appellate court found the trial court exercised its constitutional authority to ensure fair proceedings when it ordered the department to pay the attorney. Accordingly, the appellate court concluded the trial court did not err in ordering the department to pay the attorney's legal fees. However, the appellate court found the amount the trial court awarded did not comport with the amount of attorney's fees either requested by the attorney or approved by the trial court, and the trial court erred in awarding reasonable attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The appellate court amended the judgment to reduce the amount of attorney's fees awarded and to delete the award of reasonable attorney's fees. The appellate court affirmed the judgment as amended.

 

1616 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Hull v. Stalder


2000 CA 2730


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 2730 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/15/02); 808 So. 2d 829; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 229



February 15, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 474,695 "I"), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE R. MICHAEL CALDWELL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which sustained its own exception of no cause of action and signed a judgment in favor of defendants, secretary of state corrections department and warden of correctional institute, dismissing the inmate's suit which challenged the institute's system for access to its law library.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court determined that because the inmate asserted no claim of actual injury or harm that had resulted from his limited access to the prison library, his petition stated merely a grievance against the prison system that addressed itself exclusively to the administration of the prison; it did not set forth a claim of deprivation of a constitutionally protected right. As such, the appellate court found the inmate's complaint about the prison's call-out procedure for library access was not the type of claim traditionally cognizable in a trial court, and thus was not a "civil matter" reserved for the trial court. Accordingly, because the administrative remedies set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171 et seq. provided the exclusive remedy available to the inmate for the type of grievance presented, the appellate court concluded his grievance should have been processed through administrative channels before being reviewed by the trial court. Therefore, the appellate court concluded the trial court did not have jurisdiction over the inmate's claim and its judgment sustaining the exception of no cause of action was void.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the dismissal of the inmate's petition but vacated the portion of the trial court's judgment that sustained an exception of no cause of action and assessed costs to the inmate.

 

1617 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


No. 2001-KA-1062


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001 1062 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/27/02); 812 So. 2d 139; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 456



February 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 4, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 413-394, SECTION "K". Honorable Arthur Hunter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish (Louisiana) of attempted possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute. The trial court sentenced him to two years' imprisonment at hard labor and fined him. The trial court granted defendant's motion for appeal. Pursuant to a multiple bill, the defendant was re-sentenced as a triple offender to two years at hard labor with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: The arresting officers approached defendant and four other men who were loitering. The officers saw defendant leave the other men, throw something over a fence, and return to the group. The officers secured the men and retrieved the object defendant had discarded, a bag of crack cocaine. On appeal, the court found that the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence because (1) the object was discarded by defendant without police interference, and, therefore, the officers could retrieve it; (2) defendant had no expectation of privacy; (3) the abandonment gave the officers reasonable suspicion -- sufficient articulable knowledge of particular facts and circumstances -- to justify detaining defendant; and (4) once the object was retrieved, and it appeared to be crack cocaine, the officers had probable cause to arrest, as facts and circumstances within their knowledge, based on reasonable and trustworthy information, justified a belief that defendant had committed a crime. However, the trial court erred by failing to sentence defendant to life as a third felony offender without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

1618 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Daniel


No. 2001-KA-1736


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-1736 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/13/02); 811 So. 2d 84; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 569



February 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 414-743, SECTION "L". Honorable Terry Alarcon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), one defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and sentenced to five years at hard labor, while the other defendant was convicted of simple possession of cocaine and sentenced to two years at hard labor. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants sold crack cocaine from a street corner, in plain view of the arresting officers. The appellate court held the officers had probable cause to arrest and search defendants. At one defendant's sentencing, no reasons for his minimum mandatory sentence were stated. Because the trial court imposed the lowest possible sentence, there was no reason to require compliance with the provisions of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1, calling for a statement of the reasons for a sentence, as the sentence was statutorily mandated. There was no evidence rebutting the presumption that defendant's minimum mandatory sentence was constitutional. The trial court did not enunciate the requirement of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967B(4)(b) that at least the first five years of defendant's sentence be served without the benefit of parole. Under the self-activating provision of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:301.1A, as well as La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 882, the appellate court could recognize that five years of defendant's sentence were to be served without benefit of parole, as the trial court had no discretion regarding this condition.


OUTCOME: One defendant's sentence was modified to provide that its first five years would be served without benefit of parole, and, as amended, defendants' convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

1619 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mitchell


01-0872


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-0872 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/13/02); 815 So. 2d 1041; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 186



February 13, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, NO. 98-183507, HONORABLE PAUL J. deMAHY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana), entered a final judgment of convictions after a jury found defendant guilty of manslaughter in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31(A)(1) and aggravated battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two acquaintances attempted to visit the home of defendant's girlfriend and child. While at the home, they were harassed by three neighborhood men. An altercation turned physical and caused defendant to retreat. When defendant and one acquaintance returned later, they were approached by the same three men. One of the men, a man of considerable size, approached the acquaintance. One of the other men left and returned with a bat. In short, the evidence indicated defendant was presented with a quickly escalating situation. While the evidence indicated defendant may have had sufficient time to retreat or sound a warning, he instead further escalated the confrontation by firing shots and killing the large man that had approached the acquaintance. The men then scattered, but a neighborhood man walking by froze. Defendant then shot that man twice. After defendant was convicted on two charges, the appellate court found the evidence was sufficient to support both convictions. Even though conflicts existed in witness's testimony, it was for the trier of fact, not the appellate court, to resolve those conflicts, and the jury's resolution was not irrational.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the matter was remanded to inform defendant of post-conviction relief deadlines.

 

1620 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Butler


No. 01-KA-0907


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-0907 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/13/02); 812 So. 2d 120; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 197



February 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-1903, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE CHARLES V. CUSIMANO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to suppress was denied, defendant was convicted of first degree robbery. The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, sentenced him to eight and one-half years at hard labor, but conditionally court suspended two years of the sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the early morning hours, an officer spotted a car partially hidden between two dumpsters behind a closed bank, in an area where burglaries recently occurred. He asked defendant why he was parked behind the building at that hour. A second officer saw an ATM card on the ground near defendant's car; defendant denied any knowledge of the card. From a phone call to the issuer of the card, the officer learned it had been stolen; he called the card's owner, who described the man who had robbed her hours before. Her description matched defendant; some clothing she described was found in his car. The appellate court held that, after finding the card near defendant's vehicle, and learning it had been stolen, the officers had reasonable suspicion of a crime sufficient to justify a Terry stop. Reasonable suspicion ripened into probable cause for arrest when the officer spoke to the victim and heard her describe the robber. The suppression motion was thus properly denied. But the trial court erred in suspending a portion of defendant's sentence, as suspension of a sentence in a first degree robbery conviction violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.1(B).


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, but the case was remanded to the trial court for re-sentencing and to advise defendant of the two-year prescriptive period for filing an application for post-conviction relief.

 

1621 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. 01-KA-0842


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-0842 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/13/02); 812 So. 2d 106; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 198



February 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 2002.
Writ of error denied State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 840 So. 2d 532, 2003 La. LEXIS 762 (La., Mar. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-6773, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE HENRY G. SULLIVAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, denied defendant's motion to suppress and his oral motion in limine regarding identification evidence. He was convicted of 2 counts of armed robbery and sentenced to 2 concurrent terms of 49.5 years' imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. He was then found to be a third-felony offender and sentenced to life imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: An armed man approached a couple in a car at 2:00 a.m. An unarmed man then approached. The woman of the couple let him in. He demanded money and frisked her. She gave him her keys. The couple got out and the robbers fled. Police soon responded and the couple gave descriptions. Within 2 hours, police drove the couple within 25 feet of a suspect. The couple identified defendant as the unarmed robber. At trial, the woman testified that the area of the robbery was well lit and that she saw defendant during the robbery for a few seconds. The appellate court found that defendant failed to prove that the "show-up" identification's suggestiveness created a very substantial likelihood of misidentification. The trial court did not err in not admitting a transcript of the woman's recorded description into evidence. It had been used to refresh her memory and not for impeachment purposes. Thus her testimony, not the transcript, was the evidence. As to one apparent discrepancy between the male victim's trial testimony and transcript, the defense took no further steps to impeach. Defendant's prior crimes were violent and his habitual offender life term was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1622 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Knight


No. 01-KA-881


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-881 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/13/02); 811 So. 2d 947; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 201



February 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-5559, DIVISION "F". THE HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his multiple offender adjudication and sentence imposed by the 24th Judicial District Court, Jefferson Parish, Louisiana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to felony theft of property between $ 100 and $ 500 and was sentenced to two years' hard labor. The State filed an information alleging that defendant was a fourth felony offender, and sought a life sentence pursuant to former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(c)(ii). Defendant admitted that he had committed the alleged offenses but argued that the imposition of a life sentence would be unconstitutionally excessive as the offenses involved drugs and theft to obtain drugs. The trial court agreed and resentenced defendant to 20 years hard labor. Defendant argued that the trial court had not advised him of his right to a hearing and to remain silent, as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(D)(1)(a), (3), and that the 20 year sentence was excessive. The appellate court held that the fact that defendant was advised of the right to a hearing by his counsel was sufficient to comply with the statute. Any failure to advise defendant of the right to remain silent was harmless. The trial court had properly found a life sentence would have been excessive and departed downward. The sentence imposed was not constitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence were affirmed.

 

1623 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


La. Electorate of Gays & Lesbians, Inc. v. State


No. 99-CA-2949


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-2949 (La. App. 4 Cir., 2/7/02); 2002 La. App. LEXIS 270



February 7, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Application for Rehearing Denied February 7, 2002. Released for Publication February 7, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: (CDC# 94-9260). DIVISION "A-5".



DISPOSITION: Application for rehearing denied; appeal transferred.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff organization's appeal was dismissed from Louisiana Division A-5 Court for lack of jurisdiction. The organization filed an application for rehearing en banc/motion to transfer to the supreme court wherein it requested that the entire court reconsider its appeal or, alternatively, that its appeal be transferred to the supreme court for consideration.


OVERVIEW: The instant court dismissed the organization's appeal for lack of jurisdiction and determined that the supreme court had jurisdiction. The organization than filed its motion for rehearing/motion to transfer. The organization reasoned that its request was to promote justice and to expedite the business of the court. The instant court found that the outcome with a full court would not differ from its original opinion issued by the current panel. Furthermore, the instant court found that it made more sense for the supreme court to consider whether the trial court's ruling concerning the unconstitutionality of certain statutes was correct. The instant court found no reason not to transfer the organization's appeal to the supreme court pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2162.


OUTCOME: The application for rehearing en banc was denied; the motion to transfer to the supreme court was granted.

 

1624 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Benson v. City of Marksville


01-1078


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-1078 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/06/02); 812 So. 2d 687; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 157



February 6, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWELFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF AVOYELLES, NUMBER 99-6595 B WILLIAM BENNETT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana), awarded attorney fees and costs pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 971 to defendant property owner after the denial of his motion to strike was reversed and plaintiff individual and corporation's petition against him alleging defamation and violation of their constitutional rights was dismissed. The individual and corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner complained numerous times to police about noise coming from the individual and corporation's nightclub. Citations were issued to the individual. He was tried in city court for noise violations. He allegedly was acquitted on all charges. The individual then brought a defamation claim against the property owner for making allegedly unfounded complaints. The property owner moved to strike pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 971, enacted two months after the individual and corporation's suit was filed. The law allowed a defendant to seek dismissal of a claim asserted against him for exercising his petition or free speech rights. Eventually, denial of the motion was reversed and the defamation and constitutional claims were dismissed. After attorney fees and costs were awarded to the property owner pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 971B, the appellate court found that applying that provision to award such fees and costs was error. It found that since the provision changed the law by creating a new obligation to pay fees and costs, the provision was substantive and could not be applied retroactively to award attorney fees and costs.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1625 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


No. 2001-KA-1268


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-1268 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/06/02); 809 So. 2d 1127; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 250



February 6, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 28, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 420-370, SECTION "F". Honorable Dennis J. Waldron, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED; AS AMENDED AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and a confession. Defendant then pled guilty to simple burglary and he was sentenced to eight years at hard labor as a third-felony offender. Defendant appealed. Defense counsel filed an Anders brief and requested to withdraw as counsel.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant argued the trial court erred in finding probable cause at the preliminary hearing because he did not commit the crime. The appellate court found that even if this position was tenable, the issue was moot. Defendant claimed that he did not remove the items from the car but found them on the street while the State presented a strong basis for believing defendant committed the criminal act in question. Thus, the appellate court found defendant's plea satisfied the Alford requirements in that there was a strong factual showing for the plea. However, it also found that the trial court erred when it sentenced defendant to serve eight years without benefit of probation or suspension as La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4 required that defendant's eligibility for parole should be left to the determination of the department of corrections.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed and his sentence was amended to delete that portion of the eight-year sentence prohibiting probation eligibility.

 

1626 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Huckabay


No. 2000-KA-1082


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1082 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/06/02); 809 So. 2d 1093; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 256



February 6, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 28, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 399-936, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by a grand jury indictment with first degree murder. He was jointly indicted with another, who was at large at the time of defendant's trial. The Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana), after a jury trial, convicted defendant of second degree murder. His motion for new trial was denied. He was sentenced to life imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A man's body was found in the street. Police found his apartment two weeks later; defendant and a woman and her 14-year old daughter were inside, along with an apparently bloodstained sofa. A search warrant was later executed; the apartment appeared to have been cleaned, but bloody items were recovered. Defendant denied the killing. Three years later, the daughter was found in Mississippi with an unrelated criminal suspect, and was put in a mental institution. Meanwhile, defendant had not tried to hide. The daughter gave a new, detailed statement that blamed her mother and defendant for the planned killing. The appellate court found that as defendant had not received the death penalty, he had no valid Witherspoon complaints. Prospective jurors with health problems, and one with a likely attention problem, were properly dismissed. A burned car found near the homicide scene one day later, which a police report linked to a homicide, was irrelevant. The trial court's disallowance of development of testimony on whether the daughter had known of a warrant for her arrest was harmless error, as was the prosecutor's marginal appeal to the jury as potential crime victims.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1627 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kennerson


01-1088


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-1088 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/06/02); 817 So. 2d 110; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 158



February 6, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWELFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF AVOYELLES, NOS. 84,984; 85,076; 85,114; 85,115; 85,116; 85,117; 85,302; and 85,303. HONORABLE WILLIAM BENNETT.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's sentences for theft and simple burglary were vacated and his case was remanded for resentencing, the Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana), consolidated the offenses. He was adjudicated a second felony offender, and sentenced to an effective term of 42 years in prison. His motion for reconsideration was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant committed various thefts and two simple burglary offenses. He was found guilty on all counts. He was then adjudicated and sentenced as a third habitual offender. The appellate court later vacated all sentences and remanded for resentencing. The trial court consolidated the offenses for resentencing. Defendant was determined to be only a second felony offender. The trial court imposed six sentences of seven years each, to run consecutive to each other, and without benefit of parole. It then imposed a seventh sentence to run concurrent with any other sentence. In a minute entry two years later, it attempted to amend one sentence. After the sentences were imposed and defendant's motion for reconsideration was denied, the appellate court found the parole restriction could not be imposed on a second felony offender. It also found the minute entry could not be used to amend a sentence already being served. It then found no abuse of sentencing discretion regarding defendant's cumulative 42-year sentence, as he was a career criminal and second felony offender. Finally, it found he should be informed of the two-year time period for requesting postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The sentences on four separate convictions for theft were affirmed, but the parole eligibility restriction was ordered deleted. An amended sentence on four counts of theft imposed by a minute entry was vacated and an earlier sentence imposed was reinstated. Two sentences, each involving two theft convictions, were remanded for sentencing clarification. An appeal on two counts of simple burglary was dismissed, and the case was remanded.

 

1628 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Albercht


No. 2001-KA-1664


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-1664 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/30/02); 809 So. 2d 472; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 169



January 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 21, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 419-193, SECTION "J". Honorable Leon Cannizzaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) of attempted possession of pornography involving a juvenile and pleaded guilty to contributing to the delinquency of a juvenile. She was sentenced to five years incarceration on the first offense, without benefits, and two years, concurrent, on the second offense. She appealed her sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant watched and participated while her husband videotaped her 16-year-old daughter performing various sexual acts, including engaging in sexual intercourse with her boyfriend. The appellate court found it was reasonable to infer from defendant's age (51) that she understood her participation in the exploitation of her daughter. She did nothing to halt her daughter's sexual abuse and, if she were powerless under the circumstances, it was because she chose to be. It could reasonably be found that defendant was one of the worst offenders and merited the maximum sentence, so the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing that term.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

1629 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Rosen v. State


No. 2001-CA-0499


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-0499 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/30/02); 809 So. 2d 498; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 173



January 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 21, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 95-9836, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE MICHAEL G. BAGNERIS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee motorist sued appellant state transportation department in the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), for injuries received in his automobile's collision with a concrete abutment on a state highway. The trial court entered judgment for the motorist, and the department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motorist ran into a bridge abutment that had no guardrail. The appellate court found that, under applicable law, the highway department had to keep the highway in a safe condition, and the requirement of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800, that the state have actual or constructive notice of a defect in order for liability to attach, did not apply. The trial court's finding of fact that the motorist was not responsible for the accident was not clearly erroneous. The weight the trial court gave the motorist's properly qualified experts was not clearly wrong. Once the department rebuilt this part of the highway, its own policies obliged it to place a guardrail in front of the abutment, under the standards of the American Association of State Highway and Transportation Officials (AASHTO); and whether to place the guardrail was no longer discretionary or immune, but was non-discretionary and subject to a duty/risk analysis of liability. Under that analysis, the department was liable for the motorist's injuries. While the department did not have to bring an old highway up to AASHTO standards, it had a duty to correct this unreasonably hazardous condition on the old highway.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1630 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Wiley v. City of New Orleans


No. 2000-CA-1544


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1544 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/30/02); 2002 La. App. LEXIS 178



January 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication March 21, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 94-10309, DIVISION "K-14". HONORABLE RICHARD J. GANUCHEAU, JUDGE.

Wiley v. City of New Orleans, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1592 (La. App. 4th Cir. May 16, 2001) 



DISPOSITION: Limited rehearing granted; affirmed as amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed a judgment by the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Division "K" (Louisiana), challenging the constitutionality of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2323.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that amendments to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2323 concerning apportionment of damages were unconstitutional. The appellate court found no invasion of any inherent judicial power by the legislature. The substantive right to allocate fault was created in 1979 with the introduction of comparative fault. As such, 1996 La. Acts 3 simply delineated a method for enforcing that substantive right as particularly applied to a statutory employer. Because the legislative changes in Act 3 were procedural, they could be applied retroactively. The employee did not have a substantive right to have a non-party's fault assigned to the parties who were found at fault.


OUTCOME: A limited rehearing was granted and the judgment was affirmed as amended.

 

1631 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brooks


No. 01-KA-864


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-864 (La. App. 5 Cir. 01/29/02); 807 So. 2d 1090; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 110



January 29, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 14, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-2509, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE JOSEPH F. GREFER AND MELVIN ZENO, JUDGES PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Underlying conviction affirmed, multiple offender vacated, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), of possession of cocaine. The trial court found defendant was a third felony offender and imposed an enhanced sentence of life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two police officers were in a neighborhood with a high rate of narcotics activity. One officer observed defendant engage in a hand-to-hand transaction. When the officers drove up to defendant, he fled. One officer began running after defendant, identifying himself as a police officer. That officer saw defendant place something in his mouth. When he caught defendant, defendant hit the police officer. When the other officer arrived he hit defendant in the stomach and a rock of crack cocaine flew out of defendant's mouth. On appeal, the court found (1) the trial court was correct to deny defendant's suppression motion because the officers had reasonable suspicion to conduct an investigatory stop; (2) the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to strike the all-white jury panel because defendant failed to meet his burden of showing that African-Americans were systematically excluded from the jury selection process; (3) a proper foundation was laid for the admission of the cocaine into evidence; and (4) the multiple offender enhancement was improper because there was a failure to prove the expiration of the cleansing period between the predicates and the instant offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the conviction, the judgment was vacated as to the multiple offender finding, and the case was remanded to allow the State to re-try the multiple offender bill.

State v. Scott


No. 34,949-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,949 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/25/02); 823 So. 2d 960; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 93



January 25, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Scott, 843 So. 2d 1122, 2003 La. LEXIS 1653 (La., May 16, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 45,633. Honorable R. Wayne Smith, Judge.
State v. Scott, 796 So. 2d 931, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1734 (La.App. 2 Cir., May 10, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana, defendant was convicted of aggravated incest, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78.1, for his act of raping his 14-year-old daughter. Defendant was adjudicated a third-felony offender and was sentenced to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal, inter alia, that the trial court erred in (1) denying his challenge for cause to a prospective juror who expressed problems with the standards for the case; (2) denying his motion for a mistrial where a witness referred to defendant having been in jail; (3) admitting a judgment of paternity; (4) adjudicating him a third-felony offender where a predicate offense was based on a defective guilty plea; and (5) imposing an unconstitutionally excessive sentence. The appellate court held that the challenge to the juror was properly denied, as the juror ultimately expressed his ability to make a decision based on the evidence and the law. The refusal to grant a mistrial was not an abuse of discretion, as the jail reference was not an unambiguous reference to another crime. The paternity judgment was properly admitted, as it was relevant and probative and fell within a La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 803 hearsay exception. The guilty plea underlying the challenged predicate offense was voluntary and was not defective. The mandatory sentence was tailored to defendant's culpability and defendant failed to rebut the presumption of the sentence's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction; defendant's adjudication as a third-felony offender; and defendant's sentence of life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.

State v. Lee

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT

January 23, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 200,229. Honorable Charles R. Scott, II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of armed robbery. The trial court found him to be a third felony offender and sentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After giving the victim and her friend a ride to a convenience store, defendant asked the victim if she had any money. When the victim showed defendant her money, defendant pulled a gun and demanded the money. When the victim resisted defendant's efforts to steal the money, defendant struck her, took the money, and left in a car with others. The victim and her friend were able to identify defendant from a photo lineup provided by the police. They also testified that they were familiar with defendant before this incident and identified him. On appeal, the court found (1) the State sustained its burden to negate the possibility of misidentification, and the evidence from the women's testimony established guilt beyond a reasonable doubt; (2) there was no suggestiveness in the pictures or the procedures used for conducting a photographic lineup, so misidentification of defendant was unlikely; (3) defendant's prior guilty pleas to felonies were properly used to show defendant's predicate offenses as a habitual offender; and (4) defendant failed to rebut the presumption that his mandatory life sentence was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

January 23, 2002; , Decided

Writ of error denied State v. Howard, 824 So. 2d 1187, 2002 La. LEXIS 2642 (La., Sept. 13, 2002)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), denied defendant's motion to suppress and entered a final judgment of conviction after it found him guilty of possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967. The State then alleged defendant was a multiple offender. After his new trial motion was denied and he was adjudged to be a second felony offender, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police officers observed defendant take currency from someone and give that person a small white object. The officers further observed defendant place a plastic bag in his vehicle. They found rocks of cocaine in his vehicle and a large sum of United States currency on his person. The trial court found defendant guilty. The State then filed a multiple bill of information alleging he was a second felony offender. The trial court later sentenced defendant to prison time. The trial court denied his continuance request even though he unfamiliar with the case. After he was sentenced, the appellate court found he was not prejudiced by the sentencing delay. It also found the evidence supported his conviction. However, it further held the failure to grant the continuance meant he was denied effective assistance of counsel and the State had to present multiple offender documentation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed. However, defendant's adjudication and sentence pursuant to the State's multiple bill of information alleging defendant was a multiple offender was reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings in the trial court.

State v. Phillips


01-0253


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-0253 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/16/02); 809 So. 2d 467; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 54



January 16, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 27, 2002. Released for Publication February 27, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, NO. 98-184609, HONORABLE GERARD B. WATTIGNY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a plea agreement, defendant pled guilty to a reduced charge of one count of possession of cocaine in excess of 28 grams and not more than 200 grams. The Sixteenth Judicial District Court, St. Martin Parish, Louisiana, sentenced him to 35 years at hard labor to run concurrent with a 15-year sentence he received for a plea in federal court for violations based on identical facts to the state proceedings. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant complained that his sentence was unconstitutionally excessive and that the State's prosecution of charges under the Louisiana criminal statute constituted double jeopardy because he was also prosecuted for similar violations under federal criminal law as a result of the same arrest. The appellate court found that other than the federal court felony plea, defendant had no prior felonies. Furthermore, several witnesses detailed defendant's cooperation with federal authorities and local law enforcement agencies in solving other cases. Contrary to the trial court's observations, the record was devoid of any proof of the possibility or probability of recidivism by defendant. The appellate court concluded that 35-year sentence imposed by the trial court shocked its sense of justice. Under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 597, the prosecution of charges under both state and federal criminal statutes did not place defendant in jeopardy of being prosecuted twice for the same crime.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, the sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

State v. Rice


No. 2001-KA-0215


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-0215 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/16/02); 807 So. 2d 350; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 86



January 16, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 7, 2002.
Writ denied by State v. Rice, 824 So. 2d 1186, 2002 La. LEXIS 2645 (La., Sept. 13, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 414-381, SECTION "B". Honorable Patrick G. Quinlan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, sentence vacated, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with possession of crack cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C). A six-person jury, before the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, found him guilty as charged, and the State charged him as a third-felony habitual offender. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer detained defendant, while another officer retrieved a small plastic bag containing crack cocaine. Defendant was placed under arrest and advised of his rights. Subsequently, he informed the officers that he was a drug user, not a drug seller, and further admitted that the cocaine belonged to him. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii), when the third felony or either one of the two prior felony convictions is a felony defined as a crime of violence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §14:2(13) the only sentence was life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence. Nevertheless, the district court was aware that the second felony conviction was for defendant's possession of a crack pipe. As to the first felony conviction, defendant pleaded guilty to attempted sexual battery, which, at the time defendant was sentenced, was not defined as a crime of violence. Further, the district court failed to state for the record that it was a crime of violence. This required reconsideration of the sentence pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction, but remanded the matter for the sentence to be reconsidered.

State v. Aleman


No. 01-KA-743


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-743 (La.App. 5 Cir. 01/15/02); 809 So. 2d 1056; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 52



January 15, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 14, 2002.
Writ of error denied State v. Aleman, 2003 La. LEXIS 641 (La., Mar. 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 95-6019, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE.
State ex rel. Aleman v. State, 745 So. 2d 601, 1999 La. LEXIS 2383 (La., Oct. 1, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon remand to allow defendant to withdraw his guilty pleas, the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, after a jury trial, convicted him of three counts of first degree robbery. The State filed a habitual offender bill of information, and defendant received 2 10-year sentences and an enhanced 20-year sentence, all consecutive. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Witnesses identified defendant as a robber with a wig, cap, and glasses. An officer testified that such things, and also a toy revolver and money which could not be traced to the second bank robbed, were recovered from defendant's apartment. A teller robbed in the second bank testified that she neither saw a weapon nor did defendant's use of his hands indicate that he had a gun, but that she assumed from what he had said that he had one, and she immediately complied with his demand. The appellate court found the evidence sufficient to show a subjective belief on that teller's part that defendant was armed with a dangerous weapon, which belief was objectively reasonable given that others either saw his hand move under his shirt or what one teller believed was a gun. The State satisfied its State v. Prieur burden for admission of similar-plan evidence of a later "wig" bank robbery where defendant's fingerprints were found. The trial court had discretion to sentence consecutively, despite the presumption for concurrence, as to the two robberies in the second bank. The sentence was not vindictive despite exceeding the sentence for which he originally plea-bargained.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.
