Perez v. Trahant


2000 CA 2372


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 2372 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/28/01); 806 So. 2d 110; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 3124



December 28, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of error denied Perez v. Trahant, 823 So. 2d 953, 2002 La. LEXIS 2528 (La., Aug. 30, 2002)
Writ of error denied Perez v. Trahant, 823 So. 2d 953, 2002 La. LEXIS 2529 (La., Aug. 30, 2002)
Related proceeding at Trahant v. Perez, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 719 (La.App. 4 Cir., Mar. 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 99-13899 C), PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE PATRICIA T. HEDGES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana, dismissed appellant former client's demands alleging legal malpractice against appellee attorney as untimely. The former client appealed and challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605.


OVERVIEW: The former client challenged judgment against him, contending that it was error to dismiss his claim, and if the claim was untimely, then the time limitations set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605 were unconstitutional as applied in his case. Further, the attorney filed a motion seeking to convert his prescription exception to an exception of no cause of action, raising the issue of accrual of the peremptive period. The appeals court, in answering the attorney's motion, held that the former client was well aware that he had lost the case and possibly would also lose it on appeal. The one-year statutorily-imposed time limitation for filing legal malpractice claims thus began to run on the date the jury returned its verdict against him and expired one-year later. Therefore, the court granted the exception of prescription filed by the attorney. Under the facts of this case, the former client could not seek suspension of peremption by insisting on application of continuous representation principles. Because the constitutional issue was not litigated, the case was remanded.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding the demands were untimely was affirmed, however the matter was remanded to allow the former client to specially plead the facts supporting his contention that the statute was unconstitutional and for the issue to be fully briefed and litigated.

Joseph v. Hosp. Serv. Dist. No. 2


2001 CA 1951


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 1951 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/28/01); 805 So. 2d 400; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 3151



December 28, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication.
Writ denied by Joseph v. Hosp. Serv. Dist. No. 2, 813 So. 2d 1083, 2002 La. LEXIS 1359 (La., Apr. 19, 2002)
Related proceeding at St. Mary Anesthesia Assocs. v. Hosp. Serv. Dist. No. 2, 836 So. 2d 379, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3995 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 20, 2002)
Related proceeding at Joseph v. Hosp. Serv. Dist. No. 2, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1912 (La.App. 1 Cir., Aug. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 106,767), PARISH OF ST. MARY, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE JOHN E. CONERY, JUDGE.
Joseph v. Hosp. Serv. Dist. No. 2, 805 So. 2d 413, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 3150 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 28, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, an anesthesia services provider and doctors, sued appellants, hospital district and its executive officer, in the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana), for injunctive and declaratory relief because of an alleged violation of the Louisiana Open Meetings Law. The trial court found the hospital district operated in violation of the Open Meetings Law. The hospital district and its executive officer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The hospital district entered into a contract with the anesthesia services provider for the provision of anesthesia services to a hospital. The newly appointed executive officer of the hospital sought to void the contract, which could be voided only for cause by the hospital district. The executive officer voided the contract by letter. The hospital district's board of commissioners affirmed the action following an executive session. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in concluding discussions at the meeting were in violation of the Louisiana Open Meetings Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:4.1 et seq. The executive session fulfilled the stated purpose of the Louisiana Enhanced Ability to Compete Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 46:1070-46:1076, because the discussions of the board regarding the viability of the contract constituted part of the hospital's plan to continue to provide anesthesia services to its patients and were certainly related to the hospital's ability to protect its competitive edge in the health care market.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for consideration and a ruling on the constitutionality of the Louisiana Enhanced Ability to Compete Act.

State v. Wilson


01-0625


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-0625 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/28/01); 806 So. 2d 854; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 3155



December 28, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF EVANGELINE, NO. 60574-FA, HONORABLE PRESTON N. AUCOIN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART: THEFT CONVICTION VACATED AND SET ASIDE; FORGERY CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of theft between $ 100 and $ 500, and forgery. Defendant appealed his convictions and resulting sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a contract to transport clients for a social welfare program. He forged the signature of a client who was no longer using the service, and turned in log-sheets bearing the forged signatures for reimbursement. Based upon the falsified signatures, the program overpaid defendant. Defendant was charged with violations of the forgery statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:72, and theft between $ 100 and $ 500 in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:67. He was convicted on both charges, and sentences were entered. After judgment was entered, defendant argued the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions, that the trial court improperly charged the deadlocked jury, that the trial court failed to remove a juror for cause, that a Batson violation occurred, that his convictions on both charges violated double jeopardy principles, and that his sentences were excessive. However, the appellate court found the alleged errors were meritless except for the double jeopardy argument. It found that because the same evidence was used to convict on both charges, double jeopardy principles applied and the remedy was to vacate the conviction on the lesser sentence, the theft.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence for theft were vacated, but the judgment of conviction and sentence for forgery were affirmed.

Stroud v. Morrison Nursery


01-931

The Office of Workers' Compensation, Lafayette Parish, Louisiana, denied the employer's exception of res judicata and the employee's claim for penalties and attorney fees. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee brought an action for the reinstatement of her benefits when the Louisiana Supreme Court determined the section under which her benefits were previously terminated was unconstitutional. The workers' compensation office ruled that the employee was entitled to have the benefits reinstated retroactive to the date of termination; it also denied the employee's claim for penalties and attorney fees. DISPOSITION: Affirmed..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Plaquemines 25th Judicial District Court (Louisiana) of distribution of cocaine and sentenced to 17 1/2 years at hard labor without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. The trial court granted defendant's oral motion for appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that: (1) his sentence was excessive; (2) the trial court erred by sentencing him to serve the first five years of his sentence without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence; (3) he had ineffective assistance of counsel; and (4) the trial court erred by allowing the admissibility of the photo line-up absent evidence of a physical description of the suspect and proper foundation. State v. Antoine


01-1036


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-1036 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/26/01); 804 So. 2d 869; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 3158



December 26, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 9585-99. HONORABLE FRED R. GODWIN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 14th Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), by jury, convicted defendant of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. He was adjudicated an habitual offender and sentenced to 15 years' imprisonment. On appeal, his appellate counsel's Anders brief failed to satisfy certain requirements and a new brief was ordered. Both a new Anders brief and defendant's pro se brief were filed.


OVERVIEW: Police were informed defendant was selling crack from his residence. Police got and executed a search warrant and found crack, among other places, under a couch defendant was sitting on. At trial, an officer testified that the amount found was not consistent with mere personal use. The appellate court found that defendant had constructive possession of the narcotics. He had access to where the crack was found and was closer to it than the other two people in the residence. Defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims were more appropriately pursued in post-conviction proceedings. The reasonable doubt jury instructions, stating that reasonable doubt was doubt based upon reason and common sense, and considered in their totality, were not likely to have been misapplied by the jury. The trial court issued reasons for the sentence, commented upon mitigators, and sentenced defendant to the minimum sentence allowable. Thus the sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The sentence was deemed to contain a provision indicating that the first five years were to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Farrell v. Am. Heavy Lift Shipping, Co.


No. 2001-CA-0693


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-0693 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/19/01); 805 So. 2d 336; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 3181; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8669



December 19, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 7, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2000-10527, DIVISION "N-8". Honorable Ethel Simms Julien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), rendered judgment affirming the decision of defendant labor department review board which denied plaintiff employee's claim for unemployment compensation. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a union member, was allegedly employed by defendant employer. She was then laid off. She received vacation pay, owed to her as a result of the collective bargaining agreement, in a lump sum payment which covered the next two months. The employee filed for unemployment benefits. The administrative law judge (ALJ) found the employee was eligible to receive a certain amount per week in benefits. Her vacation pay, when prorated, exceeded that weekly benefit amount. Since the vacation pay was treated as wages under the applicable statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1601(7)(d), the ALJ denied her claim for benefits. After the trial court affirmed, the appellate court found the statute was not ambiguous. While it was true the title and preamble of the related bill showed an intent not to count vacation pay received pursuant to a collective bargaining agreement as wages, the title and preamble were not part of the law and the statute's enacted version only showed that vacation pay should be counted as wages. The appellate court also found the statute was not unconstitutional and the federal ERISA law was not related to nor did it regulate the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Bunley


No. 2000-KA-0405


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-0405 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/12/01); 805 So. 2d 292; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 3034



December 12, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 31, 2002.
Writ denied by State v. Bunley, 836 So. 2d 41, 2003 La. LEXIS 258 (La., Jan. 24, 2003)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Bunley v. State, 926 So. 2d 538, 2006 La. LEXIS 1398 (La., Apr. 24, 2006)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Bunley v. State, 2015 La. LEXIS 1050 (La., Apr. 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 388-723, SECTION "G". HONORABLE JULIAN A. PARKER, JUDGE.
State v. Coston, 720 So. 2d 714, 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2633 (La.App. 4 Cir., Sept. 16, 1998)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; MOTION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish, Louisiana, that convicted her on a jury verdict of second-degree murder and sentenced her to life imprisonment. The State moved to supplement the record with defendant's videotaped statements.


OVERVIEW: Defendant led police to the 76-year-old victim's smoldering body. She admitted plotting with a man to "set up" the victim to rob her, but claimed that this man killed the victim and set fire to her corpse. Trial evidence showed that the victim died of suffocation consistent with her mouth and nose being covered with duct tape, and that defendant had forged the victim's signature on checks which she cashed. The appellate court held that the prosecutor had not improperly referred to earlier forgeries by defendant in his opening statement. A pathologist's opinion that the victim was killed was not an improper opinion that defendant was guilty. The jury instructions were not confusing. The evidence was sufficient to convict. Allegedly gruesome photos of the victim's corpse were properly admitted to explain the pathologist's conclusion that suffocation, not burning, was the cause of death. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to preserve for review the claim that defendant's life sentence was excessive, because it was not. The appellate court allowed the State to supplement the record with videotapes of defendant's statements, as they were sufficiently identified.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the State's motion to supplement the record was granted.

 

1646 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. Moore


01-878


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-878 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/12/01); 805 So. 2d 277; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2956



December 12, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied February 6, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ELEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF SABINE, NO. 42,614, HONORABLE ROBERT E. BURGESS.



DISPOSITION: We reverse in part, amend in part, and otherwise affirm.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mother, on behalf of herself and her minor child, sued appellant, the Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD), alleging that a defective intersection caused an auto accident in which the mother and her child were injured, and her other child was killed. The Eleventh Judicial District, Parish of Sabine, Louisiana, rendered judgment that the DODT was 100 percent liable for the accident. The DODT appealed.


OVERVIEW: As the mother was waiting to make a left turn, another driver changed lanes, and struck the mother's vehicle from behind, pushing into oncoming traffic. The mother and her two children were injured; one child died of her injuries. The appellate court held that the trial's court's viewing of the scene of the accident was not an abuse of discretion, as it did so to better visualize the scene, and did not conduct experiments or take measurements. While the trial court erred in requiring the mother to prove notice, this error did not harm the DODT. The trial court did not err in finding the DOTD at fault for the accident, as the evidence showed that the highway created an unreasonable risk of harm to a left-turning motorist. However, it was error to assess 100 percent of the fault to the DODT, as the other driver had switched lanes without ensuring that it was safe to do so. The award of $ 750,00 in mental distress damages to the mother was not supported by the evidence, and was reduced. As there was no evidence that the child remembered the accident, the award to her of damages for mental distress was also reversed. The remaining damage awards were supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The portion of the judgment finding the DOTDT to be 100 percent at fault was reversed, and the DOTD was assessed with 80 percent of the fault, and the non-party driver was assessed with 20 percent of the fault. The damage award to the mother for mental distress was reduced from $ 750,000 to $ 200,000. The damage award to the child for mental distress was reversed. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

State v. Richthofen


No. 01-KA-500


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-500 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/27/01); 803 So. 2d 171; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2766



November 27, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 14, 2002.
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Richthofen, 836 So. 2d 57, 2003 La. LEXIS 336 (La., Jan. 31, 2003)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Richthofen v. State, 904 So. 2d 687, 2005 La. LEXIS 2010 (La., June 17, 2005)
Related proceeding at Richthofen v. Cain, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99186 (E.D. La., Feb. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-992, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE HENRY G. SULLIVAN, JR., JUDGE.
State v. Richthofen, 754 So. 2d 926, 2000 La. LEXIS 422 (La., Feb. 11, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's short form indictment, the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, convicted him of second degree murder in the perpetration of cruelty to a juvenile under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1(A)(2)(b) and sentenced him to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a woman lived with their almost one year old child, born with an underdeveloped eye and arms but otherwise normal, diagnosed as Adams-Oliver Syndrome, and defendant's six year old daughter. One evening, the woman left him with them for a couple hours. The next morning the baby was listless. She was treated intensively by a pediatric intensive care doctor and neurosurgeon who diagnosed her with shaken baby syndrome. She did not return to normal and died from her head injuries about four months later. The woman testified that only she and defendant had primary responsibility for the victim's care, the victim had no bad falls or accidents or bumps that indicated such, defendant would become angry with the victim and deal with her in disturbing ways, and the victim cried on seeing defendant. Others testified of defendant's violent tendencies and guilty conscience. Of 24 baby photos introduced, 17 were from before the injury. The appellate court held that the circumstantial evidence was sufficient. The 17 photos were corroborative of testimony, and, in a sense, not cumulative. The totality of a certain juror's voir dire responses showed she could be fair.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Stewart


No. 2001-KA-0976


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-0976 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/21/01); 803 So. 2d 120; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2752



November 21, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 418-029, SECTION "J". Honorable Leon Cannizzaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed. Sentence amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of the responsive verdict of attempted distribution of cocaine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence supported reversal on the grounds of entrapment. Defendant stopped the police officers, approached the vehicle asking what was needed, and did not hesitate to offer his services once he knew that the officers wanted drugs. Defendant did not prove by a preponderance of the evidence that he was induced to obtain drugs. Thus, there was no entrapment. The trial judge sentenced defendant to seven years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. As La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967 B(4)(b) read at the time of the offense, the prohibition of parole, probation, and a suspended sentence could be applied only to the first five years of the sentence. Clearly, the sentence was illegal in part. The trial court considered that defendant had been referred to a diversionary program for a 1996 arrest for possession of cocaine. Defendant had previously been arrested and had been ordered to participate in the About Face Program of Orleans Parish Prison and complete a substance abuse program. Defendant failed to prove the trial judge abused the liberal discretion allowed in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed with an amendment of the sentence.

Gardner v. Nabors Offshore Corp.

Miller v. S. Baptist Hosp.


No. 2000-CA-1352

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee patient sued a hospital in the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), for medical malpractice. Robertson v. Ieyoub


No. 34,776-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,776 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/16/01); 799 So. 2d 863; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2696



November 16, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 444263. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; motion to remand denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates sued appellee Attorney General of the State of Louisiana (AG) and others in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, seeking, among other relief, a declaration that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 413(B) was unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the AG from the suit and the inmates appealed. While the appeal was pending, the inmates filed a motion to remand.


OVERVIEW: The inmates alleged that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 413(B) was unconstitutional because it resulted in a racially discriminatory method of selection of grand jury forepersons. The AG filed an exception on the grounds that the inmates had no cause of action against the AG's office when challenging the constitutionality of a state statute. The trial court granted the exception but allowed the inmates to amend the petition. The inmates deleted the AG from the pleadings but continued to serve pleadings on the AG's office. On motion of the AG, and with the apparent agreement of the inmates, the trial court formally dismissed the AG from the action. One of the inmates, however, filed an appeal. The appellate court held that the inmates had not demonstrated any prejudice resulting from the dismissal of the AG from the action. The State remained a party to the action and remanding the case to the trial court as requested to allow the inmates to further amend their petition would not change that fact. The court would not consider the inmate's challenge to the trial court's award of costs against the inmates because the inmate had not briefed the issue.


OUTCOME: The motion to remand was denied and the order of the trial court was affirmed.

State ex rel. J. W.


No. 2001-CA-0500


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


01-0500 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/14/01); 801 So. 2d 1182; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2698



November 14, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM JUVENILE COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 00-332-08-W A, SECTION "A". Honorable Ernestine S. Gray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, terminated a mother and father's parental rights to a child because a sibling died due to abuse and neglect while in the parents' care. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that a mere finding of negligence on their part was legally insufficient to terminate their parental rights under La. Child. Code art. 1015(3). The trial judge found more than mere negligence. Hospital records showed that the sibling had bruising on her abdomen. The sibling was denied consistent and appropriate medical treatment. The mother admitted that the household was dirty and chaotic with 18 people in two bedrooms. The coroner's report showed that the immediate cause of the sibling's death was two skull fractures inconsistent with a fall. One of the fractures was depressed, indicating the use of an extreme amount of force. The trial judge was reasonable in deciding that the child would not be safe in the care of either of her parents. The trial judge bent over backwards to protect the father's right against self-incrimination. The parents failed to raise the issue in the trial court of the constitutionality of La. Child. Code art. 1015(3) because the statute did not require a showing that the child was in danger, so the issue was not considered on appeal. The clear and convincing evidence standard of proof in the statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Adams v. Parish of E. Baton Rouge


No. 2000 CA 0424, No. 2000 CA 0425, No. 2000 CA 0426, No. 2000 CA 0427


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 0424 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/14/01); 804 So. 2d 679; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2673



November 14, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied January 11, 2002. Released for Publication January 11, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Honorable Kay Bates, Judge. Trial Court Nos. 398,693, 403,380, 405,016, and 405,674.

Adams v. City of Baton Rouge, 679 So. 2d 439, 1996 La. LEXIS 2515 (La. 1996) 



DISPOSITION: Amended, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, appellee injured parties and family members sued appellant parish in the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, for damages resulting from an automobile accident. The trial court granted a judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV) for appellees and conditionally granted a new trial. The parish appealed; two family members sought an increased damages award.


OVERVIEW: Two persons were killed and two others were seriously injured in the accident, which took place in wet weather conditions on a curve on a parish road. Evidence showed that skid tests on the road three years prior to the accident reflected a very slippery condition, that the road was more slippery during wet weather, and that there had been numerous complaints concerning the road. The parish stipulated that it was feasible to improve the road prior to the accident. The appellate court found that the trial court correctly granted the JNOV with respect to the parish's liability under strict liability and negligence theories. However, the trial court erred in finding that the parish was entirely at fault, as one of the drivers was not reasonably observant of the road conditions. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in awarding damages, but a reduction of 20 percent was necessary based on reallocation of fault. The conditional grant of a new trial was proper as the jury's verdict was not supportable by any fair interpretation of the evidence. The increase in damages requested by a decedent's family members was found not to be warranted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was amended to reduce each damages award by 20 percent and the judgment was affirmed as amended.

State v. Wilson


No. 2000-KA-1736


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


00-1736 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/14/01); 803 So. 2d 102; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2712



November 14, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 18, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 397-459, SECTION "B". Honorable Patrick G. Quinlan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, sentence vacated, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of distribution of cocaine and possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. Subsequently, the trial court found defendant to be a third offender and sentenced him to life imprisonment at hard labor without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence on each count with the sentences to be served concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not have a violent history and did not appear to have significant ties to drug distributors. Defendant could have been supporting a drug addiction with the transaction; she was fairly young, and she was a mother. If defendant did receive a life sentence, any hope for her rehabilitation would vanish, and the taxpayers would have to feed, house, and clothe her for life. On the other hand, it could not be forgotten that defendant had two prior chances to prove herself capable of rehabilitation and had failed. The appellate court was unable to conclude either that defendant's mandatory life sentence was constitutional or that there was clear and convincing evidence to the contrary. Therefore, on remand, the district court had to hold a hearing at which defendant could present evidence that she was exceptional, a victim of the legislature's failure to assign sentences that were meaningfully tailored to the culpability of the offender, the gravity of the offense, and the circumstances of the case. Also, defendant did not articulate any facts that suggested that his attorney had a conflict of interest or that counsel's representation was ineffective.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, but vacated the sentence and remanded the case for re-sentencing.

La. Electorate of Gays & Lesbians, Inc. v. State


No. 99-CA-2949


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-2949 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/14/01); 806 So. 2d 678; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2937



November 14, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 94-9260, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE CAROLYN W. GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.

Louisiana Electorate of Gays & Lesbians, Inc. v. State, 726 So. 2d 897, 1998 La. LEXIS 2939 (La. 1998) 



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, gay and lesbian organization and individuals, sued appellees, the State of Louisiana, its attorney general, and state district attorneys, seeking a declaration that certain statutes were unconstitutional. The Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans, Louisiana, declared unconstitutional certain aspects of some statutes, and denied the organization's and individuals' motion for a new trial. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The organization and individuals sued the state and a class represented by the district attorney for Orleans Parish and consisting of all district attorneys throughout the State. The trial court declared certain criminal statutes unconstitutional only insofar as they prohibited non-commercial, consensual, private sexual activity by adult human beings. The court of appeals noted that, under La. Const., art. 5, § 5(D), the Louisiana Supreme Court had jurisdiction over cases in which statutes had been ruled unconstitutional. The state had duly appealed the trial court's findings of unconstitutionality to the supreme court. Therefore, under La. Const., art. 5, § 5(F), the whole appeal was before the supreme court, not just the issue which gave it appellate jurisdiction. The court of appeals therefore lacked jurisdiction over the appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.

Bernard v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr.


2000 CA 1912


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 1912 (La. 11/9/01); 835 So. 2d 470; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2641



November 9, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by Bernard v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr., 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2832 (La.App. 1 Cir., Sept. 12, 2002)
Different results reached on rehearing at Bernard v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr., 843 So. 2d 413, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4310 (La.App. 1 Cir., Sept. 20, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 471,026, Division "J". Honorable Curtis A. Calloway, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus. The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), dismissed his petition after a commissioner screened the claim and determined it lacked merit. The inmate appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found merit in the inmate's assignment of error that the trial court erred in screening his habeas corpus application under the provisions of the Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1181-90. The provisions of the PLRA did not include habeas corpus challenging the fact or duration of confinement in prison. The petition alleged the unconstitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.5, claiming that as a result of its enforcement, he was unlawfully and unconstitutionally restrained and deprived of his liberty. The trial court's judgment was rendered in accord with a recommendation by a commissioner after a judicial screening, a procedure authorized by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1178, 1188. The trial court erred in dismissing his petition for habeas corpus on the basis of a "judicial screening" recommendation by the commissioner. The matter should be handled as any other civil matter.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded the habeas corpus matter to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Rhone v. Ward


2000 CA 1774


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 1774 (La. 11/9/01); 818 So. 2d 26; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2659



November 9, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Rhone v. Ward, 902 So. 2d 1258, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1234 (La.App. 2 Cir., May 11, 2005)
Writ denied by Rhone v. Ward, 2006 La. LEXIS 2721 (La., Sept. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge State of Louisiana. Number 453,221. Honorable Jewel E. "Duke" Welch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a petition for judicial review of an administrative decision under the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure (CARP) set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1171 through 1179. The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, dismissed the petition and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate became ill after being exposed to bacteria-contaminated water through the prison water supply system. The inmate filed a CARP complaint seeking money damages and the termination of some prison employees that the inmate alleged had intentionally misled him about the condition of the water supply. The inmate's claim was denied at all administrative levels. The trial court dismissed the inmate's petition for review based on the recommendation of a commissioner who had conducted a review of the record but had not held any other proceedings. The appellate court noted that the trial court had acted prior to the decision of the Louisiana Supreme Court in Pope v. State of Louisiana, which held CARP unconstitutional as applied to inmate tort actions because the statute improperly allowed the Louisiana Department of Public Safety and Corrections to exercise original jurisdiction in tort actions in violation of La. Const. art. V, § 16(A). Under Pope, as the inmate's claim was in tort, the trial court should have exercised its original jurisdiction and conducted a trial de novo.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was reversed.

 

1658 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Sims v. Blue Cross Blue Shield


2000 CA 1904


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 1904 (La. 11/9/01); 818 So. 2d 6; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2642; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8667



November 9, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 65,851), PARISH OF ASCENSION, STATE OF LOUISIANA HONORABLE ALVIN TURNER, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee claimant appealed a decision denying her unemployment compensation to the 23rd Judicial District Court, Ascension Parish, Louisiana. The trial court ordered payment of benefits to the claimant, and appellant Louisiana Department of Labor sought review.


OVERVIEW: Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1634(A) the department was required to file, within 60 days, the administrative record in the claimant's appeal of the decision denying her unemployment compensation. This period did not begin to run until the department was served with process. The trial court entered an ex parte order requiring it to pay the claimant benefits because the administrative record was not filed. There was no evidence in the record that anyone had been served with anything, appellee employer was not given an opportunity for a hearing, and no evidence was introduced. The only benefits awardable for this reason were payable from administrative expense funds not chargeable to the employer, at least until there was a final judicial determination of the claimant's appeal. These payments were unique administrative expenses properly payable from administrative funds under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 23:1511, 23:1513. Although La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1634(A) was vague, when it was construed with its objectives and the purposes of the unemployment compensation legislation, it was not unconstitutionally so.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was reversed.

State v. Davis


No. 2001-KA-0392


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of simple burglary and sentenced him to life imprisonment as a third felony offender, and denied his motion for reconsideration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to advise him of the post-conviction relief provisions, and in imposing an excessive sentence.
