1660 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Stelly v. Ieyoub


01-0755


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-0755 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/31/01); 799 So. 2d 1206; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2467



October 31, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 6, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF EVANGELINE, NO. 61661-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sued defendant attorney general, sheriff, and other government officials and entities in the Thirteenth Judicial District, Parish of Evangeline, Louisiana, seeking damages and a declaration that former La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 413(B) was unconstitutional. The trial court granted exceptions of no cause of action and prescription and dismissed the suit as frivolous. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that the method of selecting grand jury foremen set out in former art. 413(B) was unconstitutional due to racial discrimination. The trial court granted the attorney general's exception of no cause of action on the basis that the attorney general was not an indispensable party to a challenge to the constitutionality of a statute. The appellate court agreed; the attorney general could appear in such suits on a discretionary basis, and allowing the attorney general to be named as a defendant would have removed that discretion. The appellate court also found that the sheriff's exceptions of no cause of action and prescription were properly granted. The inmate's arrest and initial incarceration in the parish in question did not give rise to a claim against the sheriff, and even if a cause of action had been alleged it would have prescribed. The trial court did not err in dismissing the suit as frivolous pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1188 because, contrary to the inmate's argument, the statute was not limited to use by a particular judicial district, nor was it limited to review of administrative rulings.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1661 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Wyatt v. Avoyelles Parish Sch. Bd.


01-531


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-531 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/31/01); 799 So. 2d 1197; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2476



October 31, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWELFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF AVOYELLES, NO. 98-5739, THE HONORABLE WILLIAM J. BENNETT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee employees sued appellant school district in the 12th Judicial District Court, Avoyelles Parish (Louisiana), for compensation for unused annual leave upon retirement. The trial court entered judgment for the employees, and the school district appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the school district adopted a policy of compensating employees for unused annual leave, it was advised this was unconstitutional and adopted a "use or lose" policy which was never committed to writing. In the absence of a clear, written policy that vacation time was nothing more than a gratuity not to be considered an amount due or wage, the employees' accrued but unused vacation time was a vested right for which they were to be compensated upon discharge or resignation. Prescription did not begin to run until each employee retired, as a claim for unused annual leave would not have been viable prior to that time, so their claims did not prescribe. Awards were properly based on the employees' salaries at the time of retirement. One employee should have been given credit for unused annual leave days the school district admitted he was entitled to. The school district could not rely on an unlawful oral or written policy to deny the employees' claims, so it was liable for statutory penalties.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed, except that one employee was found entitled to credit for additional unused annual leave which the school district admitted he was entitled to. Another employee was awarded appellate attorney fees.

 

1662 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pierce


01-94


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-94 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/31/01); 799 So. 2d 732; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2463



October 31, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 6, 2001.
Writ denied by State v. Pierce, 834 So. 2d 427, 2003 La. LEXIS 38 (La., Jan. 10, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EVANGELINE, NO. 55,327, THE HONORABLE PRESTON N. AUCOIN, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Pierce, 2000 La. App. LEXIS 161 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 2, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and sentence vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving while intoxicated (DWI), third offense, two manslaughter counts, and one count of first degree vehicular negligent injuring. After several motions to recuse, one vacated sentence, and a hearing on a post-verdict judgment of acquittal, the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to multiple consecutive sentences. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving under the influence when he ran over three boys. Defendant fled the scene and was taken into custody some eight hours later. Defendant appealed arguing that the trial court erred by 1) not forcing the judge to recuse himself; 2) admitting into evidence his first DWI conviction because he was not advised of his right to remain silent at the prior proceeding and he was not asked whether he read and understood the guilty plea form; 3) allowing the admission of the blood alcohol test results because they had no probative value and were too remote because the test was administered approximately eight hours after the accident occurred; 4) exposing him to double jeopardy because he was charged with manslaughter based upon a felony DWI that had already been enhanced. The court of appeal found that 1) the judge was not biased; 2) counsel's vague reference to the transcript was not enough to shift the burden of proof back to the State under Boykin; 3) the state relied upon independent evidence to show intoxication and therefore was not required to introduce evidence regarding the blood-alcohol machine or test; and 4) the trial court did subject him to double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for DWI, third offense, was reversed and that sentence vacated. The remaining convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

1663 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Neal


No. 34,814-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,814 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/12/01); 795 So. 2d 1292; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2175



October 12, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 198597. Honorable Ramona L. Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND THIRD FELONY OFFENDER ADJUDICATION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RE-SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, convicted defendant of vehicular homicide and sentenced him as a third felony habitual offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that a guilty plea, resulting in a prior possession of cocaine conviction, should not have been used to enhance his sentence because the State failed to introduce the transcript of the guilty plea. The appeals court disagreed, finding that the State, through the use of the minute entry, met its burden of proof by showing that the defendant was represented by counsel at the time of the plea. Once the State did this, the burden shifted to the defendant to produce some affirmative evidence showing an infringement of his rights or a procedural irregularity, which the defendant did not do. But, the court agreed with defendant that the sentence imposed was constitutionally excessive. No evidence was taken, and the trial court failed to address any of the issues raised by the defendant or to provide any of the factors it used in reaching its decision to deny the defendant's motion for deviation from a third offender sentence. The Louisiana Supreme Court required more than a general conclusion, and because the trial court provided only a general ruling, and did not address the constitutionality of the sentence, remand was necessary.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and third felony offender adjudication were affirmed. However, the sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for re-sentencing.

 

1664 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Lay v. Scott


No. 1998 CA 2615


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


1998 2615 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/04/01); 809 So. 2d 440; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2125



October 4, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 434,804. Honorable Robert D. Downing, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court of appeal stayed defendant inmate's appeal from a judgment in forma pauperis from the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1186(F). The court then lifted the stay and ordered the inmate, ex proprio motu, to show cause why this appeal should not be dismissed pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1187.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeal ordered the inmate to show cause in light of three judgments which dismissed as frivolous civil actions brought by the inmate in forma pauperis. The court noted that under La. Rev. Stat. § 15:1187, no prisoner could bring a civil action or appeal from a civil action or proceeding in forma pauperis if the prisoner had on three or more occasions brought an action that was dismissed on the grounds that it was frivolous, malicious, or failed to state a cause of action or claim upon which relief could be granted. In response to the court's order, the inmate contended that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1186 and 1187 were unconstitutional. He further argued that the judgments dismissing his three prior suits were null due to application of an unconstitutional standard of review to his federal causes of action. The court held that the constitutionality of the statutes must first have been questioned in the trial court, not the appellate courts, and the unconstitutionality must have been specially pleaded and the grounds for the claim particularized. The inmate had not brought a declaratory action in the district court challenging the constitutionality of the statutes.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1665 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Graves


01-0156


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-0156 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/03/01); 798 So. 2d 1090; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2113



October 3, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT PARISH OF ALLEN, NO. CR-99-3772. HONORABLE JOEL GERARD DAVIS. GLENN B. GREMILLION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Thirty-Third Judicial District Parish of Allen, Louisiana convicted defendant of possession with intent to distribute marijuana and possession with intent to distribute cocaine, and sentenced him to prison. He appealed from his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: After the State rested, but before defendant commenced his case, he complained of chest pains. The trial court sent him to a hospital, and continued the trial to the next day. Defendant failed to appear, but the trial continued in his absence. His attorney submitted no evidence other than a proffer of a taped conversation between defendant and a co-defendant. Defendant sought a mistrial on grounds that his absence was due to his medical condition; the trial court refused to grant either a mistrial or a new trial. The appellate court found no error. The trial court found, based on conversations with hospital personnel, that defendant did not have a serious medical condition. The burden then shifted to defendant to show that his medical condition prevented him from appearing. His generic doctor's note, asking that he be excused from work or school, was insufficient. Moreover, defendant told counsel to proceed without him. Defendant was not entitled to a review of his sentence for excessiveness, as he failed to make timely oral or written motions. Because he had been convicted of four felonies and numerous misdemeanors, his sentence was not excessive as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1666 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Twin B. Casinos, Inc. v. State ex rel. La. Gaming Control Bd.


2000 CA 1681


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 1681 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/28/01); 809 So. 2d 995; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2054



September 28, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. State of Louisiana. Number 468,838. Honorable Jewel E. "Duke" Welch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business owner's application for a video gaming license was granted by a hearing officer and then denied by appellee gaming control board, and he appealed to the 19th Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, which affirmed the denial. He sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The owner was charged with terrorizing over 10 years before his application. Public record of the charge was expunged under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:9. His application asked if he was ever charged with a criminal offense, regardless of the final outcome, and he said he was not. The application asked if he ever had a criminal record expunged under § 44:9, and he said he had not. An investigation showed the charge. If the owner had been convicted of certain crimes within the previous 10 years, he would have been automatically disqualified, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 27:310(A). In considering his suitability for a gaming license, the owner's entire criminal history was relevant under § 27:310(B)(2), as was his lack of candor in completing the application. A preponderance of the evidence supported the denial of the owner's application. The state had a legitimate interest in regulating the gaming industry, and its licensing scheme clearly and rationally promoted that interest, so it was not unconstitutional, nor was the owner deprived of due process, since he had no protectable property interest in obtaining a license.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1667 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Felder


2000 KA 2887


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 2887 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/28/01); 809 So. 2d 360; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2080



September 28, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 21st Judicial District Court Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana. Honorable Douglas Hughes, Judge Presiding. Docket No. 90067 D.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 21st Judicial District Court Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana, refused to allow defendant to introduce to the jury evidence of the victim's dangerous reputation, by jury convicted him of second degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1, denied his post-verdict motions, and sentenced him to life in prison at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension or sentence. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim's friend was in prison for the murder of defendant's brother. One day the victim got in a conversation with defendant's other brother. Witnesses got the impression that someone was "fixing to get killed." They saw nothing resembling a weapon in the victim's hands, nor aggressive moves on his part. They saw defendant, off to the side with a gun, shoot the victim, then get over him continuing shooting. No gun was found on the victim. Defendant admitted the shooting claiming that the victim had been reaching for a weapon and that the victim had a reputation for pulling guns on people. After denying defendant's post-verdict motions, the trial court asked his counsel if he was aware of any applicable delays which would prevent sentencing, was told no, and sentenced defendant. The appellate court held that his self-serving, uncorroborated, and contradicted testimony did not constitute appreciable evidence tending to establish a La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 404 "overt act" by the victim to permit admission of the reputation evidence. As the sentence had been mandatory, the trial court's failure to delay sentencing 24 hours per La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 873 was harmless.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed. The trial court was directed to give defendant written notice of the prescriptive period for applying for post-conviction relief within 10 days of rendition of this opinion and to file written proof in the district court record of the proceedings that defendant has received the notice.

 

1668 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr.


2000 CA 1468


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 1468 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/28/01); 809 So. 2d 398; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2087



September 28, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 20th Judicial District Court. Parish of West Feliciana, Louisiana. Docket No. 16,550, Division "B". Honorable Wilson R. Ramshur, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sued appellees, warden, department of public safety, and contractor for personal injury. The 20th Judicial District Court, Parish of West Feliciana, Louisiana, granted a change of venue to the 19th Judicial District Court. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was injured when an object fell off a roof that was being repaired by the contractor at the prison where the inmate was confined. The trial court held that a change of venue as requested by the warden, the department, and the contractor was required by the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1177, which provided that an inmate aggrieved by a decision rendered pursuant to an administrative remedy procedure could seek review of the decision only in the 19th Judicial District. Subsequent to the trial court's order the statute had however been declared unconstitutional as it related to tort actions. As there was no other basis to change venue in the action, the appellate court therefore held that the trial court had erred in ordering the change of venue.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed in part, vacated in part, and the action was remanded to the trial court.

 

1669 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baker


No. 34,973-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,973 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/26/01); 796 So. 2d 145; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2010



September 26, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Richland, Louisiana. Trial Court No. F99-110. Honorable Glen W. Strong, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Richland (Louisiana) of kidnapping and attempted forcible rape. Defendants were sentenced to concurrent sentences of five years at hard labor for kidnapping and two and one-half years at hard labor for attempted forcible rape. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the victim left a store, defendants forced her into her van, drove to a secluded area expressing an intent to have sex with her, and began sexually molesting her. When a car appeared, they fled. The victim testified as to what happened, store clerks testified defendants placed the victim in her van and left, and the State presented the victim's damaged watch and jewelry. The appellate court found (1) the evidence was sufficient to support defendants' kidnapping conviction; (2) the evidence was sufficient to show defendants had the specific intent to forcibly rape the victim and did an act in furtherance of that purpose; (3) race-neutral reasons existed for the peremptory challenges exercised by the State against African-American jurors; (4) even if the trial court erred in denying defendants' request for the victim's rap sheet, defendants were not prejudiced by the error; (5) the jury was sufficiently informed of its duty to acquit defendants if the evidence warranted only a finding of either sexual battery or criminal mischief; (6) defendants did not file their postconviction proceedings within the proper time; and (7) the sentences were not unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

1670 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hansbro


No. 35,027-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


35,027 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/26/01); 796 So. 2d 185; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2033



September 26, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied State v. Hansbro, 827 So. 2d 1177, 2002 La. LEXIS 3077 (La., Oct. 25, 2002)
Writ denied by State v. Hansbro, 885 So. 2d 582, 2004 La. LEXIS 3207 (La., Oct. 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 199,070. Honorable Leon L. Emanuel, III, Judge.
State v. Hansbro, 758 So. 2d 156, 2000 La. LEXIS 884 (La., Mar. 24, 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted on a jury verdict of second degree murder by the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, and was sentenced to life imprisonment without parole. He appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: After a man was found beaten to death, defendant was arrested for public intoxication. He admitted being at the scene of the homicide; though he accused his companion of the crime, his shoeprints were matched to marks on the victim's face and neck, and the victim's blood was on his jeans. The appellate court held that the evidence, including the companion's testimony that defendant was the killer, was sufficient to prove that defendant was the perpetrator, and that he had the intent to kill or cause great bodily harm. The motion to suppers was properly denied. There was probable cause to arrest defendant for public intoxication; his request not to be questioned, was honored, and his statements were not coerced. The fact that no one testified to taking defendant's jeans from him did not preclude admissibility, as defendant did not deny the jeans were his, and a defect in the chain of custody went to the weight of the evidence, not its admissibility. As a life sentence was mandatory, the trial court was not obliged to consider the factors set forth in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1. A life sentence for a brutal murder of a helpless man did not shock the sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1671 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. 34,902-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,902 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/26/01); 796 So. 2d 201; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2038



September 26, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 201,960. Honorable Charles R. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, convicted defendant on a jury verdict of possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: A deputy testified he saw defendant throw a baggie as police chased him. A forensic chemist testified that the baggie contained 22 grams of crack cocaine. An officer testified that one who bought crack for personal use would buy no more than one gram. The appellate court held that the evidence was sufficient to convict. Testimony that defendant threw the baggie up to 42 feet was not inherently improbable. Defendant's intent to distribute was proved by the large amount of drugs he possessed, and his statement to police that he could get "other dealers" if he was not charged. The trial court properly excluded an experiment by defendant's expert, as there was no foundation laid to show the experiment replicated the conditions of the baggie toss at the time of defendant's arrest. The jurors' handling and tossing the baggie did not amount to scientific experimentation so beyond their normal understanding as to establish that they were prejudiced by considering evidence adduced outside of the trial. Defendant did not show that the sentence imposed under the Habitual Offender Law was a purposeless infliction of suffering, and the sentence was not shocking to the sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1672 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCraney


NUMBER 01-KA-439


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-439 (La.App. 5 Cir. 09/25/01); 798 So. 2d 227; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2015



September 25, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 16, 2001.
Post-conviction proceeding at State ex rel. McCraney v. State, 2011 La. LEXIS 2138 (La., Sept. 23, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NUMBER 00-5709, DIVISION "J", HONORABLE STEPHEN J. WINDHORST, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was sentenced in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, for distribution of cocaine in a drug free zone. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Three agents were conducting an undercover narcotics operation. One of the agents approached defendant and asked for a "20." Defendant went to a car, returned with a package, and the agent paid him $ 20. The transaction took place within 1,000 feet of a school playground. The two rock-like substances contained in the package tested positive for cocaine. Considering the gravity of the offense and the defendant's extensive prior criminal history, the sentence of 22 years of imprisonment was neither excessive nor an abuse of the trial court's discretion. The sentence was actually illegally lenient. The prosecution, however, neither objected to the sentence at trial nor appealed on the issue, and the appellate court would not correct the illegally lenient sentence imposed. Defendant had stated that he was ready for sentencing. This response constituted a waiver in delay of sentencing. No error resulted from the trial court's immediate imposition of the sentence. The trial court did err, however, in not informing the defendant of the final prescriptive period for filing post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment, but the matter was remanded so that the trial court could inform defendant of the post-conviction relief prescriptive period.

 

1673 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Langlois v. E. Baton Rouge Parish Sch. Bd.


2001 CW 1227


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 1227 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/24/01); 809 So. 2d 274; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1990



September 24, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Supervisory Writs from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court. Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 442,379. Honorable Janice Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school board sought supervisory writs from an order of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, denying its exception of insufficiency of service of process pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5107(D).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff parent, in her own right and on behalf of her minor child, sued the school board for damages arising out of a vehicular accident. Parent requested that service be withheld and the school board, upon its non-receipt of service, filed an exception of insufficiency of service, which the trial court denied. Upon rehearing, the school board was again denied relief. Upon the writ request, the court of appeals agreed that service upon the school board was required within the 90 days stated in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5107(D), and parent failed to effectuate the same. Further, the court rejected the parent's argument that service was not necessary, because the school board had knowledge of the suit. Actual knowledge of a legal action could not obviate the need for proper citation to issue. Further, the court pretermitted the issue of whether parent was entitled to demonstrate good cause for the failure to timely request service.


OUTCOME: The writ was granted, reversing the trial court's judgment overruling the exception, and judgment was rendered in favor of the school board. Further, the matter was remanded to the trial court for it to consider the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5107(D).

 

1674 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Homes


No. 2000-KA-2121


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-2121 (La. App. 4 Cir. 10/17/01); 799 So. 2d 549; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2224



September 19, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Release for Publication November 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 413-410, SECTION "J", HONORABLE LEON CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, No. 413-410, Louisiana, convicted both defendants, one male, one female, of possession of cocaine and denied requests to reconsider their sentences. Both defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants contended on appeal that they received ineffective assistance of counsel, while only the male defendant contended that his sentence was excessive. The appeals court disagreed as to both contentions. Sentencing the male defendant to pay fines, although he was indigent, was not improper, as he would not have been subject to incarceration for failure to pay. On the ineffectiveness claim, the court reasoned that a motion to suppress would have been futile. The arresting office turned his car and the defendants saw him. Although he shined his lights on them, there was no indication there was a stop. The officer was alone, there were no weapons, and the defendants were not surrounded. The male defendant dropped the crack pipe and therefore abandoned it. At that point, the officer stopped the defendants and, seeing the other defendant concealing something in her purse, took it from her for his protection. Once the officer found the crack pipe, he had probable cause for arrest at that point. He found the second pipe in a search of the purse incident to the other defendant's arrest. Thus there was no authority to support suppression of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment as to both defendants was affirmed.

 

1675 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Finney


No. 2000-KA-2761


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


00-2761 (La. App. 4 Cir. 09/05/01); 798 So. 2d 1051; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2372



September 5, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 25, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM Criminal District Court Orleans Parish. NO. 412-235, Section "F". Honorable Dennis J. Waldron, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, of possession of cocaine and simple battery on a police officer and was sentenced to life in prison as a fourth time offender under the Habitual Offender Law. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two police officers, who had arrested defendant a month earlier on other drug charges, saw defendant engaging in what the officers believed was a narcotics transaction in which defendant had a white spherical object about the size of a tennis ball. Defendant attempted to flee to his nearby house. The officers pursued defendant into a bathroom where they caught defendant trying to flush crack cocaine down the toilet. Defendant struggled with the officers and one of the officers received a broken hand, although the officer could not say when the injury occurred. The appellate court held that defendant's actions, coupled with the officer's knowledge of defendant and the area, gave the officer's probable cause to arrest and the officers could properly pursue defendant into the house. The trial court had therefore properly denied defendant's motion to suppress. While a trial court could depart from a mandatory minimum sentence imposed under the Habitual Offender Law if the sentence would have been excessive, such a departure would not have been appropriate in defendant's case given defendant's record and the facts of the case.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1676 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. Baldwin


No. 2000-CA-0802


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-0802 (La. App. 4 Cir. 08/29/01); 801 So. 2d 485; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2415



August 29, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied October 3, 2001. Released for Publication October 3, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 92-7042, DIVISION "J". Honorable Nadine M. Ramsey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgement in favor of plaintiff for malicious prosecution and intentional infliction of emotion distress, was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The City of New Orleans appealed a judgment from the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, in favor of the plaintiff and against the city for damages for malicious prosecution, as well as intentional infliction of emotional distress, based on the claim that plaintiff was improperly convicted of murder and was improperly incarcerated for 30 years.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiff contended at trial that 1) the criminal trial transcript was inadmissible because no predicate was laid; and 2) the City was liable for malicious prosecution because police investigators did not give him information about a witness who could have given him a self-defense claim. The court of appeal held that 1) the criminal trial transcript was relevant to determine if there was malicious prosecution and if any failure to disclose evidence was the City or State's fault; 2) the transcript was not being used to show the truth of the matter but to explain the surrounding circumstances to determine if there was sufficient evidence concerning the self-defense claim, whether the missing witness's testimony was cumulative, whether there was a finding of error in the witness's testimony's omission, and if any error should have been imputed to the City; and 3) there was no showing that the police's failure to get the witness's data or a "court clerk's" sending the witness home from the trial was done intentionally to suppress evidence or ruin plaintiff's defense. The trial court's determination that the City was liable for malicious prosecution was clearly wrong.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal reversed the civil trial court's judgment against the City.

 

1677 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


City of Shreveport v. Chanse Gas Corp.


No. 34,958-CA consolidated with No. 34,959-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,958 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/22/01); 794 So. 2d 962; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1911



August 22, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 446,984. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed two suits to expropriate three tracts of land belonging to defendant property owners. The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, approved the expropriation, finding a valid public purpose and legitimate public interest. A jury unanimously fixed the market value of the property and awarded moving and other expenses to the property owners, plus attorney fees. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: City leaders had advocated the need for a new, larger convention center. The city hired a large accounting and management firm to conduct a convention center study. The report recommended building a new, state-of-the-art convention center. The report also suggested that the city foster the development of a convention headquarters hotel. On appeal, the property owners urged that the trial court erred in allowing the city to expropriate their property for the building of the hotel. Given the constitutional authority and the home rule charter, the appellate court found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 19:102 specifically conferred that power. Special legislative authority was not needed for the city to expropriate land. Moreover, the record did not support the property owner's contention that the city would donate expropriated land to any hotel developer. The city argued it should not have to pay the losing party's legal fees. The appellate court could not say the trial court abused its great discretion in denying certain items, such as preparation for a mock trial, as costs. Expert witness fees were also not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1678 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Bank of N.Y. v. Williams


No. 2000-CA-1922


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


00-1922 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/22/01); 796 So. 2d 69; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2368



August 22, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 11, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 99-3010, DIVISION "L-15". Honorable Max N. Tobias, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; MATTER REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, granted summary judgment for appellee current trustee in dispute to determine whether the trustee was obligated to make payments in lieu of taxes previously owed by a hotel prior to its default under certain agreements. Appellant assessor, appellant city, and appellant Industrial Development Board of the City of New Orleans, Louisiana, challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The board and the hotel ratified a lease agreement, under which the hotel was to erect and operate the hotel until January 1, 2003. Because the board was organized pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:1151 et seq., the property it acquired was exempt from ad valorem taxes. The parties specified that although no property taxes were due on the property, the hotel would make annual payments to the city in an amount determined by the assessor. The hotel, subsequently, went into bankruptcy. The issue was whether the current trustee for the bondholders who financed the transaction was obligated to make payments in lieu of taxes previously owed by the hotel prior to its default. The trial court did not err in granting the trustee's motion for summary judgment; nullifying the prior assessments, liens, and adjudications; and prohibiting future tax assessments and/or tax enforcement against the property at issue. Any factual issues were resolved by reference to the 1983 contracts. No factual issue existed concerning the hotel's bankruptcy action. As long as the property at issue was owned by the board, which was established as a public body, it was exempt from taxation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the matter was remanded.

 

1679 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Vieux Carre Prop. Owners, Residents & Assocs. v. City of New Orleans


No. 2001-CA-0658


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-0658 (La. App. 4 Cir. 8/16/01); 797 So. 2d 103; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2724



August 16, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 3, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2000-13284, DIVISION "F-10". Honorable Yada Magee, Judge.

Vieux Carre Prop. Owners v. City of New Orleans, 788 So. 2d 433, 2001 La. LEXIS 1043 (La. 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sued appellee city council in the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, challenging the enactment of two zoning ordinances. The trial court dismissed the lawsuit, holding it was prescribed or preempted. The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city council enacted two zoning ordinances and the citizens filed a petition challenging their enactment 25 days later. The trial court dismissed the petition as untimely. The citizens appealed, arguing the 15-day period to file suit under New Orleans, La., Comprehensive Zoning Ordinance § 16.9.9.5, did not begin to run until the two ordinances were signed as approved by the mayor, returned by the mayor to the clerk of council, and entered into the record of the clerk of council. Alternatively, the citizens asserted the ordinances were unconstitutional and that prescription did not run as to a challenge to an unconstitutional ordinance. The appellate court initially noted the plain text of New Orleans, La., Comprehensive Zoning Ordinance § 16.9.9.5, required that a lawsuit be filed within 15 days of the final action of the city council. The appellate court held the citizens' action was prescribed or preempted because it was untimely filed. The appellate court concluded the citizens' remaining argument was not preserved for review because it was not raised in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1680 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


In re Trestman


No. 2000-KA-1367, COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


00-1367 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/01/01); 795 So. 2d 398; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1853



August 1, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published September 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: IN RE: ISRAEL TRESTMAN APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. D-30584-89, SECTION "C". Honorable Sharon K. Hunter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, entered judgment against appellant City, finding La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:3(F) constitutional and allowing appellee family members access to government death records. From that order, this appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: The City of New Orleans challenged the district court's ruling, declaring La. Rev. Stat. § 44:3(F) constitutional and allowing victim's family members to access records relevant to the investigation of the death of the victim, due to the passage of ten years after the crime. The City argued that the order jeopardized their ability to prosecute the death, that passage of the statute did not make it constitutional, and the statute violated the prohibition against the passage of local or special laws. The court of appeals disagreed, reasoning that allowing the family access to records was a statewide concern and affected all citizens and every bereaved family that was in this unfortunate position. Thus, it was not special legislation. Further, there was no merit to the City's argument that there was no reasonable basis for the creation of this statute since every Louisiana citizen who was the victim of crime would not be able to enjoy the fruits of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Flagg


No. 01-KA-65


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-65 (La.App. 5 Cir. 07/30/01); 792 So. 2d 133; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1808



July 30, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 10, 2001.
Writ denied by State v. Flagg, 825 So. 2d 1159, 2002 La. LEXIS 2729 (La., Sept. 20, 2002)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Flagg v. Cain, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 35237 (E.D. La., Apr. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, NO.99-6979, DIVISION "J", HONORABLE M. JOSEPH TIEMANN, JUDGE.
State v. Flagg, 798 So. 2d 339, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1925 (La.App. 5 Cir., July 30, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, convicted defendant of possession of heroin and cocaine. The trial court denied his motion for new trial and sentenced him, as a fourth felony offender, to life imprisonment without benefit of parole. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Based on a tip, some police corroboration of the tip, prior suspicion that the drugs were sold at the residence, and the location of the encounter in a high drug trafficking area, the appellate court found that the police had reasonable suspicion to justify an investigatory stop. Having found that the initial stop of the car was justified, the appellate court found that the seizure of the narcotics was proper pursuant to the plain view exception to the warrant requirement. Also, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence used to convict him. The drugs were on the floorboard of the front seat within arm's reach of defendant and thus, he had easy and immediate access to them. Also, the car belonged to defendant's brother. Thus, a rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was in possession of the narcotics and that he knowingly possessed them. Furthermore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for new trial. Finally, defendant's life sentence was mandated under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(ii), and was not excessive or unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. White


No. 01-KA-134


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-134 (La.App. 5 Cir. 07/30/01); 792 So. 2d 146; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1809



July 30, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 10, 2001.
Writ denied by State v. White, 824 So. 2d 1190, 2002 La. LEXIS 2621 (La., Sept. 13, 2002)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at White v. Cain, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 98407 (E.D. La., Sept. 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-0498, DIVISION "D". HONORABLE KIRK R. GRANIER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of armed robbery. The Twenty-Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles, Louisiana, sentenced him to nearly 50 years in prison without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbing a bank. He filed a motion for post verdict judgment of acquittal and a motion for a new trial. The motion for a new trial was grounded upon a Batson claim. Both post trial motions were denied. On appeal, defendant, a black male, contended the facts established a pattern of discrimination by the State in its exercise of peremptory challenges against black individuals in the selection of the petit jury. Specifically, he contended the trial court erred in finding the State presented race-neutral reasons for the exercise of its challenges. The appeals court ruled that the trial court correctly denied defendant's Batson challenge, as the State gave race-neutral reasons for each of defendant's challenges. None of the reasons for exclusion expressed by the prosecutor indicated a discriminatory intent, rather they were directed at effective trial strategy. Further, the trial court's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive, as the record revealed that the trial judge clearly particularized the sentence to the offender and the offense.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1683 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miller


No. 2000-KA-0218


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-0218 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/25/01); 792 So. 2d 104; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1841



July 25, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 12, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 402-084, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED, MOUTON'S ADJUDICATION AS AN HABITUAL OFFENDER AFFIRMED AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED, AND MILLER'S SENTENCE AFFIRMED AND CASE REMANDED FOR SENTENCING ON CONVICTION FOR POSSESSION WITH INTENT TO DISTRIBUTE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both defendants were charged in a two-count bill of information in count one with distribution of marijuana. Only one was charged in count two with possession of marijuana with intent to distribute. On 14 December 1998, a motion to suppress evidence was denied as to both appellants. The Criminal District Court Orleans Parish, Section G (Louisiana), convicted them and sentenced them to 25-year terms. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that one defendant offered to get undercover officers, whom he thought were tourists, "whatever they needed," girls or drugs; that the officers gave him a marked $ 20 bill for weed; that he in turn gave it to the other defendant; and that the other defendant gave the officers marijuana. Defendants were arrested. More marijuana was found in the first defendant's shoes. They were convicted. The appellate court held that HIV status was not a legislatively recognized mitigator. Thus the first defendant's sentence was not excessive, nor his counsel ineffective. As the second defendant pled guilty to the multiple bill, he could not appeal as to whether there was sufficient evidence at the multiple offender hearing. As each defendant testified that he did not know or speak to the other on the night of the offense, and although the jury found neither credible, the record indicated no actual conflict by their joint counsel. The evidence showed sufficient intent by the second defendant. The first defendant wrongly was convicted on two counts but sentenced on only one.


OUTCOME: The convictions and the one-count defendant's habitual offender adjudication were affirmed. The two-count defendant's sentence was affirmed and the case remanded for sentencing on possession with intent to distribute due to the trial court's apparently inadvertent vacating of the sentence imposed on that count.

State v. Payne


No. 2000-KA-2129


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-2129 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/25/01); 794 So. 2d 79; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1843



July 25, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 12, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 413-121, SECTION "K". Honorable Arthur Hunter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of two counts of aggravated assault and two counts of armed robbery. He was sentenced to serve 10 years at hard labor on each count of armed robbery and 5 years at hard labor on each count of aggravated assault. All sentences were to be served concurrently. Defendant's motion to reconsider sentence was denied and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court found the victims' testimony that defendant approached them with a gun and told them to give him their money, both men gave the defendant their money as requested, defendant then fled the scene, one of the victim's chased defendant until he fired at him, and that both victims identified defendant as the person who robbed them, was sufficient to prove defendant committed armed robbery. Also, the officers' testimony was sufficient to prove that defendant committed aggravated assaults upon the police officers when they testified that defendant pulled a gun and attempted to fire on them. Further, the trial court's sentences of five years at hard labor on each conviction of aggravated assault were not unconstitutionally excessive sentences where defendant had a prior conviction for possession of stolen property and where he committed the aggravated assaults on the police officers in his attempt to escape apprehension for two armed robberies. The trial court did not err when it denied defendant's motion in arrest of judgment because it was not timely filed and he did not assert proper grounds in support of the motion.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

State v. Washington


No. 2000-KA-1055


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1055 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/18/01); 793 So. 2d 376; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1799



July 18, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 14, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 403-341, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, denied defendant juvenile's motion to suppress, convicted him of armed robbery, sentenced him to 30 years at hard labor and 6 months for contempt to run consecutively to his 30 year sentence, and denied his motion to reconsider the sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prosecutor had the right under La. Child. Code art. 305(B) to transfer defendant juvenile to the district court. Defendant cited no authority and presented no argument as to why his rights were violated by the application of La. Child. Code art. 305. Also, defendant failed to prove that the identification procedure was suggestive; thus, the trial court properly denied the motion to suppress the identification. Defendant pointed the gun at the victim's six-month-old son to coerce him into complying with his demands, struck the victim in the head and stomach with his gun, put the gun in his mouth, asked him if he wanted to die, and then demanded money and the victim's laptop computer. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of armed robbery. Also, based on those facts, defendant's sentence was not excessive and did not shock the sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Taylor


No. 34,823-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,823 (La.App. 2 Cir. 07/11/01); 793 So. 2d 367; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1763



July 11, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 192,736. Honorable Leon L. Emanuel, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, convicted defendant of manslaughter and sentenced him to serve 26 years at hard labor, with 20 years to be served without benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court found that the trial court applied the mandatory sentence for firearms use under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893.3 and that the article was not in effect at the time the crime was committed. Therefore, the trial court was in error in applying a minimum 20-year without benefit sentence for defendant's crime, which occurred before the 20-year minimum sentence was added to the statute. The trial court's application of the article was an unconstitutional ex post facto application of the law.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed but the case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

State v. Camese


2000-KA-1943


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1943 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/23/01); 791 So. 2d 173; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1795



July 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 386-211, SECTION "D". Honorable Frank A. Marullo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and attempted second degree murder in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana. From those convictions and sentences, he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his convictions and sentences, contending that the trial court: (1) assessed an excessive sentence and (2) erred in denying his motion to suppress, and also (3) that the evidence was insufficient to warrant conviction. The appeals court disagreed. The trial court was within its discretion in assessing harsh consecutive sentences, despite failing to fully articulate the factors it considered. Due to severity of the crime and defendant's criminal and arrest record, the assignment of error was without merit. The denial of a suppression order was also not error, as defendant failed to make a threshold showing that the identification procedure was suggestive. Further, the victim not only knew the defendant by face but by name. Defendant's act of shooting the victim at close range so that he could steal his car, and again shooting the victim after he had stolen the car, was evidence that substantiated the convictions.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Richardson


No. 01-KA-239


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-239 (La.App. 5 Cir. 06/27/01); 790 So. 2d 717; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1711



June 27, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 24, 2001.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had been convicted of aggravated battery in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana. The trial court imposed the maximum allowable prison term of 10 years. Defendant's conviction was affirmed on appeal but the case was remanded for sentencing due to a technical error. The trial court again imposed a 10 year sentence and defendant appealed the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the imposition of the maximum allowable prison term for the offense of which he was convicted was excessive. The appellate court therefore limited its review to whether the sentence was constitutionally excessive. Defendant had entered the home of his ex-girlfriend to check on the couple's child and got into a fight with the girlfriend's live-in companion, who thought defendant was going to attack him in bed. The victim got a knife but defendant took the knife and stabbed the victim several times as the victim tried to flee. The victim was so badly injured that he missed several months of work. The appellate court held that the sentence was not constitutionally excessive, and given the facts of the case the trial court had not abused its discretion in imposing the maximum allowable prison term.

In re New Orleans Train Car Leakage Fire Litig.


No. 2000-CA-0479


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-0479 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/27/01); 795 So. 2d 364; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1731



June 27, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by In re New Orleans Train Car Leakage Fire Litig., 794 So. 2d 956, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1858 (La.App. 4 Cir., Aug. 1, 2001)
Rehearing denied by In re New Orleans Train Car Leakage Fire Litig., 794 So. 2d 955, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1860 (La.App. 4 Cir., Aug. 1, 2001)
Rehearing denied by In re New Orleans Train Car Leakage Fire Litig., 794 So. 2d 954, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1861 (La.App. 4 Cir., Aug. 1, 2001)
Writ denied by In re New Orleans Car Leakage Fire Litig., 827 So. 2d 411, 2002 La. LEXIS 2992 (La., Oct. 14, 2002)
Writ denied by In re New Orleans Car Leakage Fire Litig., 827 So. 2d 411, 2002 La. LEXIS 2991 (La., Oct. 14, 2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Nova Chems. Inc. v. Adams, 538 U.S. 944, 123 S. Ct. 1623, 155 L. Ed. 2d 484, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 2519 (2003)
Decision reached on appeal by Adams v. CSX R.R., 902 So. 2d 413, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1320 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 20, 2005)
Appeal after remand at In re New Orleans Train Car Leakage Litig., 903 So. 2d 9, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1318 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 87-16374, DIVISION "AD HOC - B". HONORABLE WALLACE A. EDWARDS, JUDGE AD HOC.
In re New Orleans Train Car Leakage Fire Litig., 773 So. 2d 147, 2000 La. LEXIS 3062 (La., Nov. 3, 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Unlike six other companies, three defendants, buyer, tank manufacturer, and transporter, did not settle with plaintiffs, residents, in their class actions over a railroad tank car chemical leak and fire. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Division "Ad Hoc-B" (Louisiana), by jury, found the three liable for 5, 5, and 15 percent, respectively, of the compensatory damages, and transporter liable for $ 850 million punitives. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: Buyer bought a flammable volatile carcinogenic heavier-than-air and easy-to-smell gas, arranged for its transport, but sent no one to inspect the loading. Transporter was notified that the pressurized railroad tank car was parked on its interchange tracks, which were in a residential area. Over six hours passed without inspection. The gas leaked; spread and reached an ignition source, possibly a home's hot water heater; ignited; and flashed back to ignite the car. The neighborhood was evacuated. The fire burned for two days, depositing soot in the area. Five other such cars coupled to the burning one were successfully moved away. Fortunately the car neither exploded nor launched itself. Residents sued. The appellate court held that the jury could have found that by not making inspection, transporter acted in wanton disregard of public safety under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.3. The leak was foreseeable. The fact that the quantum of punitives were determined when the quantum of compensatory damages had been determined as to only 20 of 8,047 plaintiff class members did not violate due process. Manufacturer had duty to warn about gasket.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case remanded for proceedings as to the quantum of compensatory damages with respect to the remaining class members.

State v. Marino


No. 2000-KA-1131


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1131 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/27/01); 804 So. 2d 47; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1754



June 27, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 18, 2002.
Writ of error denied State v. Marino, 823 So. 2d 936, 2002 La. LEXIS 2494 (La., Aug. 30, 2002)
Writ of error denied State ex rel. Marino v. State, 2003 La. LEXIS 761 (La., Mar. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 392-252, SECTION "L". Honorable Terry Alarcon, Judge.
State v. Marino, 773 So. 2d 151, 2000 La. LEXIS 3061 (La., Nov. 3, 2000)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: By bill of information, defendant was charged with possession of marijuana with the intent to distribute. He pleaded not guilty, and he was tried by a jury in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, which found him guilty as charged. Defendant filed a motion for new trial that was denied. The trial court denied defendant's motion for reconsideration of sentence and granted his motion to appeal.


OVERVIEW: A parole officer knocked on a door, which was answered by defendant, and identified himself. He asked defendant to open the door, and defendant did so, whereupon the officer detected a strong smell of marijuana. The appellate court found nothing in the record to support the contention that the warrantless search of defendant's home was a subterfuge for a police investigation. The officer had reasonable suspicion that defendant was in parole violation when he and the other agents went to defendant's home. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction: defendant exercised dominion and control over the marijuana. As to defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel, defendant was essentially complaining about the attorney's trial strategy. Defendant failed to meet his burden in showing counsel was ineffective. As to the sentence, the trial court did not err in sentencing defendant as a second offender.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Bradley


00-KA-1090


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-1090 (La.App. 5 Cir. 06/28/01); 791 So. 2d 156; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1722



June 27, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 24, 2001.
Writ of error denied State v. Bradley, 817 So. 2d 1151, 2002 La. LEXIS 2074 (La., June 14, 2002)
Appeal after remand at State v. Bradley, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 647 (La.App. 5 Cir., Mar. 11, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NO. 99-5477, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; DETERMINATION AND SENTENCE AS A MULTIPLE OFFENDER VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the 24th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) to possession of cocaine, reserving his right to appeal the denial of his motion to suppress evidence. The trial court sentenced defendant. Defendant stipulated as to the allegations in a multiple bill of information the State then filed and was resentenced as a habitual offender. Defendant appealed the denial of his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was patrolling in an area known to have a high volume of narcotics trade and prostitution. He saw defendant knocking on the doors of a motel. The officer suspected that defendant was preparing to commit a burglary, looking to purchase or sell narcotics, or looking for a prostitute. The officer stopped defendant and conducted a pat down search. The officer found a wrapper containing crack cocaine on the ground next to defendant's leg and cocaine on defendant's pants leg. Defendant alleged the officer did not have reasonable suspicion to stop defendant for an investigation. On appeal, the court found that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence as the preponderance of the evidence did not clearly favor suspicion. However, the failure of the trial court to advise defendant of his right to a hearing and to remain silent as to the multiple bill violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(D)(1)(a). Further, defendant was not advised by the trial court of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. The multiple offender finding and sentence were vacated, and the original sentence was reinstated The case was remanded for another multiple offender hearing.

 

1692 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Evergreen Presbyterian Ministries, Inc. v. La. Dep't of Health & Hosps.


2000 CA 0852


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 0852 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/22/01); 808 So. 2d 681; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1630



June 22, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 469,623, Division "I". Honorable R. Michael Caldwell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ministry sued defendant Department of Health and Hospitals (DHH) seeking injunctive relief to prevent implementation of a plan for reducing public funds expenditures, resulting in decreased funding to it. Ministry challenged the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, sustaining the DHH's objection to jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sustained the DHH's exception pleading lack of subject matter jurisdiction as to injunctive relief. The ministry filed an appeal, assigning as error the trial court's judgment partially granting the DHH's declinatory exception pleading the objection of lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The DHH relied on La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 3601 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4062. The ministry argued the case did not involve the expenditure of public funds. If the case involved expenditure of public funds and the expenditure would result in a deficit, no injunctive relief was possible. The trial court rejected the ministry's argument, stating it was clear the case involved the expenditure of public funds. The appellate court found no error in the trial court's ruling. Likewise, the appellate court rejected plaintiff ministry's argument asserting a right to traverse the affidavit of the DHH secretary, and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court sustaining the DHH's exception pleading lack of subject matter jurisdiction as to injunctive relief.

 

1693 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mitchell


No. 1999 KA 0283 R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


1999 0283 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/22/01); 808 So. 2d 664; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1639



June 22, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of St. Mary, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 98-148,741. Honorable John E. Conery, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sixteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of St. Mary, State of Louisiana, convicted defendant of one count of attempted first-degree murder. The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction. However, the supreme court reversed the appellate court's decision and remanded the case so the appellate court could address defendant's remaining assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: The criminal case allotment system in the trial court violated due process. However, defendant did not argue that prejudice occurred as a result of the allotment of his case and there was no record of any actual prejudice to defendant. Thus, the assignment of defendant's trial under the unconstitutional allotment system was at most harmless error. Also, defendant argued that the prosecutor improperly commented on his right to remain silent in his closing argument. Because defendant failed to object at the time that the statement was made, he was precluded from raising the issue on appeal. Further, although the definition of the crime the trial court read to the jury during voir dire was incorrect, the error did not warrant a mistrial because the correct definition was given during the trial court's final instruction to the jury. In addition, defendant the evidence was sufficient to support the element of a drive-by shooting that required the shooting to take place from a public highway or street. Finally, the appellate court found that defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentence.

 

1694 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


NUMBER 2000 KA 2202


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 2202 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/22/01); 809 So. 2d 198; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1649



June 22, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of West Baton Rouge State of Louisiana. Case Number 991112. Honorable J. Robin Free, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of West Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, sentenced defendant to 12 years of imprisonment at hard labor after he was found guilty of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A and B. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the evidence that resulted from an unconstitutional search and seizure. A search by a club security guard, a private citizen, was not prohibited by the Fourth Amendment because it only protected against illegal searches by government agents. By entering the club, defendant had no expectation of privacy and consented to the search. Defendant maintained that the seizure of the plastic bag containing cocaine by the detective was prohibited because the officer did not know what was contained in the defendant's pocket when he initiated the search. The Fourth Amendment did not prohibit governmental use of the then non-private information. The officer conducted a limited search, which was the least intrusive means reasonably available to insure the officer's own safety. When the plastic bag containing the white rocks became apparent to the officer, he possessed probable cause at that point to search and seize the bag without a warrant. The officer had probable cause to believe that the defendant possessed contraband or a weapon, and was justified in the warrantless detention/arrest and search.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1695 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State Farm Fire & Cas. Co.


No. 2000 CA 0539


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 0539 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/22/01); 804 So. 2d 41; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1663



June 22, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Brown v. State Farm Fire & Cas. Co., 803 So. 2d 37, 2001 La. LEXIS 3362 (La., Dec. 7, 2001)
Later proceeding at, Sub nomine at Wooley v. State Farm Fire & Cas. Ins. Co., 2005 La. LEXIS 142 (La., Jan. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. DOCKET NO. 451,286. HONORABLE CURTIS CALLOWAY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) dismissed the claims of plaintiff, the Commissioner of Insurance, that he had a constitutional right to seek judicial review of adverse administrative decisions in an action against defendant insurance company. The Commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner alleged that the trial judge erred in ruling that the Commissioner did not have standing to seek judicial review of the decision rendered by the Division of Administrative Law and in dismissing the suit with prejudice without allowing the Commissioner an opportunity to amend the petition. The Louisiana Administrative Procedure Act (LAPA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:964(A)(2), allowed the Commissioner to argue its position before the administrative law judge but specifically excluded judicial review to an agency or an official. The court found that the legislature manifested a clear intention to limit the Department of Insurance's right to seek judicial review. The Louisiana Constitution did not give a juridical person, the Commissioner, the same constitutionally protected rights reserved to the individual and for the good of the whole. There was no error by the trial court in failing to allow the Commissioner to amend the petition because the insurance company's exception of no right of action was constitutional. The Commissioner had an adequate remedy at law by filing a declaratory judgment action or other type proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lightfoot v. Stalder

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought judicial review in the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) of a disciplinary decision made by the Louisiana Department of Public Safety and Corrections after the inmate filed a frivolous claim. The district court dismissed the suit. Following the denial of his motion for a new trial, the inmate moved for a devolutive appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that a corrections officer was unable to do his job because he was handicapped and took numerous pills. The claim was investigated and found to be frivolous. The inmate was found to be in violation of a disciplinary rule and sentenced to a custody change to a maximum-working cellblock and two weeks of confinement. The inmate alleged in the trial court that he was subjected to disciplinary action for exercising his right to free speech and was subjected to cruel and unusual punishment. On appeal, the court found no error in the dismissal of the inmate's petition for judicial review or in the finding that the claim constituted a successive claim or strike pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1187 of the Louisiana Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure Act (Act), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171 et seq. Further, the appellate court was without jurisdiction since under the Act the inmate could not seek appellate court review of the district court's decision.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the district court was affirmed.

Mexic v. Mexic


2000 CA 1274


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 1274 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/22/01); 808 So. 2d 685; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1627

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, vacated, recalled, and annulled the writ seizure and notice of seizure in garnishment, and granted summary judgment to defendant husband decreeing a Roth individual retirement account exempt from seizure. Plaintiff wife appealed the summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The husband and the wife were divorced. The wife filed a petition to make executory a 1990 judgment in her favor and against defendant husband, in a suit partitioning community property following termination of the matrimonial regime. The husband argued that the Roth individual retirement account was exempt from seizure by law and sought a court order declaring its exempt status. The appellate court found that all Roth individual retirement accounts were exempt from seizure under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3881. Therefore, the judgment of the trial court vacating, recalling, and annulling the writ of seizure and notice of seizure in garnishment was affirmed.

State ex rel. Ieyoub v. Racetrac Petroleum, Inc.


01-0458


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-0458 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/20/01); 790 So. 2d 673; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1574



June 20, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 99-4911, HONORABLE JOHN DAMIAN TRAHAN.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general sought injunction relief in the 15th Judicial District, Lafayette Parish, Louisiana, against defendant gas wholesaler and retailer for alleged violations of antitrust, false advertising, and unfair sales. From an order denying the same, the appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: The Louisiana State Attorney General appealed the order of the district court denying injunctions against appellee gas wholesaler and retailer for violations of statutes prohibiting restraints of trade and monopolies. In response, motions and exceptions were filed. The trial court sustained these exceptions and found that the State presented no cause of action. The court of appeals affirmed, holding that the State failed to plead even bare bone facts to support its allegations.
