Rev. Stat. Ann. 13:50811. Use of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 51:1411 was improper after the suit was filed. Improper cumulation had occurred. The trial court properly compelled discovery of all relevant materials to the defense, and the court properly held that federal antitrust law did not preempt state antitrust law. The court further declined to consider appellee's answers as they did not arise from final judgments.


OUTCOME: The order of the district court was affirmed.

 

1699 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Garrett v. City of Bossier City


No. 34,784-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,784 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/20/01); 792 So. 2d 24; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1599



June 20, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 99,930. Honorable Cecil P. Campbell, II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART, AFFIRMED IN PART, AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen sued appellees city and police officer in the 26th Judicial District Court, Bossier Parish, Louisiana, for arresting him when he was unable to produce his driver's license, after being stopped for not wearing a seatbelt. The trial court dismissed the citizen's complaint, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen could not produce his driver's license, because he left it at home when he went to pick up his wife from work. A municipal court judge had recommended that anyone unable to produce a driver's license should be arrested, and that recommendation had been passed on to the city's police officers without any determination of its legality. This procedure created a de facto policy. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:411.1 and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 211.4, when the officer had reasonable grounds to believe the citizen was driving without a license, he was to, and did, determine if a license had been issued to the citizen and whether that license was under suspension, revocation, or cancellation. When he determined a valid license had been issued to the citizen, he was to issue a citation rather than arrest the citizen. While the officer could not be held accountable for following a departmental "directive," the city was obligated to determine the legality of the judge's recommendation and could be held liable for its failure to do so. The citizen's arrest was statutorily prohibited.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment dismissing the citizen's complaint against the city was reversed, and the citizen was awarded damages. The trial court's judgment dismissing the citizen's complaint against the officer was affirmed.

 

1700 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodrigue


No. 2000-KA-1369


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-KA-1369 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/13/01); 789 So. 2d 729; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1698



June 13, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 2, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 408-386, SECTION "J". Honorable Leon Cannizzaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), of vehicular homicide and perjury. He then pleaded guilty to being a multiple offender. Defendant was sentenced to 15 years at hard labor, without benefit of probation, parole or suspension. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant hit another vehicle, causing it to flip over, while trying to pass a truck. The other vehicle's driver died. Defendant testified at his wife's trial that she had been driving the car, but later admitted he had been driving. Under La. Rev. Stat. 14:32.1, defendant should have been assessed a fine, as well as imprisonment, but the appellate court did not correct this error since the State did not raise it. Defendant was not entitled to the suppression of results of blood tests conducted with his consent. Defendant's motion to continue, after one of his attorneys discovered the victim was a close friend's fiancee, was properly denied because orally made after jury selection had begun. Considering defendant's criminal history, and his lack of remorse, outlined in the trial court's extensive findings under La. Code Crim. Proc. 894.1, defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive. Defendant did not preserve his argument to suppress his blood tests because they were conducted by persons without the requisite qualifications since he did not object to their admission at trial, and his argument at a hearing to suppress them was different than that raised on appeal.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1701 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kezerle


01-0079


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-0079 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/06/01); 789 So. 2d 725; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1447



June 6, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF VERNON, NO. 57,863, VERNON BRUCE CLARK, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of vehicular homicide and DUI in the 30th Judicial District Court, Vernon Parish, Louisiana. On appeal, he contended that his sentence for the homicide was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to 20 years at hard labor and a concurrent term of 6 months in jail upon convictions for DUI and vehicular homicide. A motion to reconsider the sentences was denied. On appeal, he contended that the sentence was unconstitutionally excessive and did not give sufficient weight to the mitigating factors he presented. The appeals court disagreed and affirmed. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1 allowed for imprisonment with or without hard labor for not less than nor more than 20 years. The trial judge considered the facts of the accident, the pre-sentencing investigation report, as well as evidence of mitigation, including that he had a family, a career, remorse for the victim, and a realization of what he had done. However, appellant had numerous past offenses for DUI, a callous disregard for the safety of others, a blood alcohol content of three times the legal limit, and an incapability or refusal to achieve alcohol rehabilitation. Thus the sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1702 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walker


No. 01-KA-51


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-51 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/30/01); 789 So. 2d 86; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1346



May 30, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published July 16, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NO. 00-963, DIVISION "O", THE HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of armed robbery committed with a gun, pursuant La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. The State filed written notice of its intention to apply the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §14:64.3. At the conclusion of trial, a jury in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, returned a verdict of guilty as charged as to both counts. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: The two victims had dinner and then checked into a motel. Two men appeared in the open doorway of the motel room. One of them, later identified as defendant, pointed a gun. The victims were ordered into the bathroom. When they came out, they saw that the victim's car was gone. In his first allegation of error, the defendant alleged that the imposition of a greater sentence under the auspices of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.3 was unconstitutional. The appellate court's relevant inquiry was whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.3 required a factual determination, and if so, whether that determination increased the sentence beyond the maximum statutory penalty. The statute clearly required a factual determination as to whether the armed robbery was committed using a firearm as opposed to some other dangerous instrumentality. The only weapon mentioned by prosecution witnesses was a gun. The trial court's imposition of two five-year sentences did not increase the penalty beyond the maximum term. The sentence, therefore, did not violate due process. Under the circumstances, the appellate court also did not find that the 30-year sentence was excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the matter was remanded to provide notice to defendant of limitations for filing post convictions relief.

 

1703 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Succession of Chatelain


No. 2000-CA-1267


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1267 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/16/01); 788 So. 2d 620; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1585



May 16, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published July 11, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 97-14806, DIVISION "D-16", Honorable Roland L. Belsome, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant heir filed a petition to reopen the succession of his deceased mother. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, denied the petition and heir appealed.


OVERVIEW: Heir's mother died testate. Mother's will named heir and his brother as co-executors, with only one of them being empowered to act if the other was unable or unwilling. Brother made several unsuccessful attempts to get heir to cooperate in administering the estate. Brother finally filed a proposed judgment of succession, after notice to heir, and the estate was distributed according to the plan. Heir questioned the accuracy of the distribution. A meeting was held and letters were exchanged, but no further action was taken, other than a request by heir for the distribution of proceeds of the sale of property the brothers received as part of the estate, until almost one year later, when heir file his petition to reopen. Heir had cashed all distribution checks sent to him. The appellate court held that a succession could be reopened only where other property was found or there was other good cause. The case did not involve new found property and, as heir had not filed his petition until after all the property had been distributed, the appellate court could not say that the trial court had abused its discretion in denying the petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1704 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walker


No. 2000-KA-1349


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1349 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/16/01); 789 So. 2d 632; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1586



May 16, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published July 11, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 402-882, SECTION "H", Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted possession of cocaine with intent to distribute in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), and sentenced as a second felony offender to 14 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed placing a gun in the trunk of an automobile he had not been occupying. An officer retrieved the gun and found a bag of crack cocaine. When defendant was arrested, he had a key to the trunk in his pocket. Only the first five years of a sentence for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute could be imposed without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension. That period was two and one-half years, when the conviction was for attempt. Finding a key to the car's trunk in defendant's pocket, after he was observed placing a gun there, was sufficient to establish his dominion and control over the contraband also found in the trunk. The trial court's mischaracterization of the felony defendant was previously convicted of, in finding him to be a prior offender, was not a basis for vacating his multiple offender adjudication. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by not ordering a presentence investigation. The trial court enumerated the factors it considered in imposing sentence, pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1, as well as the current conviction, and did not abuse discretion in imposing sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction, multiple offender adjudication, and sentence were affirmed.

 

1705 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gilbert


No. 00-KA-1822


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-1822 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/16/01); 788 So. 2d 574; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1135



May 16, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published July 16, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NO. 98-2433, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE CHARLES V. CUSIMANO, II, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his enhanced second felony offender sentence imposed by the 24th Judicial District, Jefferson Parish, Louisiana, contending that it was both excessive and illegal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of obscenity and sentenced as a second felony offender to six years in prison at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. The trial court denied a motion to reconsider, and on appeal, defendant contended the sentence was both illegal and excessive and that there was nothing in the record to support imposing a maximum sentence. The appeals court upheld the sentence. The court reasoned that the instant offense was committed only 18 months after defendant was released from prison for convictions of robbery and forcible rape, for which he served 10 years. This prior imprisonment term did not serve either to rehabilitate him or to deter him from committing sexual acts against women. The sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive. As to the illegality, the case was remanded for correction of the minute entry to reflect that the sentence was without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed, but the case was remanded to correct the minute order, reflecting the actual sentence imposed.

 

1706 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Wiley v. City of New Orleans


No. 2000-CA-1544, COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-CA-1544 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/16/01); 809 So. 2d 151; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1592



May 16, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 94-10309, DIVISION "K-14". HONORABLE RICHARD J. GANUCHEAU, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), entered a final judgment setting plaintiff's damages and apportioning fault at one-third to defendant city and two-thirds to defendant unknown driver, where plaintiff was injured when the unknown driver veered a stolen vehicle off a road and struck plaintiff. Plaintiff appealed the allocation of fault. Defendant city appealed an evidentiary finding and the sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured party was walking near an intersection designed, constructed, and maintained by defendant city. Suddenly, a stolen vehicle being driven by a person left the roadway, jumped the curb, and struck plaintiff. The driver of the vehicle fled. Plaintiff suffered debilitating injuries. Plaintiff sued defendant unknown driver, and also sued defendant city on a theory of negligent design, construction, and maintenance of a dangerous and unfit zigzag intersection. Plaintiff introduced testimony from an expert witness who based his testimony on the dangerousness of the road on police reports. The trial court found defendant city one-third liable and defendant unknown driver two-thirds liable for plaintiff's injuries. After judgment was entered accordingly, the appellate court modified the judgment because La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2324 allowed plaintiff to recover 50 percent of his damages from one tortfeasor even though that tortfeasor was found only one-third liable. Also, the evidence was sufficient to find defendant city negligent. The expert's testimony was properly admitted and plaintiff's award of interest could not be capped.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed as modified. No error occurred in assigning fault. Also, plaintiff's expert was properly allowed to testify as to opinions based on police reports otherwise inadmissible as hearsay. However, under applicable statutory law, plaintiff was entitled to recover from defendant city 50 percent of his damages even though it was found only one-third at fault. Finally, plaintiff was entitled to full judicial interest.

State v. Norwood


No. 34,584-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,584 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/09/01); 789 So. 2d 614; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 951



May 9, 2001, Rendered

PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 200945. Honorable Leon L. Emanuel, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) convicting him of aggravated oral sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated oral sexual battery. On appeal, he made several assignments of error regarding the sufficiency of the evidence convicting him, the denial of his due process rights, and the length of his sentence. Upon review, the appellate affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that: (1) the evidence was sufficient to convict the defendant; (2) the defendant was not denied due process; and (3) the defendant's sentence was not excessive. In viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, a rational trier of fact could have found that the defendant touched the genitalia of the victim with his mouth or tongue against her will by force despite her utmost resistance, and the facts presented at trial supported the district attorney's decision to prosecute him under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.4. The trial court considered a wide range of factors in sentencing the defendant, and a sentence of four-and-one-half years could hardly be considered excessive given the aggravating nature of his crime and the possible range of sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Williams


No. 2000-KA-0011 C/W No. 2000-KA-1058


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-0011 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/09/01); 788 So. 2d 515; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1235



May 9, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published July 11, 2001.
Writ denied by State v. Williams, 815 So. 2d 832, 2002 La. LEXIS 1556 (La., May 10, 2002)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Williams v. State, 872 So. 2d 487, 2004 La. LEXIS 1510 (La., Apr. 30, 2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at State ex rel. Williams v. State, 888 So. 2d 857, 2004 La. LEXIS 3833 (La., Dec. 17, 2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at State ex rel. Williams v. State, 888 So. 2d 861, 2004 La. LEXIS 3836 (La., Dec. 17, 2004)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Williams v. State, 965 So. 2d 393, 2007 La. LEXIS 2291 (La., 2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Williams v. Cain, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 109099 (E.D. La., July 16, 2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Williams v. Cain, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 139674 (E.D. La., Dec. 14, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 399-049, SECTION "H". HONORABLE CAMILLE BURAS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment, based upon a jury verdict, of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicting him of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. He pled guilty to attempted possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. The trial court adjudicated appellant a third felony offender as to the cocaine charge, and sentenced him to life imprisonment, with a concurrent four year sentence on the firearms charge.


OVERVIEW: Officers, armed with a search warrant for appellant's residence, set up a surveillance to verify appellant was still selling narcotics. The officers observed 11 drug transactions and ultimately seized numerous bags of cocaine, two beepers, a significant amount of cash, and a revolver. On appeal, the appellant argued the search warrant application failed to establish probable cause to believe that contraband would be found. He also contended the search warrant was "stale." The convictions were affirmed. The search warrant affidavit established the confidential informant's knowledge, reliability, and veracity. Further, information provided by the informant regarding ongoing cocaine sales at appellant's residence gave the trial judge probable cause to believe that five days after the first controlled purchase, cocaine would still be found. The erroneous denial of a motion to recuse one trial judge, who was a former district attorney, was harmless error, as appellant did not suffer any prejudice. Finally, appellant failed to rebut the presumption that the mandatory life sentence imposed on him as a third-felony habitual offender was unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. There was no indication appellant would have faired better had one trial judge, who had been employed with the district attorney's office at the time the office was prosecuting appellant, been recused as to the firearm charge and a new judge appointed to accept appellant's guilty plea. Mandatory life sentence for appellant, a third offender convicted of three drug offenses, was not unconstitutionally excessive.

 

1709 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Hardy v. Blood Sys., Inc.


01-0134


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-0134 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/03/01);  794 So. 2d 13; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 869



May 2, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied June 6, 2001. Released for Publication June 6, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 99-685 CONSOLIDATED WITH 99-686. HONORABLE J. BYRON HEBERT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sued appellees in the 15th Judicial District Court, Lafayette Parish (Louisiana), for medical malpractice, alleging one of their children contracted the hepatitis C virus as a result of a blood transfusion administered by appellee hospital with blood supplied by appellee blood bank. The trial court granted appellees' exceptions of prescription and appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sued 15 years after the transfusion. Appellees asserted the three year medical malpractice prescriptive period in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 prescribed the action. Appellees were not "qualified health care providers" under the Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq., but § 9:5628 applied to non-qualified health care providers, like appellee hospital, as the statute did not preclude such application, and the definition of "health care provider" included hospitals. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41(D) also required this conclusion. "Health care provider" did not include "community blood center," so § 9:5628 did not prescribe appellants' action against appellee blood bank, and their action was filed within the general tort prescriptive period. The fact that the latency period of appellants' child's disease exceeded the prescriptive period in § 9.5628 did not render application of the statute unconstitutional as it did not create a classification discriminating against a class of individuals because of their physical condition, and the record did not indicate the statute furthered no state interest.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was partly affirmed, as appellants' claim against appellee hospital was prescribed, and partly reversed, as appellant's claim against appellee blood bank was not prescribed because, at the time of the transfusion, blood banks were not health care providers under the medical malpractice act, and the action was filed within the general tort prescriptive period.

 

1710 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Affordable Hous. Developers, Inc. v. Kahn


No. 2000-CA-0611 CONSOLIDATED WITH: No. 2000-CA-0612


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-0611 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/25/01); 785 So. 2d 251; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1196



April 25, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied May 31, 2001. Released for Publication June 11, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NOS. 98-16719 C/W 99-6703, DIVISION "G-11". HONORABLE ROBIN M. GIARRUSSO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, in separate lawsuits consolidated because they addressed similar legal issues, each sued appellees in the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), to recover penalties and interest assessed on delinquent property taxes. The trial court maintained exceptions of prescription, and appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city adopted an ordinance imposing penalties and interest on those who were delinquent in paying their property taxes. Those penalties and interest were imposed on appellants, who acknowledged they were delinquent in the payment of their property taxes. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2110 (Supp. 2001), appellants could only challenge the validity of the tax if they first timely paid it. This included a challenge to appellee city's ordinance imposing penalties and interest for delinquent taxes. Appellants' acknowledgments, in each of their petitions, that they were delinquent in the payment of their taxes, placed upon them the burden of negating appellees' allegation that their claims had each prescribed, since prescription was apparent on the face of their petitions. The payment-under-protest requirement of § 47:2110 applied not only to the base ad valorem tax but also to the enforcement of any provision of the tax laws, including a challenge to interest and penalties.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed because appellants were not statutorily eligible to challenge appellee city's ordinance imposing penalties and interest for delinquent taxes unless they timely paid their taxes. Having admittedly failed to do so, their claims prescribed.

Kaiser Aluminum & Chem. Corp. v. USW


No. 00-CA-1851


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-1851 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/24/01); 785 So. 2d 238; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 831; 168 L.R.R.M. 2145



April 24, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Refused April 26, 2001. Released for Publication April 26, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. JAMES, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NUMBER 25,613, DIVISION "D,". HONORABLE PEGRAM MIRE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employer sought to enjoin defendant unions from picketing in the Twenty-third Judicial District Court, Parish of St. James (Louisiana). The parties stipulated to an order on the picketing. The parties filed rules for contempt for violations of the order. The trial court ordered plaintiff to erect a sign and found three of its employees in contempt. Plaintiff filed a devolutive appeal and suspensively appealed the judgment of contempt.


OVERVIEW: The parties agreed to a stipulated order to govern picketing at a plant. The trial court ordered plaintiff to erect a sign to advise car driver entering the plant to stop after it found three of plaintiff's employees had violated the stipulated order in entering the plant. The trial court found the three employees were in contempt of court. Before the appeal could be heard the labor dispute was resolved. The appellate court found (1) any ruling on the claim that the trial court erred in ordering a sign to be erected was moot, (2) the trial court's factual determinations did not constitute an abuse of discretion, (3) the trial court did not error in refusing to enjoin the impeding of vehicles during the labor dispute, (4) the trial court did not error in its findings that plaintiff's employees failed to allow defendants' members to picket as stated in the stipulated order, (5) the stipulated order was not vague and ambiguous and gave plaintiff's employees fair notice, (6) the record showed that plaintiff's employees were proven guilty of contempt beyond a reasonable doubt, (7) the convictions and sentences did not violate equal protection, and (8) the sentences were not excessive.


OUTCOME: Appeal of order to erect a sign was dismissed as moot. Judgment was affirmed as to all remaining parts as the trial court did not err in its findings and orders.

State v. Davis


No. 00-KA-1753


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-1753 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/24/01); 786 So. 2d 834; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 837



April 24, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published June 18, 2001.
Related proceeding at State ex rel. Davis v. State, 2004 La. LEXIS 518 (La., Feb. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, NO. 97-3403, DIVISION "F", HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, that convicted him on a jury verdict of aggravated burglary, found him to be a third felony offender, and imposed a sentence of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A victim identified defendant as one of three men who robbed him at gunpoint. Defendant was tried and convicted of aggravated burglary, found by the trial court to be a third felony offender, and sentenced to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed; the appellate court affirmed. The sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive, as it was imposed under the Habitual Offender Statute, which had previously been held to be constitutional. Defendant claimed that the State made a deal with the victim, who had criminal charges pending, in exchange for his testimony. He claimed error in the State's failure to disclose this deal, in the perjury the victim committed when he denied that any deal was made, and in the trial court's bias against defendant because of the deal. But the victim, on direct examination, denied that any deal had been made; the fact that after the trial the victim pled guilty to theft and received a suspended sentence was not proof of any deal, and the trial court did not err in refusing to allow defendant to cross-examine witnesses about the victim's alleged drug dealing, because such evidence was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1713 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


No. 00-KA-1930


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-1930 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/11/01); 786 So. 2d 798; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 813



April 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published June 18, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-3705, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appeals the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Jefferson Parish, Louisiana, denying his motion to suppress a gun seized and that his guilty plea was invalid, as the court imposed an incarceration condition, which he had not been informed of, prior to his plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to the charge of with being a convicted felon in possession of a firearm. On a Crosby appeal, he alleged that the trial court erred in failing to suppress the gun seized from his person and that his guilty plea was invalid because the judge imposed a condition on his incarceration, that he would not be eligible for parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, which he had not been informed of previously. The appeals court affirmed his conviction, first reasoning that officers had probable cause to suspect defendant had been involved in a crime, pursuant to a disturbance call. When defendant fled, this added to the officer's suspicions that rose to probable cause to arrest. The resulting search and seizure was thus incident to a valid arrest. On the second claim of error, the court reasoned that the record established defendant was informed of the condition. Further, under a Crosby appeal, defendant could not claim a sentence qualification as error, since it was not a non-jurisdictional defect.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Abuan v. Smedvig Tankships, Ltd.


No. 2000-CA-1120


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1120 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/11/01); 786 So. 2d 827; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1207



April 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied May 15, 2001. Released for Publication May 15, 2001. Certiorari Denied February 19, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 745.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM PLAQUEMINES 25TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NO. 38-719, DIVISION "B". Honorable William A. Roe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART AND AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, through his guardian, sued various defendants. After trial of the admiralty claim, the 25th Judicial District Court, Louisiana, found for plaintiff and awarded him damages. Plaintiff moved to tax costs, including witness fees and expenses. Plaintiff and the sheriff of a parish moved to tax as costs the sheriff's commission. Defendants appealed the judgments awarding the sheriff his commission and plaintiff his costs.


OVERVIEW: In opposition to the sheriff's motion to tax cost, defendants argued in their memorandum that the fee and commission were an unconstitutional tax on interstate commerce in violation of the United States Constitution. The appellate court found no error in the trial court's judgment. Defendants complained that the cost of the fee awarded for the testimony of a witness fee was excessive. After reviewing the record, the appellate court did not find that the trial court abused its discretion in awarding this expert's fee, totaling $ 3,000, for his preparation and testimony at trial. The appellate court, however, reversed the judgment awarding the travel expenses of a foreign witness. However, the appellate court affirmed the award of this witness's fee. Defendants complained that the trial court erred in awarding costs for reports prepared by an expert before plaintiff filed suit. Because the record convinced the court that the expert prepared these reports as part of plaintiff's medical examination and treatment, the appellate court believed the trial court abused its discretion awarding the cost of these reports to plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, in part, reducing the award of costs. The judgment was also affirmed, in part.

 

1715 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


No. 2000-KA-1050


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1050 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/11/01); 784 So. 2d 781; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1212



April 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 1, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 410-489, SECTION "J". Honorable Leon Cannizzaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), of attempted possession of a firearm while in possession of a controlled and dangerous substance. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was among a group of people stopped by police as possible truants. One of the group attempted to dispose of cocaine by swallowing it. Police then patted defendant down, discovered a pistol, and arrested defendant for carrying a concealed weapon. Upon a search incident to arrest, police discovered crack cocaine in one of defendant's pockets. The stop and search of defendant were both permissible, in light of the involvement of illegal narcotics, even though they were initially found on defendant's companion. At trial, the prosecutor stated defendant had earned his living by selling crack cocaine, although there was no evidence of that. The trial court sustained defendant's objection, but defense counsel failed to request a mistrial. The comment was clearly improper under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 774, and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 770(2) required the trial court to grant a mistrial, upon motion. Defense counsel's failure to request a mistrial and/or an admonition of the jury prejudiced defendant to the extent of depriving him of a fair trial. Therefore, defendant did not receive the effective assistance of counsel guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was vacated because he did not receive effective assistance of counsel when his counsel failed to move for a mistrial after the prosecutor's unsupported comment that defendant had earned his living by selling drugs, particularly where defendant's defense depended upon the jury's evaluation of defendant's credibility.

 

1716 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Points


No. 2000-KA-1371


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1371 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/11/01); 787 So. 2d 396; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1215



April 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 1, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 372-254, SECTION "A". HONORABLE CHARLES L. ELLOIE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment, based upon a jury verdict, of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicting him of manslaughter and sentencing him to serve 40 years in prison at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of killing the mother of his estranged wife. The victim was six and one-half months pregnant when she died. The fetus died with the victim. On appeal, defendant argued the evidence was insufficient to support his manslaughter conviction. He did not dispute that his gun fired the fatal bullet. He insisted, however, that the weapon discharged accidentally. The judgment was affirmed. The evidence indicated that shortly before the shooting, defendant and his estranged wife argued over custody of their child and interfering family members at the victim's residence. Defendant returned to his apartment, armed himself with a gun, and returned to the victim's apartment. Several witnesses testified defendant forcibly entered the residence by breaking the door, and then proceeded to the victim's bedroom. The State's witnesses testified defendant stood in the bedroom, and fired the fatal shot with no words spoken. The jury's verdict was rational. Further, the statutory maximum sentence of 40 years was not unconstitutionally excessive due to the sense of shock and outrage at the loss suffered by the victim's family.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Even though defendant testified the shooting was accidental, the jury rationally chose to disregard defendant's account, and instead, credited the testimony of the State's witnesses that the shooting was intentional. Though maximum manslaughter sentence was imposed, the trial court properly considered the sentencing guidelines and its sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive.

State v. Lindsey


No. 2000-KA-0301


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-0301 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/11/01); 786 So. 2d 814; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1224

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted second degree murder in Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, and was sentenced to 30 years in prison without probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and seriously wounded another black man with whom he had been selling drugs when the victim refused to sell "bunk" drugs to some white men. Any error was however harmless beyond a reasonable doubt given that victim knew defendant well and positively identified him as the shooter. The serious nature of victim's wounds and defendant's juvenile record of drug and weapon offenses, which was included in the record as required, justified defendant's sentence as not excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Maraist v. Alton Ochsner Med. Found.


2000 CA 0404


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 0404 (La.App. 1 Cir. 4/4/01); 808 So. 2d 566; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 817



April 4, 2001, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied June 11, 2001. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published June 11, 2001.
Writ denied by Maraist v. Alton Ochsner Med. Found., 800 So. 2d 882, 2001 La. LEXIS 3743 (La., Nov. 2, 2001)
Subsequent appeal at Maraist (In re Maraist), 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1457 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 390,743 H), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE MICHAEL MCDONALD, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sued defendants for medical malpractice in the 19th Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana. They settled with one defendant for the maximum allowed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42B(1), and summary judgment in favor of the remaining defendants was granted. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' advised defendants of certain symptoms their child was experiencing. The child was diagnosed with bacterial meningitis, resulting in profound neurological impairment. Plaintiffs alleged defendants' medical care of the child had been substandard. They settled with one defendant and the Louisiana Patients' Compensation Fund (Fund) for the maximum amounts allowed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42B(1) and pursued their action against the remaining defendants. Those defendants moved for summary judgment on the grounds that, when plaintiffs settled with one defendant and the Fund, they received the maximum amount to which they were legally entitled. When damage could not be apportioned between multiple tortfeasors because the damage was indivisible, the claim was not severable. If the damage could be divided into two or more parts, with each part caused by a separate defendant, then each part constituted a separate injury under § 40:1299.42B(1). Otherwise the injured party could only recover the maximum provided by § 40:1299.42B(1). There was no evidence the child's injury could be divided into parts with each part traceable back to a specific delictual origin.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed because plaintiffs had recovered the maximum amount to which they were statutorily entitled when they settled with one of the defendants. Therefore, they could not pursue their claim against the remaining defendants. Plaintiffs' constitutional challenge to the applicable statute was not considered, since they received the maximum statutory recovery.

 

1719 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Haywood


No. 00-KA 1584


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-1584 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/28/01); 783 So. 2d 568; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 654



March 28, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 16, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 99-5020, DIVISION "K,". HONORABLE MARTHA E. SASSONE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, of possession of cocaine. After a multiple bill hearing, the trial court sentenced defendant as a second felony offender. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Officers, checking on a complaint of drug sales, knocked on a motel room door. A man who fit the description given by the anonymous complainant answered the door; drug paraphernalia was in plain view. Officers found defendant hiding in a shower, and handcuffed him after he tried to flee. He made movements towards his ankle; an officer frisked him and felt a package, which proved to contain drugs, in his sock. Defendant was tried and convicted of possession of cocaine, and sentenced as a multiple offender. He appealed; the appellate court affirmed. The officers needed no reasonable suspicion to knock on the door, and the drug gear in plain view gave them probable cause to arrest. Further, the warrantless entry was justified by exigent circumstances. Defendant's actions supplied reasonable suspicion to detain and frisk him. So the motion to suppress was properly denied. When defendant pled guilty to the predicate offense, he was advised of and waived his Boykin rights, and advised of potential sentences, and thus was properly sentenced as a second felony offender. His sentence was not excessive, as he had prior criminal activities and committed the crime while on probation.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The trial court properly denied the motion to suppress, as the warrantless entry of the motel room, and the pat-down search of defendant, were legal. Defendant was properly sentenced, as the record proved that his guilty plea to the predicate offence was proper under Boykin, and the sentence was not excessive in light of his criminal record and the fact that he committed the instant crime while on probation.

 

1720 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Galjour v. Harris


No. 2000 CU 2696


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 2696 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/28/01); 795 So. 2d 350; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 661



March 28, 2001, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied November 13, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 10357.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 97-11875 B. Honorable Elaine W. Guillot, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, uncle and aunt of the child, brought action against defendant father in the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana, seeking custody of their sister's minor child. Intervenor-plaintiffs were the child's maternal grandparents. When the trial court awarded visitation rights to the intervenor-parents, all parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the father of the minor child. The child's mother died from the effects of an inoperable brain tumor. Immediately following the mother's death, plaintiffs, her brother and his wife instituted the instant action seeking issuance of an emergency ex parte order granting them full custody of the child pending further orders from the court. The intervenor-plaintiffs were the maternal grandparents. At first blush, La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 136 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344 appeared to conflict. However, the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344 superceded those provisions of the article. Accordingly, the trial court awarded visitation rights to the maternal grandparents. Having found La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 136 to be inapplicable to these facts, there was no need for the trial court to undertake an analysis of the five factors listed in the article to determine if such visitation was in the best interest of the child. Since the intervenor-plaintiffs were granted visitation pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344A, it was hoped that they would serve as the natural conduits through which plaintiffs could sustain their relationship with the child.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1721 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Washington


No. 99-KA-1111


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-1111 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/21/01); 788 So. 2d 477; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1176



March 21, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 10, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 395-123, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court Orleans Parish, Section G (Louisiana) granted the State's motion in limine, and denied defendant's; convicted him, by jury, of possession with intent to distribute heroin, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1); and sentenced him to life imprisonment at hard labor, without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A uniformed officer driving to work in his personal car saw defendant in a high drug area leaning into a car manipulating something, appear startled, and immediately withdraw upon noticing the officer and walk to a nearby store. Two hours later the officer and his partner returned. The car was in the same place. Defendant was handing another male something, was startled on seeing the officers, balled up his fist and began walking to the store, was stopped and frisked by the officers, and dropped a foil packet on the ground. The other male had walked the other way. The officers found heroin in the packet, arrested defendant, entered the car, and found heroin and a gun there. The officers took defendant away. The car was gone when they returned. Defendant was convicted. The appellate court held that the motion to suppress was properly denied. Under the totality of the circumstances, the officers reasonably suspected that defendant was committing a crime, and had probable cause to believe more contraband was in the car. Admission of the gun was not prejudicial. Defendant had full access to the car. Exclusion of newspaper allegations against the officer was proper.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1722 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


McCall v. Bossier Parish Sch. Bd.


No. 34,983-CA, No. 34,984-CA (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,983 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/16/01); 785 So. 2d 57; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 553



March 16, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 105,347 & 105,348. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents of expelled high school students challenged the order of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, which affirmed rescinding a TRO and denied their injunctive relief against the expulsions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant students were expelled for leaving school without authorization and for use/possession of controlled substances. Their parents sought review and injunctive relief from the district court, contending the expulsion was not supported by substantial and rational evidence. The district court issued a temporary restraining order, TRO, directing the board to re-admit, but later rescinded and dismissed the TRO and denied appellants' requests for injunctive relief. The appeals court found technical error in charging the students with possession of a controlled substance, but did not find any procedural violations. The board properly found a violation subject to suspension and expulsion. However, the expulsions were vacated because of the confusion in the record created by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:416(C)(2)(a)(ii). The court recognized expulsion with assignment to an alternative school was a possible punishment, but the officials' discretion in administering punishment was arbitrary and abusive and did not account for any prior disciplinary problems, or lack of the same, and the actual disruption to the educational environment resulting from the student's drug use.


OUTCOME: Order vacated and case remanded. School board did afford appellants clear notice of their acts of misconduct and the opportunity to be heard, but official discretion was arbitrary and abusive for not accounting for any prior disciplinary problem (or lack of same) and the actual disruption to the educational environment.

La. Hand & Upper Extremity Inst., Inc. v. City of Shreveport


No. 34,404-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,404 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/28/01); 781 So. 2d 695; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 330



February 28, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 436,632. Honorable Roy L. Brun, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana dismissed plaintiff doctor's negligence claims against defendants, realtor and city, over medical clinic property subjected to a parking ordinance. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff doctor, through defendant realtor, bought a building on property that was zoned B-2 and had it renovated for $ 150,000. Plaintiff discovered that half the parking spaces actually belonged to the neighboring office. Defendant city issued a certificate of occupancy. Defendant city amended its medical clinic parking ordinance and made Shreveport, La., Code of Ordinances § 106-1338(2), deleting any low patient count exception. Plaintiff was denied a variance for more parking and received no offers when he listed the property for sale as a medical office. Plaintiff sued defendant realtor for breach for having failed to determine parking ordinance compliance, and sued defendant city for negligently granting building permits and a certificate for a project that did not conform with the parking law. Defendants were granted dismissal. The court affirmed. The sale contract with defendant realtor put the burden on plaintiff to confirm zoning compliance. Defendant realtor had no duty to warn of a potential parking ordinance amendment. The permit for mere renovation required no parking plat, and by the time the certificate issued, plaintiff's costs had been all incurred.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Contract with defendant realtor put the burden of zoning confirmation upon plaintiff, and defendant city's building permit had not required a parking plat.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana, convicting him of second degree murder, aggravated kidnapping and obstruction of justice, and sentencing him to two consecutive sentences of life imprisonment, following denial of his motion to reconsider sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in trial court of second degree murder, aggravated kidnapping and obstruction of justice, and sentenced to two consecutive sentences of life imprisonment, following denial of his motion to reconsider sentence. Defendant appealed, claiming insufficient evidence, double jeopardy, excessive sentences, improper trial court evidentiary rulings, improper jury instructions, prosecutorial misconduct, and ineffective assistance of counsel. The court vacated defendant's conviction for aggravated kidnapping, holding that defendant's convictions for both second degree felony murder and aggravated kidnapping subjected him to constitutionally prohibited double jeopardy. State v. Lacy


No. 99-KA-2225


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-2225 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/21/01); 782 So. 2d 47; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 564



February 21, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 402-434, SECTION "J". Honorable Leon Cannizzaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED, SECOND OFFENDER ADJUDICATION AND SENTENCE VACATED, THIRD OFFENDER ADJUDICATION ENTERED, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) of crime against nature. The trial court found defendant was a second offender, vacated the original sentence, and re-sentenced her to six years' hard labor. Defendant and the State appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with crime against nature in soliciting a police officer to engage in oral copulation for money. The State filed a multiple bill, accusing defendant of being a fourth offender. After a hearing, the trial court found defendant to be a second offender. Defendant alleged counsel was ineffective for failing to object to the sufficiency of prior convictions that were used to find defendant a second offender. The State alleged the evidence was sufficient in the two convictions the trial court rejected. The appellate court found the evidence presented was sufficient to support a finding defendant was advised of her Boykin rights. Therefore, counsel was not ineffective for his failure to object. The State's presentation of a minute entry for one conviction showing defendant was attended by counsel when she pled guilty, along with a properly executed waiver of rights/guilty plea form, was sufficient to carry the State's burden under the multiple offender statute. However, because the plea form for the other conviction was not dated and a handwritten addition could have been added at any time, the evidence was not sufficient for the other conviction.


OUTCOME: Conviction was affirmed as trial counsel was not ineffective. The trial court's adjudication of defendant as a second felony offender and defendant's sentence as a second felony offender were vacated. The appellate court adjudicated defendant to be a third offender, and remanded the matter to the trial court for re-sentencing as a third offender.

Snearl v. Mercer


No. 1999 CA 1738 C/W: No. 1999 CA 1739


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


1999 1738 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/16/01); 780 So. 2d 563; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 342



February 16, 2001, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied April 2, 2001. Released for Publication April 2, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Eighteen Judicial District Court for the Parish of Iberville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 45,874 "D" c/w 46,109 "D". Honorable Jack T. Marionneaux, Judge.



DISPOSITION: MOTION TO INTERVENE DISMISSED; EXCEPTION OF NO CAUSE OF ACTION DENIED; JUDGMENT REVERSED IN PART; AMENDED IN PART; AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED; AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found the defendant Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD) 90 percent at fault in a personal injury case. The remaining 10 percent of fault was attributed to the driver of a dump truck. The 18th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Iberville, Louisiana entered judgment in accordance with the verdict. A motion to intervene was filed on behalf of the State's insurer. Defendant DOTD appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were employees of defendant construction company. Plaintiffs were in a company dump truck traveling to a job site. One of the plaintiffs was driving while the other two sat in the front seat. As the unloaded dump truck approached an Interstate Highway 12 (I-12) overpass the plaintiff driver suddenly swerved into the left lane. The truck careened into the bridge rail along the overpass and vaulted over the railing to the ground below. One of the plaintiffs was left confined to a wheelchair for the remainder of his life and required reconstructive surgery. Defendant DOTD's liability was based on the defective condition of the bridge rail along the I-12 overpass. Plaintiff driver was also required to share some responsibility for the harm suffered. The awards of general damages bore a reasonable relationship to the elements of the proved damages. The appellate court declined to modify the award for future medical costs and life care. The appellate court did find it likely that the jury made an award of sympathy to one plaintiff's mother and reduced this award.


OUTCOME: The motion to intervene by defendant State's insurer was dismissed. The judgment of the trial court finding the driver 10 percent at fault was reversed, and the percentage of fault attributable to the driver was increased to 35 percent. The award to the mother of the plaintiffs was amended to $ 125,000. In all other respects, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Kennedy v. Macaluso


1999 CA 3016


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


1999 3016 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/16/01); 791 So. 2d 697; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 343



February 16, 2001, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 21st Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of Tangipahoa, State of Louisiana. Suit Number 9901881. Honorable Zorraine M. Waguespack, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individually and on behalf of their minor child, alleged that defendant negligently allowed their medical malpractice claim to prescribe. Also in this original petition, the plaintiffs raised the issue of the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605. The 21st Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of Tangipahoa, State of Louisiana sustained the defendants' exception of prescription. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The determination of the date of discovery in the instant case was greatly facilitated by the plaintiff mother's own admission, in a letter written to their current attorney and attached to their petition, that a short time prior to April 28, 1997, they were told by other attorneys that defendant had let the time run out on their medical malpractice claim. Thus, by her own admission, plaintiffs knew of defendant's alleged wrongful conduct at the latest by the date of the letter. Therefore, their action against him, filed more than one year from the date of discovery, was untimely, and the trial court was correct in so finding. Plaintiffs also sought a remand for consideration of the issue and a reevaluation of their prescription arguments in light of the outcome on the constitutionality issue. The appellate court found no merit to plaintiffs' argument.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Plaintiffs' action was untimely when action was filed more than one year of discovery.

Louisiana Assessors' Retirement Fund v. City of New Orleans


No. 1999 CA 3049


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


1999 3049 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/16/01); 796 So. 2d 687; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 345



February 16, 2001, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 459,362. Honorable J. Michael McDonald, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, issued a writ of mandamus to compel defendants, City of New Orleans and treasurer for the City of New Orleans and collector of revenue for the city, to remit certain tax monies to plaintiffs, Louisiana Assessors' Retirement Fund and the Louisiana Clerks' of Court Retirement and Relief Fund, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 11:1481, 11:1561. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, Louisiana Assessors' Retirement Fund and the Louisiana Clerks' of Court Retirement and Relief Fund, brought a mandamus action against defendants, City of New Orleans and treasurer for the City of New Orleans and collector of revenue for the city, seeking an order that defendants comply with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 11:1481, 11:1561 to remit to them a percentage of taxes. The parties testified that no contributions had ever been made by defendant city to either retirement fund in accordance with the statutes. The writ was granted. An order issued as to 1999 and subsequent years. Defendants appealed. The court affirmed. The statutes' constitutionality was not reviewable as defendants had not raised that below. Defendants' contemporaneous construction argument, that defendant city had interpreted the statutes as not applying to it for 25 years and that therefore such interpretation deserved deference, was undermined by defendant treasurer's testimony that he had not been aware of the statutes. Apparently, defendants had never made a conscious decision to ignore the statutes. Because of defendant city's chronic financial challenges, mandamus was the proper remedy.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Defendant city had never made a conscious decision to ignore the tax percentage remission statutes. Because of defendant city's chronic financial challenges, there was no other adequate remedy for plaintiffs besides mandamus.

Bank of West Baton Rouge v. Stewart


NUMBER 2000 CA 0114


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 0114 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/16/01); 808 So. 2d 464; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 417



February 16, 2001, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of West Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Suit Number 27,782. Honorable Jack T. Marionneaux, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, RENDERED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank challenged a trial court's judgment, entered by the Eighteenth Judicial District Court in and for the parish of West Baton Rouge (Louisiana), where the trial court found that a tax sale of property by the sheriff and ex-officio tax collector for the parish to be validly executed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant bank sued seeking redemption of a property or cancellation of a tax sale of property on which it was a mortgagee. Appellant alleged the sheriff and ex-officio tax collector had violated the bank's constitutional right to due process. The mortgagor had given appellant a mortgage on the property. Appellant duly recorded that interest in the parish's public records. The property was sold at a sheriff's sale after the mortgagors failed to pay taxes. Although the mortgagors received notice of the sale, appellant was not notified of it. Appellant claimed either that it was entitled to notice under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180.1 or that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court found both the sale and the statute to be valid. Appellant challenged that holding. The court reversed. A reasonably ascertainable mortgagee, as a party with an interest in property, did not waive its constitutional due process right to notice of seizure and sale of property by failing to request notice under the statute. While the statute was constitutional, appellant was entitled to notice of the seizure and sale because it was a reasonably ascertainable mortgagee.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and judgment rendered for appellant because the failure of the sheriff and ex-officio tax collector to give appellant, in its capacity as mortgagee with a significant property interest, due notice of the tax sale violated appellant's constitutional right to due process.

State v. Spencer


NUMBER 2000 KA 1318


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 1318 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/16/01); 808 So. 2d 455; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 429



February 16, 2001, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at State ex rel. Spencer v. State, 67 So. 3d 481, 2011 La. LEXIS 1731 (La., 2011)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Spencer v. Cain, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 188259 (E.D. La., July 24, 2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Spencer v. Cain, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 124919 (E.D. La., Sept. 4, 2012)
Writ denied by State v. Spencer, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 2673 (La.App. 1 Cir., Mar. 25, 2013)
Writ denied by State v. Spencer, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 1813 (La.App. 1 Cir., Sept. 9, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Spencer v. State, 147 So. 3d 173, 2014 La. LEXIS 1664 (La., 2014)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Spencer, 2016 La. App. LEXIS 1288 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 27, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Washington, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 96 CRI 64076. Honorable William J. Burris, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the life sentence imposed by the District Court, Parish of Washington, Louisiana, on his conviction for second degree murder, arguing that the trial court erred in not considering the aggravating and mitigating factors, and in not imposing the longest sentence that was not constitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: Appellant stabbed his victim 40 times, bludgeoned him with a hammer, and set fire to the victim's trailer to cover up the crime. He was tried for and convicted of second-degree murder. The trial judge sentenced him to life in prison without the possibility of parole. Appellant sought review; the appellate court affirmed. While the trial court did not explain why it imposed a life sentence, the record showed that appellant's crime involved profoundly violent acts resulting in the victim's death. Although only in his 20s, he had committed numerous criminal acts that endangered others. His crimes had escalated and, as evidenced by his assault of a sheriff and an inmate while the case was pending, he continued to be a danger to others. These factors justified the life sentence. Further, appellant failed to clearly and convincingly show that because of any unusual circumstances he was a victim of the legislature's failure to assign sentences meaningfully tailored to the culpability of the offender, the gravity of the offense, and the circumstances of the case. As the trial judge apparently concluded, there were no circumstances justifying a deviation from the mandatory sentence.


OUTCOME: Sentence affirmed. Appellant's life sentence was justified by the heinous nature of his crime, his criminal record, and his post-crime violence. Moreover, he failed to show any unusual circumstances justifying a deviation from the mandatory minimum sentence provided for the offense.

Holmes v. Forster


No. 2000-CA-0632


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-0632 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/14/01); 781 So. 2d 656; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 312; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8662



February 14, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 98-18448, DIVISION "F-10". Honorable Yada Magee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) upholding the decision of the administrative law judge and board of review, denying her unemployment compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was denied unemployment insurance benefits. On appeal, the issue was whether her employer, who admittedly failed to carry its burden at an administrative hearing of presenting competent evidence to prove that she was disqualified from receiving benefits, was entitled to a remand of the case to allow it a second opportunity to meet its burden of proof. The appeals court decided the issue in the negative. The court held that insufficient legal competent evidence was originally presented; thus it was unable to decide whether appellant was properly denied benefits. The only evidence that was admitted was based on hearsay. It also rejected the argument that remand should have been allowed so that the board of review could take additional evidence, to purge the hearsay, and expressed an unwillingness to make a finding with any certainty grounded on what was shown by the unsatisfactory record. The case was thus remanded for an award of benefits to appellant.


OUTCOME: Order reversed. The case was remanded for the sole purpose of allowing the board of review to enter an order in accordance with the mandate of the court, awarding appellant benefits. The employer was not to be allowed to present additional competent evidence on remand.

 

1733 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodriguez


No. 2000-KA-0519


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


00-0519 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/14/01); 781 So. 2d 640; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 321



February 14, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 396-349, SECTION "E". Honorable Calvin Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), of attempted possession of cocaine and sentenced to eight years at hard labor, without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence, with credit for time served. The appellate court granted defendant's writ application, ordering the trial court to grant defendant an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fled from a car a police officer pulled over for an expired tag. The officer saw defendant discard a bag. The officer did not see defendant discard a gun, but the officer found a gun by the bag, which contained cocaine. The appellate court found there effectively was no minimum sentence for a person convicted of attempted possession of cocaine in an amount more than 28 grams but less than 200 grams. Therefore, defendant's sentence was to be amended to delete the provision denying him the benefits of probation and parole. Further, the evidence of the recovery of the gun next to the bag had minimal relevance, but any error in admission of that evidence was harmless. Defendant was precluded from raising both the claim of excessive sentence and the claim that the trial court failed to consider the sentencing factors. Considering defendant's record and that he received a sentence of less than one-third of the maximum possible sentence to which he was exposed, it could not be said defendant's sentence was unconstitutionally excessive. Therefore, defense counsel's failure to file a motion to reconsider sentence did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed as to the conviction. Defendant's sentence was amended to delete the portion denying him the benefit of parole or probation and affirmed as amended.

 

1734 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chairs


No. 99-KA-2908


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-2908 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/07/01); 780 So. 2d 1088; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 257



February 7, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 396-767, SECTION "H", Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of two counts of simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling, and the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), sentenced him to life imprisonment as a habitual offender. He appealed his convictions and sentence, claiming the sentence was excessive, the evidence of his guilt and his prior convictions was insufficient, and that the trial court should have granted a mistrial.


OVERVIEW: Police saw appellant in the victim's home, chased and captured him, and found property belonging to the victim on his person. At trial, the victim testified that she had never seen appellant before, and did not give him permission to be in her home. Appellant was convicted of simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling, and because of a prior robbery and a burglary conviction, was given a mandatory life sentence under the Habitual Offender Law. He appealed; the appellate court affirmed. That the jury learned of appellant's aliases did not mean he was entitled to a mistrial, since reference to the aliases did not equate to evidence that appellant had committed another crime. The evidence was sufficient to allow a reasonable jury to conclude that appellant made an authorized entry and had the intent to commit a theft or felony. Fingerprint evidence established that appellant was the same person who committed the prior felonies ascribed to him. Finally, as the life sentence was required by the Habitual Offender Law, and appellant did not meet his burden to rebut the presumption that the life sentence was constitutional, the sentence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because (1) reference to appellant's alias in the indictment read to the jury did not mandate a mistrial; (2) the evidence was sufficient to convict; (3) appellant's prior convictions were adequately proved; and (4) the life sentence was appropriate under the Habitual Offender Law.
