State v. Richardson


No. 2000-KA-0416


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


00-0416 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/07/01); 780 So. 2d 1103; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 259



February 7, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 30, 2001.
Writ of error denied State v. Richardson, 823 So. 2d 934, 2002 La. LEXIS 2486 (La., Aug. 30, 2002)
Writ of error denied State ex rel. Richardson v. State, 836 So. 2d 38, 2003 La. LEXIS 269 (La., Jan. 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 401-631, SECTION "G". HONORABLE JULIAN A. PARKER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, for simple burglary under La. Rev. Stat. § 14:62. He asserted insufficient evidence, error in denying a motion to suppress, and that the trial court erred when it adjudicated him a fourth felony offender.


OVERVIEW: Officers testified defendant was standing in an empty lot with clothing with security tags and a store's labels on them. They later learned the store was burglarized. Store's manager identified the clothes as taken from the store. Store's surveillance tapes recorded the burglary, showing a black male riding a bicycle past the store immediately before the door was smashed, the perpetrator entering the store, and the perpetrator's clothes, which matched defendant's. Defendant implicitly admitted he committed the burglary, stating to the officers he was at the store by himself. Evidence was sufficient, there was reasonable cause to detain, and probable cause to arrest. Evidence of prior guilty pleas showed he was represented by counsel and advised of his rights. Defendant produced no evidence showing an infringement of his rights or a procedural irregularity in the taking of the pleas. The applicable enhancement statute was the one existing at the time of the commission of the offense for which the sentence was to be enhanced.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Police testimony of finding defendant with stolen clothing and surveillance tape from burglary showing suspect with same clothes worn by defendant, coupled with his statements he was at the store alone provided sufficient evidence for conviction. Officers had reasonable cause to detain and to arrest. There was no evidence of an infringement of rights or irregularities in prior pleas used for the enhancement.

Odom v. City of Lake Charles


00 01050-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


001050 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/31/01);  790 So. 2d 51; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 68



January 31, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied March 28, 2001. Released for Publication March 28, 2001.
Writ denied by Odom v. City of Lake Charles, 794 So. 2d 787, 2001 La. LEXIS 2069 (La., June 22, 2001)
Related proceeding at State through Div. of Admin. v. Nat'l Union Fire Ins. Co., 984 So. 2d 91, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 265 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU. [NO.92-3767]. HONORABLE ALCIDE JOSEPH GRAY.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AMENDED IN PART; OTHERWISE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff curator sued defendant city and defendant state transportation agency in the Fourteenth Judicial District, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana) after his son was injured in an auto accident. Defendant city settled with plaintiff. Defendant state transportation agency was found liable and assessed a percentage of fault in the award. Defendant state transportation agency and plaintiff appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff curator brought suit on behalf of his son against defendant city and defendant state transportation agency after the son was injured when his vehicle was catapulted off a bridge. All experts agreed that the curb and rail configuration caused the vehicle to vault over the bridge rail. Defendant city settled with plaintiff. The trial court found defendant state transportation agency was 60 percent at fault and defendant city had been 40 percent at fault and awarded damages. The appellate court found the trial court correctly assessed the fault of defendant state transportation agency. However, the appellate court found the son was partly at fault and reduced the percentage of fault to defendant city. Further, the trial court erred in accepting defendant's expert witness's testimony as to the amount of future medical expenses instead of plaintiff's expert witness's testimony.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed insofar as percentages of fault was allocated. Judgment was amended as to the award of future medical expenses and to include legal interest from the date of judicial demand. Judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

 

1737 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Trahan v. Our Lady of Lourdes Regional Med. Ctr., Inc.


00 1140


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


00 1140 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/31/01); 778 So. 2d 1205; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 48



January 31, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 991472, HON. EDWARD D. RUBIN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs challenged a judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District, Parish of LaFayette (Louisiana) granting defendant's exception of prescription after plaintiffs brought a medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed a complaint with the state's patient compensation fund against defendant medical center on October 30, 1996, claiming that defendant was negligent in failing to screen and, thereafter, in transfusing Hepatitis C infected blood to plaintiff husband during surgery following a motorcycle accident in January 1987. The medical review panel rendered its opinion in December 1998, stating that there was insufficient evidence to support a finding that defendant breached the standard of care. Thereafter, on March 26, 1999, plaintiffs filed a medical malpractice action against defendant alleging negligence. The trial court held that plaintiffs' suit had prescribed and that § 9:5628 was constitutional as it applied to plaintiff husband. Judgment was affirmed. Based on plaintiffs' failure to present any evidence that § 9:5628 did not further a reasonable state interest or was not rationally related to a state interest, the appellate court found the exception of prescription was properly granted. Section 9:5628 did not unfairly discriminate against plaintiff husband based on his physical condition.


OUTCOME: The judgment sustaining the exception of prescription in favor of defendant was affirmed, as plaintiffs failed to meet their evidentiary burden in challenging the constitutionality of the applicable statute of limitations because they did not offer any evidence that the statute furthered no state interest or was not rationally related to the state's interest.

 

1738 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fifteen Thousand Four Hundred Thirty-One Dollars


00 01252-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


00 1252 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/31/01); 779 So. 2d 1043; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 50



January 31, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 944570. HONORABLE PATRICK LOUIS MICHOT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State department of revenue appealed an order of the Fifteenth Judicial District, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana) finding appellee Lafayette Parish district attorney had the power to cause its tax lien to be cancelled thereby allowing appellee to unconstitutionally exercise a power exclusively reserved to the executive branch.


OVERVIEW: Police seized 10 pounds of marijuana from a homeowner and various other property. Appellee recorded a notice of forfeiture lien and appellant department of revenue recorded a tax assessment and lien. The homeowner pled guilty to possession of marijuana with intent to distribute and appellee district attorney filed a petition to obtain a forfeiture of all the items seized, naming only the homeowner in the forfeiture action. Appellee and the homeowner entered into a settlement agreement, but it made no reference to appellant or to either recorded lien. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment to cancel both liens and the trial court granted it. Appellant challenged the ruling, arguing appellee did not have the authority to cause its tax lien to be cancelled. The court held nothing in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1578 provided appellee any authority over a Louisiana Department of Revenue taxation lien. The court reversed, holding the constitutional separation of powers between the executive and judicial branches precluded appellee from cancellation appellant's lien.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, because the constitutional separation of powers between the executive and judicial branches precluded appellee district attorney from exercising the authority of the secretary of the department of revenue and taxation. Therefore, the trial court erred in granting the cancellation of the department of revenue's tax lien.

Hubbard v. Lakeland Nursing Home


No. 00-1004


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


00-1004 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/31/01); 781 So. 2d 95; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 52



January 31, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, PARISH OF RAPIDES. [NO. 98-05663], DISTRICT NO. 2. HONORABLE ANTHONY P. PALERMO.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant nursing home terminated the workers' compensation benefits for temporary total disability which appellee nurse had been awarded, appellee brought a disputed claim for compensation with the Office of Workers' Compensation, Parish of Rapides, District No. 2 (Louisiana). Appellee was found to be temporarily and totally disabled and entitled to benefits until she was capable of returning to work. Appellant challenged the decision.


OVERVIEW: Appellee nurse was assaulted while at work in appellant nursing home. She was awarded temporary total disability benefits for mental injury. After 104 weeks, appellant stopped weekly compensation benefits pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(d)(iii). Appellee disputed the termination of benefits. At trial, the Office of Workers' Compensation Administration found appellee was temporarily totally disabled and entitled to workers' compensation benefits until capable of returning to work. The appellate court found the relevant statute had been declared unconstitutional after the trial. By using the wrong standard of law, the trial court committed legal error. Further, there was clear and convincing evidence appellee suffered a mental injury that had caused her to be temporarily and totally disabled and not currently employable but possibly able to work part-time in the future.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed as appellee was temporarily totally disabled and entitled to workers' compensation benefits from the date of the termination of the benefits to the present.

 

1740 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Derouin


00 01150-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


00 01150 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/31/01); 778 So. 2d 1186; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 85



January 31, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THIRTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF VERNON, NO. 57,134. HONORABLE VERNON B. CLARK.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her sentence upon conviction for possession of marijuana from the Thirtieth Judicial District, Vernon Parish (Louisiana), asserting that the trial court erred in resentencing her and failed to consider the same as excessive.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was originally given a suspended sentence upon conviction of possession of marijuana. The court granted the State's motion to reconsider the sentence, as appellant was a second felony offender, and thus suspension of her sentence was prohibited. She appealed, asserting that her first conviction could not enhance her sentence because she had been pardoned, and that the ultimate sentence was excessive. The appeals court affirmed the sentence, reasoning that the automatic pardon provision under La. Const. art. IV, § 5(E)(1) did not in and of itself alter the prohibition against certain sentence suspensions under La. Code Crim. P. art. 893(A). Moreover, despite the court's error in its assessment of the degree of discretion it had in sentencing appellant, the sentence was not excessive. Given the minimum nature of the sentence imposed, the prior felony conviction, and the benefit gained by appellant through the plea bargain, the penalty imposed was not so grossly disproportionate to the severity of the crime.


OUTCOME: Sentence affirmed. Trial court did not err in granting the State's motion and resentencing appellant. The automatic pardon provision did not preclude consideration of her prior conviction. Further, the sentence imposed was not excessive as to shock the sense of justice.

Bally's La., Inc. v. Louisiana Gaming Control Bd.


No. 1999 CA 2617


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


1999 2617 (La.App. 1 Cir. 1/31/01); 807 So. 2d 257; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 126



January 31, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 459,170. Honorable Jewel E. "Duke" Welch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor appealed from the judgment of the District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, whereby a permanent injunction was issued enjoining defendant, the Louisiana Gaming Control Board, from enforcing its escrow orders relating to plaintiff's gaming revenues.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, part owner and manger of a casino, appealed the order of defendant, the Louisiana Gaming Control Board, that the casino's gross revenues be escrowed, arguing that the Board's actions were an unconstitutional taking without due process. Intervenor, a joint owner of the casino, intervened, but the trial court quashed its subpoenas ex parte. At a hearing on plaintiff's motion for a preliminary injunction, the trial court granted the injunction and, at the request of plaintiff and defendant, but over intervenor's objections, made the injunction permanent and dismissed the case as moot. Intervenor appealed; the appellate court reversed. The trial court had no authority to convert the preliminary injunction to a permanent one over intervenor's objection, or to quash intervenor's subpoenas ex parte. It improperly heard both plaintiff's appeal and its preliminary injunction request, acting as an appeals court in the former matter, and as a trial court in the latter. The injunctive relief request was ordered severed from the petition for judicial review. The orders quashing intervenor's subpoenas, and dismissing the judicial review petition, were also reversed.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded. Plaintiff's injunctive relief request was severed from its petition for judicial review, remanded to the trial court, and randomly re-allotted for further proceedings. The trial court's orders quashing intervenor's subpoenas were reversed. As to the petition for judicial review, the case was remanded to the trial court which was to order the Board to hold a hearing under La. Rev. Stat. § 27:25.

State v. Williams


No. 99-KA-1868


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-1868 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/31/01); 778 So. 2d 1232; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 203



January 31, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 23, 2001.
Writ denied by State v. Williams, 807 So. 2d 227, 2002 La. LEXIS 217 (La., Jan. 11, 2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Williams v. Cooper, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 64877 (E.D. La., Aug. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH NO. 403-700, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment, based upon a jury verdict, of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) convicting him of manslaughter and sentencing him to 40 years in prison at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took his new girlfriend to meet the woman, victim, with whom he was living. After an argument between defendant and the victim, the latter was shot. The victim died of a single gunshot wound from a bullet that entered her heart. The shot was fired from close range. The victim also had multiple bruises on her head, elbows, and forearms. At the police station, defendant made two tape-recorded statements, which were later played for the jury. In the first statement, he admitted shooting the victim, but claimed it was an accident. About an hour later, defendant stated he did not just run away after the shooting, but rather he tried to help the victim first. He was convicted of manslaughter. Judgment was affirmed. The jury's credibility determinations and subsequent conclusion that the shooting was not accidental were not contrary to the evidence. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of defendant's ammunition and weapons paraphernalia, as it was relevant to defendant's credibility. Remarks made by the prosecutor during closing argument were all within the scope of proper argument. Sentence imposed was not excessive.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Based in part on defendant's poor credibility, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the manslaughter conviction. Defendant was not prejudiced by allegedly improper remarks made by the prosecutor in closing argument, as the prosecutor's remarks were supported by the evidence. Defendant's sentence was not excessive in light of sentences imposed by other courts in similar circumstances.

State v. Stevenson


00-KA-1296


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-1296 (La.App. 5 Cir. 01/30/01); 778 So. 2d 1165; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 75



January 30, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, DOCKET NO. 99-5385, DIVISION "K". HONORABLE MARTHA E. SASSONE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with one count of crime against nature, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89. Defendant moved to quash, on the ground that the statute under which she was charged was unconstitutional. The 24th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) denied the motion. Defendant reserved her right to appeal, after pleading guilty, the trial court's denial of her motion to quash.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant asserted three assignments of error, all regarding the length of defendant's sentence: 1) the trial judge failed to comply with the sentencing guidelines in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1; 2) the trial court erred in imposing an excessive sentence; and 3) defendant was denied effective assistance of counsel at sentencing because her counsel failed to object to the sentence and failed to file a motion to reconsider sentence with the trial court. Pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.2A(2), defendant could not now seek review of her sentence, to which she agreed prior to her plea. The trial court incorrectly advised defendant that she had a three-year time period in which to seek post-conviction relief. However, at the time of sentencing, the time period had been shortened to two years. The trial court needed to inform the defendant of the correct provisions of the statute, by sending appropriate written notice to defendant within ten days of the opinion, and to file written proof in the record that defendant received such notice.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed for the trial court to inform the defendant of the correct time period for filing a claim of post-conviction relief.

Crooks v. Metropolitan Life Ins. Co.


No. 00-0947


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


00-0947 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/17/01); 779 So. 2d 966; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 9



January 17, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Amended January 31, 2001. Released for Publication March 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES [NO. 187,832]. HONORABLE DONALD JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sued defendants for damages as a result of plaintiffs' exposure to asbestos. The Ninth Judicial District Court Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) granted defendants' motion for summary judgment dismissal of the case. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued, inter alia, that medical monitoring existed as a valid cause of action at the time their suit was filed, which was prior to the legislature's adoption of an amendment to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315, which prohibited medical monitoring as a cause of action. Plaintiffs claimed that the amendment to art. 2315 created new law and that its application to their cause of action deprived them of a constitutionally vested right because it was written after the filing of their suit. The appellate court reversed the trial court's decision, concluding that the statutory amendment made a substantive change in the law. Thus, the amendment could not be applied retroactively so as to deprive plaintiffs in this case of their vested rights.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment reversed and case remanded for further proceedings. Statutory amendment prohibiting medical monitoring as a cause of action made a substantive change in the law and could not be applied retroactively so as to deprive plaintiffs of their vested rights.

 

1745 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Kruger v. Garden Dist. Ass'n


No. 2000-CA-1135


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


00-1135 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/11/01); 779 So. 2d 986; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 149



January 17, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied February 15, 2001. Released for Publication February 15, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 99-4685, DIVISION "N-8". Honorable Ethel Simms Julien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE:  La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9092 created appellant Garden District's Security Special Taxing District and a tax. The district court found § 33:9092 unconstitutional and granted appellees, tenant and company, a preliminary injunction of implementation of its tax. On suspensive appeal, the Louisiana Supreme Court vacated the unconstitutionality finding and transferred the matter to the court for a determination as to the preliminary injunction.


OVERVIEW:  La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9092 created appellant Garden District's Security Special Taxing District, designated the composition of its board of directors, and authorized a five-year property tax on property within the district provided that voters approved it, which they did. Appellees, tenant and company, alleged § 33:9092 to be unconstitutional and were granted a preliminary injunction suspending implementation of the tax. The court vacated the injunction and remanded. There was neither irreparable injury nor a due process violation sufficient to justify the injunction. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2110, unlawful levying of a tax was fully compensable in money. Enjoining appellant possibly would have led to citizens being subject to various crimes such as battery, which would be difficult to compensate with money. Thus, under a duty-risk analysis, the injunction was unwarranted. The court restricted St. Raymond v. City of New Orleans, 769 So. 2d 562, which required no showing of irreparable harm where the action sought to be enjoined directly violated a vested "state property" right, to its specific facts involving construction and building permit revocation.


OUTCOME: Judgment was vacated and the matter remanded. Appellees made no showing of a sufficient due process violation or irreparable harm. An unlawful tax could be compensated with money. Enjoining appellant might have led to more serious and difficult-to-compensate harms to citizens. The court restricted the holding of a pertinent case cited by appellees.

1747 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Briscoe


No. 99-KA-1841


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-KA-1841 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/17/01); 779 So. 2d 30; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 156



January 17, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 399-719, SECTION "G". HONORABLE JULIAN A. PARKER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED,  REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with possession of cocaine. The trial court denied the defendant's motion to suppress the evidence. Defendant was found guilty of attempted possession of cocaine. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) adjudicated the defendant a third-felony habitual offender and sentenced the defendant to life imprisonment at hard labor. The trial court granted the defendant's motion for appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the trial court erred in admitting irrelevant evidence consisting of 2 AK 47 assault rifles, boxes of ammunition for the guns, drug paraphernalia, 2 plastic bags containing a total of 40 pieces of crack cocaine, and several bags of powdered cocaine. Defendant was barred from raising this issue on appeal. Considering that defense counsel allowed all of this testimony concerning the firearms and contraband, it could not be said that the defendant was prejudiced by the routine admission of physical evidence. The appellate court could not say that trial counsel's failure to attack a prior guilty plea at the trial court level prejudiced the defendant. As to whether defendant's sentences were excessive, defendant's three offenses were nonviolent drug offenses and were not sufficient alone to declare his sentence excessive. The record suggested that the defendant was simply a drug addict who might not be deserving of the minimum mandatory life sentence provided by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii).


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but the sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing. The appellate remanded the case for a hearing at which the defendant could show by clear and convincing evidence that the mandatory sentence was unconstitutionally excessive as applied to him.

 

1748 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


No. 2000-KA-0013


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


00-0013 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/09/01); 777 So. 2d 1252; 2001 La. App. LEXIS 139



January 10, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 2, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 394-080, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) denying his motion for new trial after a jury convicted him of two counts of first degree robbery. After adjudicating defendant a second felony offender on each count, the trial court sentenced defendant to serve 30 years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence on each count, to be served consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of twice robbing a video store where he had once worked. The cashier on duty during both robberies gave police a general description of the suspect. The cashier and defendant had worked two shifts together at the video store when defendant was briefly employed there as a security guard. Defendant denied involvement in the robberies. He did, however, admit ownership of a ring identified by the cashier as the ring worn by the perpetrator. On appeal, defendant contended the State failed to prove his identity as the person who committed the crimes. Defendant's conviction was affirmed, as the cashier positively identified defendant. In addition, the jury was able to view the store's surveillance videotapes from both robberies. Defendant's sentences were vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing because the sentences were imposed before defendant's motions for new trial and post verdict judgment of acquittal were disposed of. Defendant's adjudications and sentences as a second felony offender were reversed, as the State failed to produce sufficient evidence to prove that a prior guilty plea on a narcotics charge was knowingly and voluntarily made.


OUTCOME: Convictions were affirmed, sentences were vacated, and case was remanded for resentencing. Surveillance videotapes of robberies provided sufficient evidence to corroborate store cashier's testimony regarding the identify of perpetrator. The State provided insufficient documentation regarding defendant's alleged prior narcotics offense committed in another state. Thus, the trial court erred when it adjudicated defendant a second felony offender.

 

1749 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Palacios v. Louisiana & Delta R.R., Inc.


No. 00 00971


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


000971 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/02/01); 775 So. 2d 698; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3460



December 29, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied January 31, 2001. Released for Publication January 31, 2001.
Writ denied by Palacios v. 791 So. 2d 653, 2001 La. LEXIS 1202 (La., May 4, 2001)
Related proceeding at Palacios v. 2004 La. LEXIS 1559 (La., Apr. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT PARISH OF IBERIA NO. 80628 JUDGE GERARD B. WATTIGNY.
Palacios v. Louisiana & Delta R.R., 740 So. 2d 95, 1999 La. LEXIS 1703 (La., July 2, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a case arising out of a collision between an automobile and a train, plaintiff sought supervisory relief from a judgment of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court of Iberia (Louisiana), which upheld the constitutionality of 23 U.S.C.S. § 409, thereby precluding plaintiff from discovering certain evidence vital to her case.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff moved to compel the production of records of defendant Department of Transportation and Development pertaining to the railroad crossing where the collision occurred. Defendant opposed the discovery requests on the basis of 23 U.S.C.S. § 409, which regulated discovery and admission of certain reports and surveys of railway highway crossings. Plaintiff challenged the constitutionality of § 409 on two grounds, that application of the statute deprived her of due process and an adequate remedy under U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV, as well as the Louisiana Constitution; and that the statute violated U.S. Const. amend. X and La. Const. art. 12, § 10, which provided that neither the state nor any state agency shall have been immune from suit and liability for injury to person or property. The court upheld the constitutionality of § 409. Defendant was not immune from suit and liability, and plaintiff's constitutional rights to due process and an adequate remedy were not abrogated. Other entities could provide plaintiff with the information she sought.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Federal statute regulating discovery and admission of certain reports and surveys of railway highway crossings was not unconstitutional.

State v. Durant


NUMBER 00-KA-1246


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-1246 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/27/00); 776 So. 2d 1265; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3447



December 27, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 22, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 00-421, DIVISION "I". HONORABLE JO ELLEN GRANT, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of one count of armed robbery and sentenced defendant to 10 years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another man robbed a cab driver of his money at gunpoint and fled. The cab driver gave the police a description of the men and told them the amount of money taken. The police found both men nearby from the description of the clothes they were wearing. An hour after the robbery the police took the cab driver to the men and he identified the men as the robbers. Defendant had approximately the amount of money stolen on him, but the gun was not found. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence. Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and sentenced to 10 years. The court found the identification was admissible. The evidence was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to find beyond a reasonable doubt defendant was guilty of armed robbery. The sentence imposed was proper and the minimum allowed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:64, 14:64.3.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction and sentence was affirmed as the evidence as to the arrest and identification of defendant was admissible into evidence, the evidence at trial was sufficient to support the conviction, and the sentence imposed was proper and the minimum sentence compelled by statute.

Huang v. Louisiana State Bd. of Trustees for State Colleges & Univs.


No. 99 CA 2805


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 2805 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/22/00); 781 So. 2d 1; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3583



December 22, 2000, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 25, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 405529. HONORABLE J. MICHAEL MCDONALD, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which ruled in favor of defendants dismissing plaintiff's claims, which alleged denial of tenure based on national origin, in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1981, 1983, as well as La. Const. art. I, § 12.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed suit against defendants for denial of tenure allegedly based on national origin, in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1981, 1983, as well as La. Const. art. I, § 12. The district court ruled in favor of defendants dismissing plaintiff's claims. On appeal, plaintiff argued the district court erred in that it made incorrect factual findings and conclusions of law and made unreasonable evaluations of credibility. The appellate court affirmed the judgment, finding no reversible error. The appellate court reasoned that, based upon the undisputed facts, the record revealed plaintiff had not proven that there was discrimination on the basis of his national origin or ancestry. The appellate court noted that the overwhelming evidence, as determined by the district court, was that plaintiff was not qualified for his particular position inasmuch as he could not effectively communicate in English; his research was of an inadequate level; and his public service achievements were minimal, if any.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment because the record revealed evidence from which a fact finder could reasonably conclude that defendant's decision to deny tenure was not based on plaintiff's national origin or ancestry.

 

1752 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Dennis v. Finish Line, Inc.


99 CA 1413 c/w 99 CA 1414


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 1413 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/22/00); 781 So. 2d 12; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3566



December 22, 2000, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 25, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Docket No. 91-11957 c/w 91-12668. Honorable Donald M. Fendlason, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; AMENDED IN PART AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated personal injury cases arising out of a two-car collision, plaintiffs sued each other and multiple defendants. After some of the defendants were dismissed based on settlements, the 22nd Judicial District Court Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana, apportioned fault between plaintiffs, defendant driver, defendant bar, and defendant state agency. Plaintiffs and defendant state agency appealed.


OVERVIEW: Employees of defendant bar placed a passed-out patron, defendant driver, in his car. Later that night, plaintiff bartender followed defendant driver as he drove away. Defendant driver crossed the center line of a highway, causing plaintiff driver to swerve off the road. Plaintiff driver swerved back onto the road and collided with plaintiff bartender. In consolidated cases, plaintiffs sued defendants for their injuries, and the trial court apportioned damages. The appellate court reversed the allocation of fault to defendant bar because a causal link to establish the liability of defendant bar was not established. The court re-allocated the fault, placing fault on plaintiff driver for imprudently swerving back onto the road and placing fault on defendant state agency and defendant driver. The court determined that there was no limitation on defendant state agency's liability for general damages and that the general damage awards were not excessive. However, the court reversed the awards for loss of future earning capacity. Also, due to the pre-trial settlement between the plaintiffs, defendant state agency was solidarily liable for only 50 percent of plaintiffs' damages.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed regarding apportionment of fault and awards for loss of future earning capacity, but was affirmed regarding general damage awards.

Batson v. S. La. Med. Ctr.


NUMBER 98 CA 0038R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0038R (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/22/00); 778 So. 2d 54; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3553



December 22, 2000, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of error denied Batson v. South 792 So. 2d 740, 2001 La. LEXIS 1329 (La., May 11, 2001)
Appeal after remand at Batson v. S. La. Med. Ctr., 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1950 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Thirty-second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Terrebonne, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 101,385. Honorable John R. Walker, Judge Presiding.
Batson v. S. 750 So. 2d 949, 1999 La. LEXIS 3237 (La., Nov. 19, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees sued for life threatening complications and extensive disability suffered under appellants' care. The trial court determined, and the Louisiana Supreme Court affirmed, that three separate $ 500,000 caps on damages, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39(F) of the Medical Liability for State Services Act (MLSSA) applied to appellees' claims. The supreme court remanded for quantum review of the damage awards under each cap.


OVERVIEW: Appellee patient underwent a routine surgical procedure. Because treating physicians failed to prescribe antibiotics, appellee patient developed sepsis, a life threatening complication which led to multi-organ system failure. During months of hospitalization appellee patient developed numerous and extensive decubitus ulcers, bed sores, due to the failure of the nursing staff to reposition her. She also developed severe flexion contractures of the hips, knees and ankles, from lack of proper orthopedic care and physical therapy. Appellees, the patient and her parents, sued. The supreme court determined that a separate $ 500,000 cap on damages as set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39(F) applied to each independent act of negligence with caused appellee patient's sepsis and related injuries, her flexion contractures and her decubitus ulcers, and remanded to the appellate court for a full quantum review of the damage awards under each cap. The appellate court found that considering the multitude of complications, the degree of resulting pain and suffering, and the resulting disability, there was no abuse of discretion in any of the trial court's damage awards.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's damage awards arising from acts of malpractice which resulted in sepsis and related injuries, flexion contractures and decubitus ulcers. The appellate court remanded the issue of whether appellants were entitled to a credit against the amounted they owed on the flexion contractures claim, as a result of a settlement between appellees and other defendants because it required a factual determination.

Jim & Lu Enters., Inc. v. Alcoholic Bev. Control Bd.


No. 99 CA 2907


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 2907 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/22/00); 778 So. 2d 75; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3584



December 22, 2000, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied March 1, 2001. Released for Publication March 1, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 450,399. HONORABLE CURTIS CALLOWAY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff convenience store proprietor appealed denial, by 19th Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), of his petition for damages and injunctive relief after defendant alcoholic beverage control board revoked his liquor license, arguing insufficiency of evidence and denial of due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant local alcoholic beverage control board revoked plaintiff convenience store owner's liquor license after police were called to the store several times. Plaintiff commenced a new action, which was unsuccessful in the trial court, seeking damages and an injunction, arguing that defendant revoked his license based on insufficient evidence and that he did not receive due process at his hearing. The court held that plaintiff's action was in essence an appeal of the administrative proceeding rather than an independent action. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4788 required that an appeal of a trial court's decision in a liquor license had to be filed within 10 days and that an appeal from a judgment relating to a preliminary injunction had to be taken within 15 days. Since plaintiff failed to meet either deadline, the court lacked jurisdiction to hear his appeal at all.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff's appeal as untimely, because he failed to file within either the 10-day period required for liquor license appeals or the 15-day period for proceedings involving injunctions.

State v. Turner

OVERVIEW: Defendant was the driver of a truck involved in an accident. Upon speaking with him, a deputy noticed a strong odor of alcohol on his breath. 1756 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Farmco, Inc. v. W. Baton Rouge Parish Governing Council


No. 99 CA 2837


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 2837 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/22/00); 808 So. 2d 412; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3593



December 22, 2000, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE EIGHTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF WEST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 29,745. HONORABLE JAMES J. BEST, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Eighteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of West Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, plaintiffs sued to enjoin defendant from enforcing subdivision regulations and to have the regulations declared null and void. Defendant filed an exception raising the objection of no cause of action. The trial court sustained the exception and dismissed the lawsuit. Plaintiff corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that subdivision regulations requiring the installation of fire hydrants were invalid. The trial court found that the regulations were adopted according to law by a governmental body authorized to establish such regulations. The instant court affirmed. The Louisiana Constitution and state statutes gave local governments broad power to adopt regulations for land use. State law designated a "planning commission" as the agency to establish such regulations, but allowed that a home rule charter could avail itself of the authority granted to a planning commission. West Baton Rouge Parish's home rule charter delegated that power to defendant. Thus, defendant was authorized to establish the regulations plaintiffs challenged. Defendant's exception establishes that the adoption of the regulations was as provided by law. Plaintiffs had no remedy available to them, and the trial court was not obligated to allow them to amend their petition where such amendment would be futile.


OUTCOME: Order sustaining a no cause of action exception was affirmed. The parish's home rule charter delegated to defendant the authority to establish zoning regulations, and defendant established the challenged regulations according to law; thus, plaintiffs had no available remedy.

 

1757 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


R.B. Applying for Adoption


No. 00 CJ 2101


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


00 2101 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/22/00); 778 So. 2d 80; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3601



December 22, 2000, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied March 9, 2001. Released for Publication March 9, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 21st Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 9740033. Honorable W. Ray Chutz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father appealed the decision of the 21st Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Tangipoha (Louisiana) which denied his petition to revoke respondents, adoptive parents', adoption of his daughter.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, adoptive parents, filed an application for approval of the adoption of petitioner father's daughter after agreeing with the child's mother and her former husband for the voluntary surrender of the child. Sometime after the child was placed with respondents, petitioner informed respondents that he was the child's biological father and filed a petition for paternity. Respondents then filed an exception on the grounds that petitioner's actions to annul the adoption were untimely. The trial court granted respondents' exception but ordered paternity testing. After tests showed petitioner to be the child's biological father, petitioner filed a petition to revoke respondents' adoption of his daughter. Respondents then filed an exception on the grounds of res judicata. On reconsideration, the trial court granted respondents' exception and dismissed the petition to revoke. The appellate court reversed and remanded. Res judicata applied to the validity of the mother's acts of surrender and not to petitioner's challenge. Petitioner was not precluded by res judicata from challenging the adoption of his daughter.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded. Petitioner father had a right to oppose the adoption of his daughter and the trial court erred when it dismissed his petition on the grounds of res judicata. Res judicata only applied to the validity of the acts of surrender involving the child's mother.

ANR Pipeline Co. v. Louisiana Tax Comm'n


No. 00 CA 2251


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


00 2251 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/22/00); 774 So. 2d 1261; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3558



December 22, 2000, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 25, 2001.
Writ denied by ANR Pipeline Co. v. 790 So. 2d 633, 2001 La. LEXIS 1516 (La., Apr. 20, 2001)
Later proceeding at ANR Pipeline Co. v. 795 So. 2d 1217, 2001 La. LEXIS 2832 (La., Sept. 6, 2001)
Related proceeding at ANR Pipeline Co. v. 811 So. 2d 876, 2002 La. LEXIS 734 (La., Mar. 6, 2002)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 815 So. 2d 178, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 823 (La.App. 1 Cir., Mar. 20, 2002)
Related proceeding at ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 5976 (E.D. La., Jan. 18, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 468,417. Honorable Bob Downing, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pipe line company challenged dismissal by the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, on grounds of no cause of action and prescription, of five of its six claims that appellee had improperly assessed taxes against its public service properties. Each claim was based on a single tax year. The trial court had designated its judgment of prescription as to the five oldest claims final.


OVERVIEW: For 6 years appellee tax commission assessed taxes on appellant's public service property at 25 percent of fair market value. For each of these years appellant paid and filed yearly written protests with appellee. After many delays, appellee dismissed appellant's protests, making the initial determinations final. Appellant pipe line company appealed to the district court. The district court granted appellee's exceptions of no cause of action and prescription, and dismissed appellant's claims as to the five oldest tax years, designating the partial judgment as final. Appellant filed appeal from the partial judgment. The appellate court noted that the legislature had provided two separate remedies, one for public service property, excluding land, and one for all other property subject to taxation. The district court had failed to apply the procedure of review of the tax assessment of public service property. The court found that appellant had properly followed the procedure set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1856 to challenge a public service property assessment by waiting for a final determination by appellee and then filing in district court within 30 days thereafter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district court and remanded the case for further proceedings because the suit had been timely filed under the procedures for challenging assessment of tax against public service properties.

State v. Leger


00 00920-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


00 00920 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/20/00); 775 So. 2d 1169; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3388



December 20, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 22, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWELFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF AVOYELLES. NO. 98,197-A. HONORABLE KERRY L. SPRUILL.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Twelfth Judicial District, Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana), ordering her conviction for arson with intent to defraud.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with arson with intent to defraud in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:53. Defendant appealed, asserting evidence was insufficient to support her conviction. The court rendered a judgment of acquittal. In response to defendant's challenge to the sufficiency of evidence, the court was required to decide whether, after viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crime proven beyond a reasonable doubt. There was no direct evidence linking defendant to the fire. The neighborhood had been the scene of numerous acts of vandalism in the time period of the crime. Moreover, the defendant's belongings were in the house trailer at the time of the fire, including family pictures. There was much testimony regarding the defendant's anguished state after the fire. Defendant's actions were inconsistent with having started the fire.


OUTCOME: Conviction reversed; there was no direct evidence linking defendant to the fire.

Boyd v. St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co.


No. 99-1820


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


99-1820 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/20/00); 775 So. 2d 649; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3386



December 20, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 22, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR SUPERVISORY WRITS OF REVIEW FROM FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 98-5189. HONORABLE GREGORY D. LYONS.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought supervisory writ of review from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu's decision denying defendants' request for protective order in medical malpractice action brought by plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs instituted this action initially asserting that defendant physician committed various acts of malpractice resulting in severe damage and harm to plaintiff husband. Plaintiffs filed a petition with essentially the same malpractice claim presented by them to the Medical Review Panel. The petition named as defendants the estate of the physician, defendant insurer, and defendant Louisiana Patient's Compensation Fund (PCF) as the responsible party over and above any coverage provided by defendant insurer. PCF applied for supervisory writ when its motion for protective order was denied by the trial court. The trial court acted with the great discretion afforded it in allowing the discovery process to proceed in the instant matter. The court was convinced that the Louisiana legislature, by enacting La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.44(D)(4) did not intend to allow the PCF, healthcare providers, and their insurers to thwart the judicial process with impunity or to engaged in conduct prohibited by the Medical Malpractice Act without consequence by shielding their conduct from discovery. The trial court properly denied the request for protective order.


OUTCOME: Supervisory writ denied. Trial court properly denied defendants' motion for protective order. Medical malpractice legislation, and privileges, were not intended to be used to shield conduct.

 

1762 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Webster


No. 98-KA-0807


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-0807 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/27/00); 775 So. 2d 661; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3431



December 20, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied January 12, 2001. Released for Publication January 12, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 390-438, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE REINSTATED; CONVICTION AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In light of one of its recent rulings, Supreme Court of Louisiana remanded case for court to reconsider its decision that life sentence, imposed pursuant to Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii), was excessive punishment for defendant's third-offense, when third offense was purse snatching.


OVERVIEW: In it's first opinion, the court held that the imposition of a life sentence pursuant to the "three strikes" provision of the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii), was excessive for purse snatching. Purse snatching was a "crime of violence" under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:2(13)(z). Defendant had two prior convictions for simple burglary. The trial court found no circumstance permitting it to deviate from the statutorily mandated sentence. The record disclosed nothing indicating the trial judge abused his discretion, albeit during the commission of the crime defendant was unarmed, the victim was not physically harmed, and the victim's property was recovered. By its very nature, the act of snatching a purse involved a physical act that placed the victim at risk for physical injury.


OUTCOME: Original decree vacated, and sentence of life imprisonment reinstated upon defendant. Trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding there were no circumstances permitting it to deviate from minimum sentence mandated by Louisiana Habitual Offender Law; thus life sentence for defendant for crime of purse snatching was proper, because he was habitual offender and purse snatching was crime of violence.

State v. Smith


No. 2000-KA-0523


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-0523 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/20/00); 777 So. 2d 584; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3439



December 20, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 9, 2001.
Writ denied by State v. Smith, 812 So. 2d 663, 2002 La. LEXIS 1267 (La., Apr. 12, 2002)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Smith v. State, 867 So. 2d 679, 2004 La. LEXIS 519 (La., Feb. 13, 2004)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Smith v. State, 897 So. 2d 593, 2005 La. LEXIS 969 (La., Apr. 1, 2005)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Smith v. State, 918 So. 2d 1024, 2006 La. LEXIS 28 (La., Jan. 9, 2006)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Smith v. LeBlanc, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 24450 (E.D. La., Mar. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 409-062, SECTION "J", Honorable Leon Cannizzaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a conviction for aggravated battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:(27)30.1 from Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) which adjudicated the defendant a third felony offender, vacated his original sentence, and sentenced him pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 to life imprisonment at hard labor with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the evidence did not support his conviction of aggravated battery. He argued the State did not disprove he acted in self-defense. The defendant admitted that he and the victim were engaged in an argument over money and that he armed himself with a box cutter and began to swing at the victim. The injury, therefore, was a reasonably certain consequence. The State negated the defendant's justification defense. Defendant claimed the State produced insufficient evidence of his identity for purposes of adjudicating him a third felony offender. Testimony comparing defendant's fingerprints with fingerprints found on prior arrest records was sufficient to prove defendant was the person convicted of the prior offenses. Because defendant's third conviction was for aggravated battery, a crime of violence as defined by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:2(13), the mandatory life sentence as a third felony habitual offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii) was not excessive. Considering his extensive criminal record and propensity for crimes of violence, he fit the profile of the recidivist the Habitual Offender Law was enacted to contain.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. The State negated the defendant's justification defense and proved the defendant's identity as the person who committed the predicate offenses. His life sentence as a third felony offender was not constitutionally excessive.

Metro Riverboat Assocs. v. Louisiana Gaming Control Bd.


99 CA 0863


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 0863 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/20/00); 774 So. 2d 1193; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3537



December 20, 2000, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of May 12, 2000, Reported at: 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2045.



DISPOSITION: DISTRICT COURT DECISION VACATED; APPEAL DISMISSED; WRIT GRANTED AND MADE PEREMPTORY; BOARD RESOLUTION VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Louisiana Gaming Control Board presented an appeal and an application for supervisory review seeking a rehearing of a decision by the Nineteenth Judicial District Court on judicial review of the board's conditional approval of a transfer of an interest in a riverboat gaming license. The court found a transferee was required to receive prior approval before the transfer could take place and ordered the board to conduct a public hearing.


OVERVIEW: The court decided the review of a resolution by the Louisiana Gaming Control Board should have been conducted under its supervisory jurisdiction. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 27:26, 27:89 were read in conjunction with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49 of the Louisiana Administrative Procedure Act to limit appeals from the board to final decisions resulting from adjudications. The district court lacked authority to review the matter on appeal. While remand for exercise of the district court's supervisory jurisdiction was proper, the court accepted the case under its supervisory jurisdiction. Because emergency provisions were not utilized, the board's resolution which purported to "conditionally approve" the transfer of a gaming license was not authorized. Outside the emergency provisions, which were not activated, actual transfer could take place only after prescribed requirements had been met. The district court did not err in ordering the board to conduct a public hearing. To hold otherwise would have been to allow a subsequent transferee of a gaming license to avoid the public scrutiny to which the original licensee or permittee was subjected.


OUTCOME: Resolution of Louisiana Gaming Control Board vacated and remanded for public hearing. Appeal dismissed because resolution was not a final appealable adjudication. Writ granted and made peremptory. Conditional prior approval of transfer of gaming license was not authorized by the gaming provisions; approval of transfer of license could only have been given after prescribed requirements had been met.

 

1765 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of EHM


No. 00 CJ 2705


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


00 2705 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/15/00); 808 So. 2d 397; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3548



December 15, 2000, Judgment Rendered

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant biological father appealed a judgment of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), denying his claim of parental rights to a child and dismissing his opposition to the child's adoption.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, who was incarcerated, raised three alleged evidentiary errors and also alleged the trial court was manifestly erroneous in finding he was an unfit parent and in denying his claim for parental rights. The appellate court concluded that the trial court did not err in: (1) excluding testimony about the relationship between the natural mother and appellant's family; (2) in refusing to allow appellant to introduce a statement made by the natural mother to the district attorney's office, which was inconsistent with a previous statement she made; and (3) in admitting police reports of appellant's arrest into evidence. The trial court did not commit manifest error in finding that appellant failed to provide financial support, food, clothing, shelter, or treatment for the child, either before or after the child's birth; or that appellant was unable to provide an adequate permanent home for the child, and that, based on his past conduct, including criminal convictions for violent crimes, he could pose a risk of substantial harm to the child.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Trial court did not commit manifest error in excluding testimony about the relationship between natural mother and appellant biological father's family or in refusing to allow him to introduce a statement the mother made to the district attorney's office, which was not consistent with a previous statement made by her.

December 13, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 22, 2001.
Writ denied by State v. Dennis, 802 So. 2d 629, 2001 La. LEXIS 3231 (La., Nov. 21, 2001)
Subsequent appeal at, Writ denied by State ex rel. Dennis v. State, 872 So. 2d 1076, 2004 La. LEXIS 1610 (La., May 7, 2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Transferred by State ex rel. Dennis v. State, 23 So. 3d 940, 2009 La. LEXIS 3678 (La., 2009)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Dennis v. State, 139 So. 3d 1020, 2014 La. LEXIS 1165 (La., 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Dennis v. Louisiana, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 94042 (E.D. La., June 25, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA NO. 98-6886, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE WALTER J. ROTHSCHILD, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgement of Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, convicting him of aggravated battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and convicted of aggravated battery, and appealed. The court affirmed. Defendant's objection to a policeman's testimony about defendant's prior statements, on grounds it varied from his testimony at the suppression hearing, was properly denied. Defendant failed to file a motion under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 716(C) for discovery of any statements he made to police, and could not complain of the variance in testimony; in any event, the "variance" was insubstantial. Defendant's claim of insufficiency of the evidence to convict was meritless, as several eyewitnesses identified him as the shooter. Defendant's claim that the battery statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34, was unconstitutionally broad because it did not require that the battery occur without the victim's consent was rejected. Because the battery statute affected conduct, not speech, and conduct that was harmful and controlled by criminal laws, application of the overbreadth doctrine was inappropriate. The court found error patent in the court's failure to inform defendant of the time limits for seeking post-conviction relief and the case was remanded so this notice could be given.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because officer's testimony was properly admitted, as no discovery violation occurred; evidence was sufficient to convict; and the aggravated battery statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad. Case was remanded with instructions to the trial court to advise defendant of time limits for filing motions for post-conviction relief.

In re Adoption of A.P.C.


NUMBER 00-CA-1381


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment by the Juvenile Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) that terminated his parental rights in accordance with La. Child. Code art. 1138.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the biological father to two minor children, sought review of a judgment which terminated his parental rights. On appeal, appellant contended that the juvenile court committed manifest error by terminating his parental rights pursuant to La. Child. Code art. 1138. The appellate court found, however, that appellant had failed to establish a viable relationship with the two children. Specifically, appellant had a significant drinking problem for which he refused to seek treatment or any other established recovery program, appellant and the mother of the children were prone to bouts of violence toward each other, and appellant was not listed on either child's birth certificate as the father in an apparent attempt to avoid having to provide financial support for the children. As such, the judgment of the juvenile court to terminate appellant's parental rights was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the juvenile court was affirmed because appellant failed to demonstrate that he was a fit parent inasmuch as appellant had a significant continued drinking problem, appellant failed to provide support for the children, and appellant failed to provide evidence that he had established a substantial commitment to the children.

December 13, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 6, 2001.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Lewis v. State, 798 So. 2d 966, 2001 La. LEXIS 2935 (La., Oct. 5, 2001)
Writ denied by State v. Lewis, 827 So. 2d 1168, 2002 La. LEXIS 3100 (La., Oct. 25, 2002)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Lewis v. State, 865 So. 2d 723, 2004 La. LEXIS 404 (La., Feb. 6, 2004)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Lewis v. State, 901 So. 2d 1058, 2005 La. LEXIS 1429 (La., Apr. 29, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Lewis v. State, 998 So. 2d 97, 2009 La. LEXIS 2144 (La., Jan. 16, 2009)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Lewis v. State, 2017 La. LEXIS 1124 (La., May 19, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 406-677, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana) convicting him of attempted obscenity, sentencing him to life imprisonment at hard labor, and denying his motion for reconsideration of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted obscenity. He argued that the trial court erroneously adjudicated him to be a fourth felony offender. Defendant did not file a motion to quash the multiple bill or object to the failure of the State to prove that the cleansing periods had not elapsed at the multiple bill hearing; thus, the issue was not preserved for appellate review. The documents presented by the State reflected that 10 years had not passed between each offense, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(C); thus, defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to object based on the cleansing period argument. Defendant had been convicted of seven felonies between 1982 and 1999. Also, the facts indicated that defendant was attempting to force sexual intercourse on the victim. Thus, defendant's sentence to life imprisonment was not unconstitutionally excessive. Defendant's convictions for simple battery and attempted obscenity did not violate his right against double jeopardy because although the two convictions arose from the same transaction, the evidence for each offense was completely separate and distinct. Thus, the two convictions were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; defendant was convicted of attempted obscenity and sentenced to life imprisonment. Trial counsel was not ineffective because an objection on the cleansing period argument would have been denied because 10 years had not passed between the offenses. Defendant's life imprisonment sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive because of his prior felony convictions and the nature of the offense.

No. 00-00580-CA

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the order of the Thirty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson Davis (Louisiana) dismissing their claims premised on the alleged negligence of a government employee on grounds they failed to serve him.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs appealed dismissal of their claims premised on the alleged negligence of a government employee because they failed to timely serve him. The trial court found plaintiffs failed to show good cause for withholding service beyond the 90-day period prescribed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5107(D) and also denied plaintiffs' constitutional challenges to the statute. The former holding was affirmed, while the latter was reversed, based on the premise the court pretermitted the question, on grounds that the question was not ripe. The court was not willing to determine whether the statute was constitutional because said resolution was unnecessary to decide the case. Until plaintiffs filed a second suit naming all the defendants and reasserting the claims which were the subject of the present dismissal, the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5107(D)(3) was not at issue.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment dismissing plaintiffs' claims without prejudice affirmed as plaintiffs could not show good cause why they failed to serve defendant within prescription period. Judgment reversed on that portion addressing the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5107(D)(3) as issue was not ripe for adjudication.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of attempted purse snatching and possession of cocaine, appealed his convictions and his life sentence, imposed because he was a third-time-offender, entered in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted purse snatching, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65.1, and possession of cocaine, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967. The purse snatching offense was considered a violent felony and, based on that and prior convictions, defendant was sentenced as a third-time offender. The State presented sufficient evidence to establish defendant's prior guilty plea was informed and voluntary. Finally, the trial court did not err in refusing to allow defendant to change his plea.


OUTCOME: Convictions and sentence affirmed. Defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive, defense counsel was not ineffective, prosecutor's comments were appropriate under the circumstances of the case, and the trial court committed no error in refusing to allow defendant to change his plea.

No. CR00-983


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT

Writ denied by State ex rel. McCullough v. State, 883 So. 2d 1030, 2004 La. LEXIS 3013 (La., Oct. 8, 2004)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at McCullough v. Cain, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41994 (W.D. La., Jan. 20, 2005)
Writ denied by State ex rel. McCullough v. State, 159 So. 3d 456, 2015 La. LEXIS 259 (La., 2015)
Writ denied by State v. McCullough, 2015 La. LEXIS 2094 (La., Sept. 25, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF RAPIDES [NO. 240,891] HONORABLE WILLIAM POLK, PRO TEMP JUDGE, HONORABLE GEORGE METOYER, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. McCullough, 734 So. 2d 643, 1999 La. LEXIS 109 (La., Jan. 6, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of second-degree murder, and sentence thereon, in the Ninth Judicial District Court, Rapides Parish (Louisiana), arguing primarily that evidence of intent and of presence at the crime scene was insufficient, that trial court erred in denying a change of venue, and that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and several friends were convicted of murdering an elderly woman. Evidence indicated that defendant did not actively help stab the victim, so the jury convicted him of second-degree rather than first-degree murder. The court held that since the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of first-degree murder, it was certainly sufficient to convict him of second-degree murder. Although the case generated considerable publicity, it was not so inflammatory as to raise a presumption of prejudice. Because defendant failed to show actual prejudice, there was no error in denying him a change of venue. There was no error in excluding co-defendants' statements as hearsay, because defendant failed to show that their statements were reliable. Defendant's challenges to rejection of proposed jury instructions failed because the general charge was adequate. Finally, review of defendant's sentence was precluded by his failure to move for reconsideration. However, his life sentence was mandatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment; since evidence was sufficient to prove first-degree murder, it was more than enough for second-degree. Co-defendants' statements were not admissible because they were not shown to be reliable. Publicity was not so inflammatory that court would presume prejudice. Sentence was mandatory, and anyhow, defendant waived review.

Jeter v. Shamblin


No. 34,225-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


34,225 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/06/00); 774 So. 2d 1071; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2979



December 6, 2000, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 436,156-C. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana in her medical malpractice action in favor of defendant physician. The district court rejected her challenge that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 was unconstitutional under the La. Const. art. I, § 3 (1974) equal protection provisions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient had brought a medical malpractice action against defendant physician. An appeal of the action had been remanded for plaintiff to properly raise a constitutional challenge to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 under the La. Const. art. I, § 3 (1974) equal protection provisions. The circuit court rejected her constitutionality challenge, and entered judgment for defendant. Plaintiff appealed. Plaintiff argued § 9:5628 established a per se negligence distinction between defendants who were healthcare professionals and other defendants. The court determined that distinction was not included within the equal protection classes of § 3, which were birth, age, sex, culture, physical condition, or political ideas or affiliations. Therefore to show unconstitutionality plaintiff had to show the § 9:5628 distinction did not have a reasonable basis. The court determined plaintiff did not do that. The legislature's purpose, recognized by a prior case, to reduce the proliferation of malpractice suits to control health care costs, was a legitimate state interest. The statute was constitutional. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The challenge to the statute based on the distinction between per se negligence classification for medical malpractice and other suits did not fall under enumerated constitutionally protected classes. Plaintiff did not prove the statute did not suitably further any appropriate state interest. The stated interest furthered was to reduce proliferation of medical malpractice actions to lower medical costs.

NUMBER 00-818

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From Twenty-Seventh Judicial District, Parish of St. Landry. No. 98-K-3728-D. Honorable Donald Wayne Hebert, District Judge.
