CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of attempted simple robbery in the 27th Judicial District, Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), challenged the sufficiency of the evidence and the constitutionality of his sentence of life without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for attempted simple robbery, and he was charged as a third felony offender. The victim testified that he was surprised, scared, intimidated, and believed the defendant would try to hurt him in order to get his money. Rational trier of fact could have reasonably concluded that the act of jumping into the victim's vehicle and demanding money was a use of force and intimidation sufficient to prove the necessary element of attempted simple robbery. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Evidence was sufficient to show that defendant had the specific intent to take money from the victim by use of force. Other crimes evidence was properly evaluated as circumstantial evidence of defendant's specific intent. Sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment.

Davis v. Dempster, Inc.


NUMBER 00-662


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


00-662 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/29/00); 790 So. 2d 43; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2955



November 29, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal From Thirty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Allen. No. C-94-255. Honorable Joel Gerard Davis, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the Thirty-third Judicial District Court, Parish of Allen's (Louisiana) judgment sustaining defendant parent corporation's exception of lack of personal jurisdiction, in a suit to determine whether sufficient contacts existed with Louisiana for the exercise of personal jurisdiction over defendant parent corporation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendants, alleging that plaintiff employee sustained injuries due to the breaking of a turnbuckle assembly on a waste disposal truck. Defendant manufacturer and defendant parent corporation (parent) each filed exceptions of lack of personal jurisdiction. The trial court denied defendant manufacturer's exception, but sustained defendant parent's exception. Plaintiffs appealed the decision to sustain defendant parent's exception. The appellate court held that the mere existence of a parent-subsidiary relationship between defendant parent and defendant manufacturer would not support the assertion of jurisdiction over defendant parent unless defendant parent so dominated defendant manufacturer that they did not in reality constitute separate and distinct corporate entities. However, plaintiffs failed to establish that defendant parent exercised the degree of control over defendant manufacturer necessary to support an exercise of personal jurisdiction. Plaintiffs also failed to establish the existence of minimum contacts with Louisiana due to the conduct of defendant parent. Consequently, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment sustaining defendant parent corporation's exception of lack of personal jurisdiction was affirmed. Plaintiffs showed only that defendant manufacturer was owned by defendant parent corporation; this, alone, was insufficient to support an exercise of personal jurisdiction. Also, plaintiffs failed to show that the conduct of defendant parent corporation provided the requisite minimum contacts with Louisiana.

Writ denied by State v. Crowell, 826 So. 2d 1112, 2002 La. LEXIS 2901 (La., Oct. 4, 2002)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Augustine v. Cain, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 44179 (E.D. La., July 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 394-135, SECTION "J". Honorable Leon Cannizzaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed respectively their convictions for distribution of heroin and possession of heroin with the intent to distribute, and possession of heroin, both receiving sentences of life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence, one as a third felony offender, by the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana) after their arrest after police surveillance.


OVERVIEW: After a tip concerning drug sales and surveillance of defendant seller transacting, police got a warrant for a house, and after more surveillance searched it and found wrapped heroin. Defendant purchaser who had driven away was also arrested with heroin. Defendants were convicted respectively of distribution of heroin and possession with intent to distribute it, and possession, defendant purchaser as a third felony offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and both life-sentenced. The court affirmed. As defendants were charged differently, there was no possibility of antagonistic defenses; thus joint trial was not improper. Warrant was justified because surveillance corroborated informant's detailed tip. Evidence sufficiently showed intent to distribute, and police reports' discrepancies were unrelated to elements of crimes. Guilty plea and waiver of rights forms to previous offenses showed defendant purchaser's guilty pleas to predicate offenses had been voluntary. Thus defendant purchaser's trial counsel was not deficient for failing to move to quash the multiple bills of information. As state did not raise issue, illegally lenient sentence was not corrected.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Warrant and joinder of defendants were proper as surveillance corroborated informant's detailed tip and defenses were not antagonistic. Evidence sufficiently showed intent to distribute, and previous offenses' guilty plea and waiver of rights forms showed defendant purchaser's guilty pleas to habitual offender predicate offenses had been informed; thus his counsel was not deficient for failing to move to quash.

Becnel v. Lafayette Ins. Co.


No. 99-CA-2966


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-2966 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/15/00); 773 So. 2d 247; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2891



November 15, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM PLAQUEMINES 25TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NO. 42-673, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE MICHAEL E. KIRBY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer challenged a judgment of the Plaquemines 25th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), awarding the sum of $ 11,048, plus penalties and attorney fees, to plaintiff insured after defendant failed to pay full claim amount for hail damage to roofs of plaintiff's house and barn.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contacted defendant claiming the roofs of his house and barn were damaged in a hail storm. Defendant retained a property damage adjuster to inspect the damage. The adjuster found extensive damage and estimated the repairs would have cost $ 15,646. Believing the roofs had sustained only minor damage, defendant retained a roof inspector to assess plaintiff property for hail damage. The inspector found damage to only 13 shingles and estimated replacement costs at $ 480. In light of the inspector's opinion, defendant refused to pay plaintiff for the replacement of the roofs. Dissatisfied, plaintiff obtained another estimate of the damage. This third assessor recommended both roofs be replaced. Defendant failed to make any additional payments. Plaintiff successfully sued defendant. Upon review, the court found defendant's handling of plaintiff's claim was arbitrary and capricious and therefore warranted the assessment of penalties and attorney fees. Defendant arbitrarily chose to ignore the appraisal of plaintiff's loss by its own appraiser. Judgment was amended to award interest on statutory penalties from date of legal judgment rather than from date of judicial demand.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed as amended; defendant's failure to pay plaintiff's hail damage claim, even after a third appraisal was done estimating that the roofs needed replacement, was arbitrary and capricious. Penalties and attorney fees were appropriately awarded in favor of plaintiff. Trial court's judgment was amended to award interest on penalties from date of judgment.

 

1778 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carter


No. 99-KA-0779


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-0779 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/15/00); 773 So. 2d 268; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2894



November 15, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 394-797, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish's (Louisiana) denial of his motion to suppress, his conviction for possession of heroin in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(C)(1), his adjudication as a third felony habitual offender, and his sentence purportedly pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii) to life imprisonment without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence, with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Eight police officers went to investigate a drug selling complaint. Upon arrival, an officer saw a man handing defendant money and defendant holding a plastic bag with several white objects and tin foil. Defendant fled, was caught, and found to have a syringe and bottle cap. Defendant said he was selling fake cocaine for his heroin habit. Residue in the bottle cap and foil, too small to weigh, tested positive for heroin. Defendant was convicted of possession of heroin, adjudicated a third felony habitual offender, and sentenced to life (not without the possibility of parole). The court affirmed. Police had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant. Though the amount of heroin was negligible, it supported the conviction. Defendant could be paroled after 20 years under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(A)(3), so his sentence was not cruel. Defendant's prior two felonies were not drug related or caused; thus, he was not sentenced for being an addict. Defendant had four prior convictions, an extensive juvenile record, and offered no evidence as to his redeeming qualities; his sentence, even if harsh, was not excessive.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence were affirmed. Non-weighable amount of heroin was adequate for possession conviction. Defendant admitted he was a heroin addict and had been trying to complete a fake drug sale to support his habit. Defendant's sentence allowed for the possibility of parole, he had made no showing of redeeming qualities, and his prior record was extensive; thus the sentence was justified.

State v. Toney


No. 99-KA-1574


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-1574 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/08/00); 796 So. 2d 1; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2805



November 8, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 28, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 397-762, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting and sentencing him, as a second felony offender, for possession of a firearm by a convicted felon and for possession of heroin. The trial court had denied defendant's motions to suppress a statement and evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in his aunt's home based on a warrant. In a search incident to the arrest, an officer found a syringe with heroin residue on defendant, who was arrested a second time. A rifle magazine with live rounds in it was subsequently found in the bedroom defendant had been occupying. When questioned, defendant denied any knowledge of an assault rifle, but he stated the drugs and the handgun belonged to him. A more detailed search of the bedroom revealed, inter alia, 10 packets of heroin and a handgun. Defendant wanted his statement and the drug and weapon evidence suppressed. He argued he was not able to voluntarily waive his rights as he was intoxicated from the heroin he had recently ingested. Upon review, the court found that because defendant was alert enough to communicate with arresting officers without any problems, he was not so intoxicated that he could not have comprehended the consequences of his acts. Defendant's statement gave the officers probable cause to conduct a continued search of the bedroom. Finally, the syringe containing heroin residue that was found on defendant's person was sufficient to sustain the possession of heroin conviction.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed; evidence presented at suppression hearing and at trial was insufficient to prove that defendant's alleged intoxication at time of arrest was sufficient to vitiate the voluntariness of his incriminating statement to police. Because officers had information that defendant, a convicted felon and parolee, was in possession of a weapon, they had probable cause to search bedroom which defendant had been occupying.

Post-conviction proceeding at State ex rel. Morris v. State, 925 So. 2d 1252, 2006 La. LEXIS 1136 (La., Mar. 31, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Morris v. Cain, 2008 U.S. App. LEXIS 18287 (5th Cir. La., Aug. 20, 2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Morris v. Cain, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 52378 (M.D. La., Apr. 22, 2010)
Application denied by State ex rel. Morris v. State, 2012 La. LEXIS 1466 (La., May 18, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 5-98-59. Honorable Donald Johnson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, convictions and sentences for possession of firearm by convicted felon, four counts of armed robbery, aggravated kidnapping, and second degree murder, with concurrent prison sentences, all at hard labor, life sentences to be followed by other concurrent sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two others robbed a supermarket early one morning. All were armed. One remained in the car. Defendant and the other entered the store and committed the robbery, but police arrived while they were there. Defendant left through the back, kidnapping an arriving employee. The other two drove away but soon wrecked the car and were arrested. Defendant was arrested the next day, after the employee's body was found. Her vehicle was found near his house. He was convicted of armed robbery, illegal firearms possession, kidnapping, and second-degree murder, and sentenced to hard labor on each count, with concurrent sentences consecutive to life sentences for the kidnap-murder. The appellate court affirmed, upheld the lower court rulings, finding the evidence against him overwhelming and the sentences justified.


OUTCOME: Convictions and sentences were affirmed. Totality of evidence was overwhelmingly sufficient to establish defendant's guilt. Any prejudice from defendant's prior conviction was too remote to matter. Denying change of venue or other motions was not abuse of discretion. Consecutive sentences were justified, as defendant kidnapped and murdered victim after completing other crimes.

State v. Scott


00 KA 0337


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


00 0337 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/03/00); 769 So. 2d 1286; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2917



November 3, 2000, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 7, 2000.
Subsequent appeal at State v. Scott, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2342 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 10-97-674. Honorable William A. Morvant, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED AND REMANDED TO THE TRIAL COURT FOR A HEARING ON SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, entered in the 19th Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), for possession of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C), and his habitual offender adjudication and life sentence, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for possession of cocaine and sentenced to life as a habitual offender, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii). On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, the trial court erred in imposing an unconstitutionally excessive sentence upon him and in failing to advise him of his constitutional rights prior to the commencement of the habitual offender hearing. Further, defendant argued his counsel was ineffective due to lack of knowledge of the case. The court affirmed the conviction, noting that defendant waived formal arraignment on the habitual offender bill, and thus, gave up his right to advice of his habitual offender rights. Additionally, the court determined the record did not support defendant's claim's of his counsel's unfamiliarity with his case. However, the court considered certain peculiar factors, including the allegation that defendant was mentally disabled, to be significant and important enough to justify remanding the matter for the purpose of allowing the trial court to receive evidence and determine whether sufficient grounds existed to depart from the mandatory life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because the record did not support defendant's claim's of ineffective assistance of counsel. However, the court remanded the case for a hearing on sentencing because certain factors of the case were significant and important enough to justify remanding the matter for determination of whether sufficient grounds existed to depart from the mandatory life sentence.

 

1782 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Huddleston v. Farmers-Merchants Bank & Trust Co.


No. 00-640


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


00-640 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/02/00); 772 So. 2d 356; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2741



November 2, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ST. MARTIN [NO. 54,781]. HONORABLE DON CHARLES L. PORTER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana) finding that the action had been abandoned and ordering a dismissal under amended La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 561, which allowed for a case to be considered abandoned if the parties failed to take any steps in its prosecution or defense for three years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was served with notice of the petition almost five years after the filing of the lawsuit and responded by pleading exceptions of no right of action, no cause of action, and abandonment. Plaintiff contended her constitutional rights of due process were violated because of the retroactive application of the amendment to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 561 which changed the statute of limitations from five years to three years. The legislature provided for a delay of one year before the amended form of the article was to become effective. This provision gave those who were to be affected by the change in the law the opportunity to take whatever actions were necessary to preserve their rights. Plaintiff had adequate notice of the impending change in the law and was not deprived of a vested right. Thus, retroactive application of La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 561 did not deprive plaintiff of any constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. A statute did not violate the constitutional prohibition against divesting a vested right provided it allowed a reasonable time for those affected by the act to assert their rights. Allowing one year from the date of enactment before enforcement of the new three year statute of limitations was reasonable and retroactive application did not deprive plaintiff of any constitutional rights.

State v. Dabney


No. 00-KA-109


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-109 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/31/00); 772 So. 2d 247; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2660



October 31, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 18, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-4825, DIVISION "K". HONORABLE MARTHA E. SASSONE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Twenty-fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, of a crime against nature arguing that the statute under which he was convicted failed to make clear on its face what behavior was proscribed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the offense of solicitation of a named woman with the intent to engage in indiscriminate unnatural carnal copulation for compensation. At trial, defendant filed a motion to quash the bill of information on the grounds that the statute under which he was charged was unconstitutional. After the trial court denied his motion, defendant tendered a plea of guilty and reserved his right to appeal. Defendant appealed, raising as a sole error that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89(A)(2) was unconstitutionally vague, because it failed to make clear on its face exactly what behavior was proscribed. The court agreed with, and was bound by, the conclusion reached by the Louisiana Supreme Court and a long line of jurisprudence, that § 14:89(A)(2) was not unconstitutionally vague. It remanded the case however, to allow the district court to correct the error of having failed to advise defendant of the prescriptive period for post conviction relief. Defendant's conviction was affirmed, and the case remanded for correction of error patent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, on finding that statute was not unconstitutional, but remanded for the district court to give defendant appropriate notice of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief.

Williams v. Jackson Parish Hosp.


No. 33,847-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


33,847 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/20/00); 768 So. 2d 866; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2550



October 20, 2000, Rendered

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In medical malpractice action, plaintiff appealed a judgment from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson (Louisiana) denying her challenge to the constitutionality of the three-year rule of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed suit when she was diagnosed with hepatitis C in 1996 against defendants hospital and blood center, alleging that she contracted the disease in 1980, when she was given a blood transfusion during childbirth. Hepatitis C was a disease with a latency period of greater than three years. The attorney general was included in the action because the plaintiff attacked the constitutionality of the three-year prescriptive period of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. Since plaintiff failed to specifically plead with particularity her additional claims of unconstitutionality, her additional claims were not properly before the court.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff's challenge to the constitutionality of the statute barring her medical malpractice claim brought after three years affirmed, even though plaintiff's disease had latency period of greater than three years.

 

1785 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. 33,791-KA, No. 33,877-KW (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


33,791 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/20/00); 771 So. 2d 798; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2551



October 20, 2000, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 201,359. Honorable Leon Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ GRANTED and made peremptory. The conviction is AFFIRMED. The sentence is REVERSED and a sentence of life without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence is imposed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Caddo Parish District Court (Louisiana) convicting him of battery of a police officer in a correctional facility in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.2(B)(2). The State appealed defendant's sentence of 27 years at hard labor as a habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for striking an officer while incarcerated and sentenced as a habitual offender to 27 years at hard labor. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because the State's witnesses testified that the attack occurred while defendant was an inmate at the correctional center. While the trial court erred by failing to instruct the jury on the lesser-included offense of simple battery and by failing to list attempted battery as a responsive verdict, the error was harmless because defendant failed to prove that he was prejudiced by the error. The court reversed defendant's sentence, because there was no clear and convincing evidence showing that defendant was exceptional and therefore was entitled to a lesser sentence than that mandated for habitual offenders. Defendant caused serious bodily injury to the officer by breaking his nose and did not admit to his crimes by entering an Alford plea to his previous manslaughter conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed because the evidence was sufficient and because the trial court committed harmless error by failing to instruct the jury on a lesser-included offense. Defendant's sentence was reversed and a sentence of life without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence was imposed.

State v. Baker

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, on one court of attempted possession of cocaine and his sentence to life imprisonment at hard labor as a multiple offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for attempted possession of cocaine. His appeal was granted. At a subsequent hearing on a multiple bill, defendant's original sentence was vacated and he was sentenced to life imprisonment. The trial court ordered that the multiple bill proceedings be incorporated into the appeal. Preliminarily, the court noted that defendant's sentence was illegally lenient, but could not have been corrected on appeal. As to the glass pipe with cocaine residue which defendant was seen to discard while sitting on a porch, the court found that as it was visible to any casual visitor, the officer's observation of it did not violate any reasonable expectation of privacy in the porch or adjacent yard. Ann. art. 894.1, and there was an adequate factual basis for the multiple offender sentence. Because the evidence reflected that defendant was a 35 year-old with a history of violent crimes and a total inability to change his life, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

State v. Hall


No. 99-KA-2887


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-2887 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/04/00); 775 So. 2d 52; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2600



October 4, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 1, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 406-537, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting him of possession of cocaine under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C), and sentencing him to 3 years at hard labor, suspended, and 3 years probation with 10 special conditions, including the payment of $ 1,000 to the "judicial expense fund."


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to possession of cocaine under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C). He was sentenced to 3 years at hard labor, suspended, and 3 years probation with 10 special conditions, including the payment of $ 1,000 to the "judicial expense fund." Defendant appealed. The appellate court, first, affirmed defendant's conviction, ruling that defendant's motion to suppress evidence was properly denied, because the police officers--albeit without a warrant--had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant. Second, the appellate court vacated defendant's sentence insofar as it ordered defendant to pay $ 1,000 to the "judicial expense fund," because: (1) pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 895.1, payment had to be made to the "criminal court fund"; and (2) the trial court had waived all costs. Third, the appellate court affirmed defendant's sentence in all other respects, because defendant failed to show that the conditions imposed upon his probation were financially excessive or that they militated against the success of his probation. Finally, the appellate court remanded the case so that the $ 1,000 could be made payable to the "criminal court fund."


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, because there was reasonable suspicion to stop defendant. Defendant's sentence was vacated insofar as it directed defendant to pay $ 1,000 to the "judicial expense fund" rather than the "criminal court fund." The case was remanded for correction of the sentence to reflect that the $ 1,000 be made payable to the "criminal court fund." Defendant's sentence was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Burnett


No. 33,739-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


33,739 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/4/00); 768 So. 2d 783; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2260



October 4, 2000, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 189,914. Honorable Ramona Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Caddo Parish District Court, Louisiana, convicting him of sexual battery and oral sexual battery, adjudicating him as a fourth felony offender, and sentencing him to life imprisonment and 10 years' imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to sexual battery and oral sexual battery. The trial court adjudicated him as a fourth felony offender and sentenced him to life imprisonment. The court affirmed. The trial court did not err by denying appellant's motion to quash the habitual offender bill of information because appellant failed to present evidence showing that his rights were infringed upon or that there was a procedural irregularity when he pleaded guilty to a previous armed robbery. Based on appellant's violent criminal history, the court held his sentence was not excessive. The trial court did not err by denying appellant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea without a hearing because it was not required to hold a hearing as appellant failed to present any evidence showing his plea was not knowingly and intelligently made because he misunderstood the venue issue. Appellant's plea was not rendered involuntary because the trial court failed to advise him of the sex offender registration requirements.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because appellant failed to show that his guilty plea to a prior armed robbery charge infringed on his rights or had a procedural irregularity, appellant's sentence was not excessive, and appellant failed to show that his guilty plea was involuntary based upon his misunderstanding of venue.

 

1790 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hurst


No. 99 KA 2868


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 2868 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/03/00); 797 So. 2d 75; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2563



October 3, 2000, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 02-97-482. Honorable Michael Erwin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction for manslaughter, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31, and sentence to 20 years at hard labor from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana.


OVERVIEW: The facts established the defendant, although perhaps initially provoked by the victim, was the aggressor at the time of the killing. The court correctly held the proposed testimony of the victim's bad or overt acts toward the defendant inadmissible. Any slight probative value of the testimony was substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice, confusion of the issues, misleading the jury, undue delay, and waste of time. Self-defense was not supported by the evidence at trial, and thus the defendant was not entitled to a self-defense jury instruction. The defense presented no indicia of the defendant's insanity at the time of the offense, and thus failed to show good cause for a change of plea. There was no error in the denial of the motion to suppress the victim's statements on the 911 tape, since they were not hearsay. The statements were made under the immediate pressure of the crime, were not a narration of the crime after its occurrence, and formed one continuous transaction in conjunction with the crime. The trial court adequately considered the statutory criteria and did not manifestly abuse its discretion in imposing the sentence.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. There was no evidence defendant was in imminent danger of losing her life or receiving great bodily harm and she had to kill the victim to save herself. Any prejudice to defendant's confrontation rights caused by playing of victim's statements concerning stabbing certainly was not unfair. Sentence was not grossly disproportionate to the severity of the offense, and thus was not unconstitutionally excessive.

 

1791 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Watters v. Department of Transp. & Dev.


No. 33,870-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


33,870 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/27/00); 768 So. 2d 733; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2199; 25 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1531



September 27, 2000, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 94-526. Honorable Benjamin Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee benefit plan challenged the judgment of the Morehouse Parish District Court, Louisiana, granting appellee employee's motion for summary judgment dismissing appellant's petition of intervention seeking reimbursement for medical benefits it paid for appellee's daughter from appellee's recovery from the state.


OVERVIEW: When appellee's daughter was seriously injured in an automobile accident, appellant paid the medical bills. Appellant recovered a portion of its expenditures from a settlement obtained from the negligent driver. When appellee sued the state, appellant petitioned to recover the remainder of its expenditures. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment dismissing appellant's petition. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court did not err by finding that appellant was not entitled to subrogation from the settlement between appellee and the state because the medical insurance policy between appellee and appellant provided only a right of subrogation against a liability insurer, and the state was statutorily excluded from the definition of "insurer." No donation of a public thing in violation of La. Const. art. VII, § 14 occurred because an insurance contract existed between appellee and appellant, and when appellee's daughter became sick, appellant was obligated to pay her medical expenses.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the medical insurance policy between appellee and appellant did not provide appellant a right of subrogation against the state, and because appellant was obligated to pay appellee's daughter's medical bills under the parties' insurance contract.

 

1792 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chisolm


No. 99-KA-1055


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-1055 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/27/00); 771 So. 2d 205; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2515



September 27, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 17, 2000.
Writ denied by State v. Chisolm, 798 So. 2d 106, 2001 La. LEXIS 2552 (La., Sept. 28, 2001)
Writ denied by State v. Chisolm, 798 So. 2d 108, 2001 La. LEXIS 2586 (La., Sept. 28, 2001)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Estes v. Cain, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29239 (E.D. La., Feb. 29, 2008)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Chisolm v. State, 2013 La. LEXIS 440 (La., Mar. 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 384-200, SECTION "G". HONORABLE JULIAN A. PARKER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgments of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting them for first degree robbery and adjudicating them as fourth felony offenders and sentencing them to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant female struck up a conversation with victim as he was leaving a bar. While she was talking to him, victim noticed someone enter his vehicle and remove his gun. After that, defendant male approached and said he knew who took the gun and would get it back for victim. The victim later invited defendants back to his house. Defendants partied with victim then left an hour later. The next morning, defendants returned to victim's house. Defendant male put a knife to victim's side and defendants proceeded to rob victim. On appeal, the court found the testimony of victim alone was sufficient to sustain the robbery convictions. Victim's drinking alcohol the night before the robbery did not make his subsequent identifications unreliable. Appellate review of defendant female's claim of excessive sentence was precluded by her failure to file a new motion for reconsideration of sentence after the trial court re-sentenced her as a habitual offender. The trial court did not err in finding the State's proof was sufficient to use defendant male's convictions as predicates in the multiple bill adjudication.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed; victim's testimony provided sufficient evidence to sustain robbery convictions. Further, both victim and follow-up police officer testified that victim identified defendants from photographic lineups, positively and without hesitation. Mandatory life sentence imposed on defendant female was not unconstitutionally excessive and trial court properly concluded defendant male was a fourth felony offender.

 

1793 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Everett


No. 99-KA-1963


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-1963 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/27/00); 770 So. 2d 466; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2517



September 27, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 17, 2000.
Writ granted by State v. Everett, 806 So. 2d 661, 2002 La. LEXIS 377 (La., Jan. 25, 2002)
Reversed by State v. Everett, 816 So. 2d 1272, 2002 La. LEXIS 1510 (La., May 14, 2002)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Everett v. State, 2017 La. LEXIS 1799 (La., Sept. 6, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 402-100, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) convicting him, upon a jury verdict, of aggravated battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34. Defendant also appealed the trial court's judgment adjudicating him a third felony offender, and sentencing him to life imprisonment at hard labor, without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury, and was sentenced, for aggravated battery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34. Following sentencing, plaintiff filed a multiple bill of information charging defendant with being a third felony offender. After a hearing, the trial court adjudicated defendant a third felony offender, and sentenced him to life imprisonment at hard labor, without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed. The appellate court affirmed defendant's aggravated battery conviction, because the victim's testimony alone was sufficient to establish the elements of the offense, and defendant's testimony was rife with internal contradictions and irreconcilable conflicts with the physical evidence. However, defendant's adjudication as a third felony offender and his sentence were vacated, notwithstanding the fact that plaintiff established that defendant had committed the prior offenses. Louisiana expanded the cleansing period in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 from 5 to 10 years, after defendant had committed those prior offenses, so to link those prior offenses with the current offense would constitute an ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: Defendant's aggravated battery conviction was affirmed. However, the trial court's adjudication of defendant as a third felony offender and his life sentence were vacated. Linking defendant's prior offenses with his current offense would constitute an ex post facto law, since the statutory cleansing period was expanded after those prior offenses had been committed. The case was remanded for defendant's resentencing as a second offender.

 

1794 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


McCoy v. Stalder


NUMBER 99 CA 1747


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 1747 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/22/00); 770 So. 2d 447; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2582



September 22, 2000, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 448,054. Honorable J. Michael McDonald, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prison inmate appealed the dismissal of his petition by the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, seeking review of an adverse decision pursuant to his Administrative Remedy Procedure, questioning the use of inmate counsel and the application of the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1171-1190, to his legal claims.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prison inmate sought to have the district court review claims related to appellant's failure to appeal his conviction and for other post-conviction relief. Appellant's proposed amendment and supplemental petitions did not remove the defects in the petition to which the exceptions were addressed, and as such the district court was not bound to allow the requested amendment. Allowing an offender to request review of more than one adverse decision in the same petition would unnecessarily complicate the reviewing court's role by having several records transmitted for review, and would not allow for orderly disposition of the suit. The assessment of a "strike" was in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1187. That statute restricted the right of a prisoner to bring a civil action or an appeal when it was shown that on three or more prior occasions that prisoner's civil action or appeal had been dismissed as being frivolous, malicious, failing to state a cause of action, or failing to state a claim upon which relief may be granted. The district court's dismissal of appellant's petition because it failed to state a cause of action was not in error.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The district court was correct in assessing a "strike" against appellant prison inmate on the basis of the suit for filing more than three frivolous appeals. Bringing the motion seeking declaratory relief of an unrelated matter clearly constituted an abuse of process.

 

1795 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Thigpen v. RPM Pizza Inc.


99 CA 1146


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 1146 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/22/00); 772 So. 2d 704; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2587



September 22, 2000, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied December 12, 2000. Released for Publication December 29, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Suit Number 424,516. Honorable Curtis A. Calloway, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant victim challenged the order of the 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) granting appellee insurer's motion for summary judgment in a personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, victim in a car accident, filed suit for damages against appellee, her employer's insurer, seeking recovery under her employer's uninsured/underinsured motorist (UM) coverage. The trial court found UM coverage did not exist as the employer had rejected UM coverage in its policy. On appeal the court reversed because the employer's rejection of UM coverage was not a valid rejection as the UM rejection form did not conform to the requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1406(D)(1)(a)(ii). The form failed to inform the insured that UM coverage was statutorily required unless specifically rejected by the insured. It also violated statutory requirements as it only provided for the insured to reject coverage completely and not choose lower liability coverage limits. The form did not inform the insured of his options and allow him to make a meaningful selection as provided in the statute.


OUTCOME: The order of summary judgment was reversed and remanded for further proceedings as the rejection form the appellee insurer used did not conform to statutory requirements.

 

1796 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


In re K.L.H.


No. 99-1995


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


99-1995 (La.App. 3 Cir. 09/20/00); 771 So. 2d 706; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2151



September 20, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ACADIA, NO. 1093. HONORABLE DON AARON JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the judgment of the Acadia Parish District Court (Louisiana) granting appellee step-mother's petition for intrafamily adoption of the parties' two daughters under La. Code Juv. Proc. Ann. art. 1245(D)(1).


OVERVIEW: When appellant failed to pay child support for her two daughters, who were living with her ex-husband, for one year, appellee petitioned to adopt them under La. Code Juv. Proc. Ann. art. 1245(D)(1). The trial court granted the petition. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the trial court manifestly erred in failing to consider as mitigating factors for appellant's failure to pay child support the domestic abuse appellant suffered from her subsequent husband and the attendant instability in her life, including unemployment and repeated relocation. The court held that the severance of all of appellant's ties with her daughters was not in the daughters' best interest. A strong bond existed between appellant and her daughters, appellant regularly visited them, and was not indifferent to their well-being. The benefits to the daughters of maintaining an ongoing relationship with appellant were not lessened by their strong relationship with appellee.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed because the trial court erred by failing to consider mitigating factors of domestic abuse when determining whether appellant had just cause for failing to pay child support for one year, and because the adoption of appellant's two daughters by appellee was not in the daughters' best interests.

State v. Dunn


No. 99-KA-1698


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-1698 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/13/00); 769 So. 2d 673; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2492



September 13, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 2, 2000.
Writ denied by State v. Dunn, 799 So. 2d 1149, 2001 La. LEXIS 3907 (La., Oct. 26, 2001)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Dunn v. State, 799 So. 2d 1149, 2001 La. LEXIS 3909 (La., Oct. 26, 2001)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Dunn v. State, 842 So. 2d 392, 2003 La. LEXIS 1267 (La., Apr. 25, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Dunn v. State, 2014 La. LEXIS 2849 (La., Dec. 8, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 391-375, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery, adjudicated as a third felony offender, and sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana). Defendant appealed the trial court's denial of his motion to reconsider.


OVERVIEW: Armed with a knife, defendant approached the victim and wrestled with him; defendant got away with victim's hat and money. Defendant was convicted of armed robbery, adjudicated as a third felony offender, and was sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The trial court denied defendant's motion to reconsider the sentence, and defendant appealed. Defendant contended the State failed to produce sufficient evidence to support his conviction for armed robbery, the trial court erred when it concluded that the defendant was a third felony offender, and the sentence imposed by the trial court was unconstitutionally excessive. The court held the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt defendant was guilty of armed robbery, defendant was a third felony offender because the State proved the validity of the guilty pleas on the prior offenses, and defendant did not present any evidence that the sentence was excessive.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the State produced sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction for armed robbery, the trial court did not err when it concluded that the defendant was a third felony offender since the guilty pleas to the prior offenses were voluntary, and the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive.

 

1798 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Cutter Biological


No. 99-CA-2068


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-2068 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/06/00); 770 So. 2d 392; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2521; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,941



September 6, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Refused October 13, 2000. Released for Publication October 13, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 93-8088, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE MAX N. TOBIAS, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, parents of an AIDS victim, appealed from the order of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), dismissing plaintiffs' tort claims against defendant manufacturers.


OVERVIEW: In 1993, an individual diagnosed with the HIV virus sued defendant, a manufacturer of hemophilia clotting factor. By supplemental petition in 1994, he added three additional defendant-manufacturers. Upon his death, his parents supplemented themselves as plaintiffs. Following a jury verdict in favor of plaintiffs, defendants filed exceptions of prescription. Finding the suit time-barred, the trial court dismissed plaintiffs' claim. The court affirmed. Pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3492, prescription began to run when damage to the plaintiffs manifested itself with sufficient certainty to support accrual of a cause of action. The record clearly established that as of 1987, decedent strongly suspected his condition was caused by a blood transfusion he received in 1984. The court rejected plaintiffs' theory that subsequent exposures to the HIV virus constituted continuing torts. While La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1153 permitted relation back to the date of filing the original pleading, art. 1153 did not apply to a supplemental petition. Plaintiffs' suit was time-barred.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; prescription began to run when injury to decedent manifested itself with sufficient certainty to support accrual of a cause of action. Plaintiffs' claims were time-barred.

 

1799 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Newman


No. 99-KA-1844


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-1844 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/30/00); 769 So. 2d 124; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2510



August 30, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 19, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 389-689, SECTION "A". HONORABLE CHARLES L. ELLOIE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; MULTIPLE BILL ADJUDICATION AND SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) which convicted him of two counts of first degree robbery sentenced to five years on each count and adjudicated him a triple offender sentenced to life imprisonment without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant committed two separate robberies where he induced the store clerks to believe and fear that he was armed. Defendant was convicted him of two counts of first degree robbery and was adjudicated a triple offender. The multiple offender sentence was life imprisonment without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The court affirmed the robbery convictions. The court found there to be sufficient identification and induction of fear that defendant was armed with dangerous weapon and that the victim's belief was objectively reasonable under the circumstances. The photographic lineup was not unduly suggestive. The court vacated the multiple offender adjudication and sentence. It was not clear which count was being enhanced. The State argued that, because the instant convictions arose out of separate and distinct criminal episodes, the defendant could be properly sentenced as a multiple offender on both counts. However the multiple bill of information charged defendant with first degree robbery, not two counts of first degree robbery, as the offense to be enhanced.


OUTCOME: The convictions of first degree robbery were affirmed. The testimony was sufficient to find that that the defendant induced a reasonable fear that he was armed. The triple offender adjudication and sentence were vacated and the case is remanded for further proceedings in accordance with the court's opinion, because it was not clear which count was being enhanced.

 

1800 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lucas


No. 00-KA-258


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


00-258 (La.App. 5 Cir. 08/29/00); 767 So. 2d 921; 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2115



August 29, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 16, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-5483 - DIVISION "S". HONORABLE JOSEPH F. GREFER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 24h Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, denying defendant's motions for mistrial alleging that the prosecutor repeatedly engaged in misconduct, convicting him for distribution of cocaine, and sentencing him to 15 years' hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of distribution of cocaine. Defendant denied a 1996 theft conviction. Prosecutor did not question defendant further. Thus, defendant was not prejudiced by the question and a mistrial was not warranted. Prosecutor's questions regarding the actions of his trial attorney did not breach the attorney-client privilege and did not constitute prosecutorial misconduct warranting a mistrial. Thus, the motion for a mistrial on the basis of the prosecutor's questioning was properly denied. The officer testified that defendant summoned him around the corner and sold him two rocks of crack cocaine. The officer identified defendant in court and in a photographic line-up as the subject who sold him drugs. The jury chose to believe the State's witnesses rather than defendant's account of the events. Thus, the evidence was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of distributing cocaine. Defendant had previous convictions for attempted murder and armed robbery. Thus, defendant was not a first time felony offender and the sentence of 15 years' hard labor was not excessive.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; officer identified defendant as the person who sold him two rocks of crack cocaine. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to convict him of distributing cocaine. Prosecutor's questions were not improper and did not warrant a mistrial. The sentence of 15 years' hard labor was not excessive because of defendant's prior convictions for attempted murder and armed robbery.
